Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
8 min
Bequest (Wasiyyah) is Recommended, Not Obligatory
Opening of Kitab al-Wasaya stating the legal status of bequest with proofs from Quran and hadith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest (wasiyyah), identify its evidence from Quran and hadith, and explain why it is recommended (mustahabb) rather than obligatory (wajib).

Core Idea
Bequest is recommended, not obligatory, limited to one-third for non-heirs.

The Kitab al-Wasaya opens by clarifying the legal status of bequest (wasiyyah). Many assume it is a duty, but the Hanafi school holds it is merely recommended (mustahabb). This lesson traces the evidence from the Quran and the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, and explains the abrogation that shifted the ruling from obligatory to recommended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a bequest (wasiyyah). The author states it is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib (obligatory).
2
Locate the Quranic evidence
Two verses are cited: 1) Surah an-Nisa 4:12, which places bequest before inheritance, and 2) Surah al-Baqarah 2:180, which originally commanded bequest for parents and relatives.
The second verse is key to understanding the abrogation.
3
Understand the abrogation
The command in 2:180 was abrogated by the inheritance verses (an-Nisa) which fixed shares for heirs. Hence bequest for heirs is no longer required, and becomes recommended for non-heirs.
This principle of naskh is crucial in usul al-fiqh.
4
Examine the hadith proof
The hadith of Sa'd establishes the one-third limit and shows the Prophet's permissive attitude, indicating non-obligation.
The hadith is from Bukhari, Muslim, and Abu Dawud.
5
State the Hanafi position
Wasiyyah is mustahabb, valid for non-heirs, up to one-third of the estate.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Book of Bequests. 138 (1) The bequest is not obligatory; it is recommended. (Urdu: Important note: Wasaya is the plural of wasiyyah. At the time of death, one makes a bequest of property for someone; this is called wasiyyah. Its evidence is this verse: 'But if they are more than that, they are partners in the third after a bequest which he makes or a debt, without harming [others]; an ordinance from Allah. And Allah is Knowing and Wise.' (Surah an-Nisa 4:12) In this verse, it is stated that inheritance will be divided after settling debts and bequests. Another verse is: 'Prescribed for you when death approaches one of you, if he leaves wealth, is a bequest for the parents and the near relatives according to what is acceptable – a duty upon the righteous.' (Surah al-Baqarah 2:180) The hadith is: On the authority of 'Amir ibn Sa'd from his father, he said: I fell ill, and the Prophet visited me. I said: O Messenger of Allah, pray to Allah that He not let me return on my heels. He said: Perhaps Allah will raise you up and benefit people through you. I said: I want to make a bequest, and I have only one daughter. Should I bequeath half? He said: Half is too much. I said: One-third? He said: One-third is too much or large. He said: So people bequeath one-third, and that is permitted for them. (Bukhari, chapter on bequest of one-third, p. 383, no. 2744; Muslim, chapter on bequest of one-third, p. 138, no. 628; Abu Dawud, chapter on what is allowed for the testator regarding his wealth, p. 39, no. 2864) From this hadith, the ruling of bequest is derived, and also that one should bequeath one-third of his wealth, not more. [3138] (1) The bequest is not obligatory; it is recommended. Some people say that making a bequest is obligatory. Therefore, the author said that making a bequest is recommended. Until the verse of inheritance was revealed specifying which heir gets how much, bequest for heirs was obligatory. In the above verse (2:180), it is mentioned that at the time of death, making a bequest for parents and relatives is necessary. But when the verse of inheritance was revealed, bequest for non-heirs remained recommended. Footnotes: (a) 'But if they are more than that...' (b) 'Prescribed for you...' (c) 'Sa'd said: I fell ill...'
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage opens Kitab al-Wasaya (Book of Bequests) by stating the basic ruling: bequest is mustahabb (recommended), not wajib (obligatory). It provides evidence from Quran and hadith. The verse from Surah an-Nisa emphasizes that bequests and debts are settled before inheritance distribution. The verse from Surah al-Baqarah initially commanded bequest for parents and relatives, but this was abrogated by the inheritance verses (Surah an-Nisa) which fixed shares for heirs. Therefore, bequest is now limited to one-third of the estate for non-heirs. The hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas establishes the one-third limit. The author clarifies that some earlier scholars considered bequest obligatory before the abrogation, but the relied-upon position is that it is recommended.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): Bequest; a disposition of property to take effect after death
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate
وارث (warith): Heir entitled to a fixed share in inheritance

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the ruling on making a bequest?
A) Wajib
B) Mustahabb
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Bequest is a recommended act (mustahabb), not obligatory, limited to one-third of the estate for non-heirs, based on Quranic abrogation and the hadith of Sa'd.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
The Ruling on Making a Will: Mustahabb and Wajib
Ruling with proof: default mustahabb, wajib with debts/trusts.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the default ruling of wasiyyah (mustahabb) and identify the condition that makes it wajib (unpaid debts or trusts), citing the relevant hadith evidence.

Core Idea
Making a will is recommended unless you have debts or trusts—then it becomes obligatory.

This lesson examines the legal ruling of making a will (wasiyyah) according to the Hanafi school. Contrary to a common assumption, wasiyyah is not always obligatory; its default status is mustahabb (recommended). However, when one has outstanding debts or entrusted properties that must be fulfilled, the ruling shifts to wajib. The passage provides hadith evidence for both rulings, demonstrating the Hanafi methodology of distinguishing between general recommendations and conditional obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its default ruling
The act is making a will (wasiyyah). Determine its hukm level from the text: mustahabb (recommended) as the default, based on the Prophet's practice and analogy to sadaqah.
The text explicitly states the default is mustahabb.
2
Examine the first dalil – the Prophet's own practice
Analyze the hadith where Ibn Abi Awfa reports that the Prophet did not leave a will of property. If it were wajib, he would have done so. This omission indicates recommendation, not obligation.
Hadith reference: Bukhari, Ibn Majah, Abu Dawud.
3
Analyze the second dalil – analogy to sadaqah
The Prophet equated wasiyyah to sadaqah, and sadaqah is mustahabb. Therefore, wasiyyah shares the same hukm.
Hadith: 'Allah has given you sadaqah at your death of one-third of your wealth.'
4
Identify the exception – debts/trusts, and its dalil
The text states that if one has debts or trusts that must be fulfilled, making a will becomes wajib. The third hadith commands a written will in such cases.
Hadith: 'It is the right of a Muslim who has something to bequeath that he should not spend two nights without having a written will.'
5
Note the cross-madhhab ikhtilaf
The Shafi'i school holds wasiyyah as wajib unconditionally for anyone with assets. The Hanafi position distinguishes based on the type of obligation.
This ikhtilaf is rooted in different usul approaches to the hadith evidence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
۱۳۹(۲) ولا تجوز الوصية للوارث الا ان يُجيزها الورثة.
وارثین کو تو حصہ مل ہی جائے گا۔ اب دوسرے ازگوں کو وصیت کر کے مال کا ہدیہ دینا ہے اور ہدیہ دینا مستحب ہے اس لئے وصیت بھی مستحب ہوگی (۲) حدیث میں ہے کہ حضور نے وصیت نہیں کی۔ اگر وصیت کرنا واجب ہوتا تو آپ ضرور کرتے ۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وصیت کرنا مستحب ہے۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ سالت عبد الله بن ابی اوفی اوصى النبي الله الله فقال لا! فقلت كيف كتب على الناس الوصية او امروابها ؟ قال اوصى بكتاب الله (الف) ( بخاری شریف ، باب مرض النبی ما ووفاته ص ۶۳۷ نمبر ۴۴۶۰ رابن ماجه مرض و شریف ، وهل اوصی رسول الله الله ص ، ۱۳۸۸، نمبر ۲۶۹۵ / ابوداؤد شریف، باب ماجاء فیما یومر به من الوصیۃ ، ج ۲،ص ۱۳۹، نمبر ۲۸۶۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ حضور نے کتاب اللہ پر عمل کرنے کی وصیت کی مال کی وصیت نہیں کی۔ اس سے معلوم ہوا کہ وصیت واجب نہیں ہے (۲) ایک حدیث میں وصیت کو صدقہ قرار دیا ہے اور صدقہ کرنا مستحب ہے۔ اس لئے وصیت کرنا بھی مستحب ہوگا۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن ابی هريرة قال قال رسول الله الله الله ان الله تصدق عليكم عند وفاتكم بثلث اموالكم زيادة لكم في اعمالكم (ب) (ابن ماجہ شریف، باب الوصیۃ باسکٹ ، ص ۱۳۹۰، نمبر ۲۷۰۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ اللہ نے تم پر صدقہ کیا تہائی مال وصیت کرنے کا، اور صدقہ کرنا مستحب ہے اس لئے وصیت بھی مستحب ہوگی۔
اگر کسی کا قرض ہو یا کسی کی امانت ہو جن کا ادا کرنا ضروری ہو تو اس کی وصیت کرنا واجب ہے۔
حدیث میں اس کی تاکید ہے۔ عن عبد اللہ یعنی ابن عمر عن رسول الله من الله قال ماحق امرئ مسلم له شيء يوصى فيه يبيست ليلتين الا ووصية مكتوبة عناده (ج) ( ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فيما يومر به من الوصیة ،ص ۳۹ نمبر ۶۲ ۲۸ را بن ماجه شریف، باب الحث على الوصیۃ ص ۱۳۸۹، نمبر ۲۶۹۹) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ کوئی چیز وصیت کرنے کی ہو تو دو راتیں بھی تاخیر نہ کرو کہ وصیت لکھی ہوئی ہو۔ جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ امانت یا قرض دینا ہو تو وصیت لکھ کر رکھے ، ایسی وصیت واجب ہے۔
Book of Wills. (2) A will for an heir is not permissible unless the heirs permit it. Heirs will get their share; now to bequeath to others is to give a gift of wealth, and giving a gift is recommended, so wasiyyah is also recommended. (2) In a hadith, the Prophet did not make a will. If it were obligatory, he would have done so. Thus, making a will is recommended. The hadith: I asked Abdullah ibn Abi Awfa: Did the Prophet make a will? He said no. I said: How then was wasiyyah prescribed or commanded? He said: He made a will regarding the Book of Allah. From this hadith, it is understood that he made a will to act on the Book of Allah, not a will of property. So wasiyyah is not obligatory. (2) Another hadith considers wasiyyah as sadaqah, and sadaqah is recommended. So wasiyyah is also recommended. The hadith: Abu Huraira reported that the Prophet said: Allah has given you sadaqah at your death of one-third of your wealth, as an increase to your deeds. This hadith indicates that Allah gave you sadaqah of one-third of wealth for wasiyyah, and sadaqah is recommended, so wasiyyah is recommended. If someone has a debt or a trust that must be fulfilled, then making a will for that is obligatory. There is emphasis in the hadith: Abdullah ibn Umar reported that the Prophet said: It is the right of a Muslim who has something to bequeath that he should not spend two nights without having a written will. From this, it is understood that if there is a trust or debt, one should have a written will; such a will is obligatory.
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the commentator on the legal status of making a will (wasiyyah). The matn states the ruling about heirs, but the commentary first clarifies the general ruling. The author explains that the default ruling for wasiyyah is mustahabb (recommended), based on two hadith: (1) The Prophet did not leave a will of property, which indicates it is not obligatory; (2) Wasiyyah is likened to sadaqah, which is recommended. However, if one has debts or trusts that need to be discharged, it becomes wajib (obligatory) to make a will to ensure they are fulfilled, based on the hadith commanding a written will for such obligations. The hadith references are from Bukhari, Ibn Majah, and Abu Dawud. The commentary follows the Hanafi position that the basic wasiyyah is mustahabb, not fard or wajib.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A will or bequest made by a person regarding the disposal of his property after death, to non-heirs (unless consented).
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended, an act that is rewarded but not obligatory to perform.
واجب (wajib): Obligatory, an act that must be performed; omission is sinful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in the passage, why is wasiyyah not obligatory in the default case?
A) Because the Prophet explicitly forbade making a will.
B) Because the Prophet did not make a will of property, indicating it is not wajib.
C) Because the verses of the Quran do not mention wasiyyah.
D) Because the hadith about debts makes it optional.

Key Takeaway
Wasiyyah is mustahabb by default but becomes wajib when one has debts or trusts that must be discharged.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
The Prohibition of Bequeathing to an Heir without Consent
Ruling with proof on wills for heirs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequeathing to an heir, identify the evidence for the prohibition, and explain how consent of other heirs can validate such a will.

Core Idea
A will favoring an heir is invalid unless all other heirs consent.

In early Islam, making a will for parents and relatives was obligatory, but the Quran later fixed inheritance shares, abrogating that obligation. This lesson examines the evidence and the exception that with unanimous consent, the will can be enforced.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the core rule: a will for an heir is not permissible (ja'iz) unless the other heirs give permission. Note that this applies to any heir who receives a fixed Quranic share.
The ruling is based on the hadith 'La wasiyya li-warith' (no will for an heir).
2
Understand the Abrogation
The passage explains that originally, making a will for parents and relatives was obligatory (Quran 2:180). This was abrogated when the inheritance verses fixed shares. Recognize that abrogation (naskh) is a key usul concept here.
The hadith of Ibn Abbas mentions abrogation: 'Allah abrogated that and made the male's share twice the female's.'
3
Examine the Evidence
The passage cites multiple hadith: (1) Ibn Abbas on abrogation, (2) Abu Umama: 'Allah has given every rightful owner his right, so no will for an heir,' and (3) the permissibility of consent from Ibn Abbas: 'A will for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs wish it.' Analyze how each supports the ruling.
The first hadith shows abrogation; the second establishes the prohibition; the third provides the exception.
4
Apply the Exception
The exception: if all other heirs consent unanimously after the testator's death, the will becomes valid. This is because they are effectively gifting their shares. Understand that consent cannot be given before death? The text implies after death.
The consent must be from all heirs who would otherwise inherit; partial consent is insufficient.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۱۳۹۱) (۲) وارث کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے مگر یہ کہ ورثہ اس کی اجازت دے۔
شروع اسلام میں وارثین کے لئے وصیت واجب تھا بعد میں قرآن نے سب حصے داروں کا حصہ متعین کر دیا تو اب وہ منسوخ ہو گیا۔ اب وارثین کے لئے وصیت کرنا جائز نہیں۔ کیونکہ اس میں بعض وارث کو زیادہ ملے گا۔ اور بعض حقدار کو کم ، ہاں ! باقی ورثہ اس وصیت کو نافذ ار کو زیادہ کرنے کی اجازت دے تو نافذ کر دی جائے گی۔
پہلے وارثین کے لئے وصیت کرنا واجب تھا اس کی دلیل یہ آیت ہے۔ کتب علیکم اذا حضر احدكم الموت ان ترك خيراً
الوصية للوالدين والاقربين بالمعروف حقا على المتقين (الف) ( آیت ۱۸۰، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اور اب یہ منسوخ ہو گیا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان المال للولد وكانت الوصية للوالدين فنسخ الله من ذلك ما احب فجعل للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب لا وصیتہ لوارث ، ص۳۸۳، نمبر ۲۷۴۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وارثین کے لئے وصیت کرنا اب منسوخ ہو گیا (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت ابا امامة قال سمعت رسول الله الله يقول ان الله قد اعطى كل ذي حق حقه فلا وصية لوارث (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الوصیة اللوارث، ص ۴۰، نمبر ۰ ۲۸۷ / ترمذی شریف
باب ما جاء لا وصیتہ لوارث ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۲۱۲۰) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وارث کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہے۔
البتہ اگر وارث اجازت دے تو اس کی اجازت سے کسی وارث کے لئے وصیت نافذ کر دی جائے گی۔ سب کی اجازت ہوگئی تو گویا کہ سب نے اپنا اپنا حصہ ایک وارث کو اپنی اپنی مرضی سے دے دیا۔ اس لئے اس کی گنجائش ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يجوز لوارث وصية الا ان يشاء الورثة (ر) دارقطني ، کتاب الوصايا، ج رابع ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۲۴۵۳ ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، اما جاء فی الوصیة للوارث، ج سادس ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۳۰۷۱۱) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باقی وارثین اجازت دے تو وارث کے لئے وصیت نافذ کر دی جائے گی۔
(2) A will for an heir is not permissible unless the heirs permit it. In early Islam, a will for heirs was obligatory; later the Quran fixed the shares of all inheritors, so it was abrogated. Now, making a will for an heir is not permissible because it would give more to some and less to others. However, if the remaining heirs give permission, the will can be enforced. The proof that it was previously obligatory is the verse: 'Prescribed for you when death approaches any of you, if he leaves good, is to make a will for parents and relatives with fairness—a duty upon the righteous.' (2:180) And it was abrogated by the hadith: Ibn Abbas said: 'The wealth was for the child, and the will was for the parents; then Allah abrogated that and made the male's share twice the female's.' Another hadith: Abu Umama said he heard the Prophet say: 'Allah has given every rightful owner his right, so no will for an heir.' So a will for an heir is not allowed. But if the other heirs consent, it is permissible, as if they gave their own shares willingly. There is a hadith: Ibn Abbas reported that the Prophet said: 'A will for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs wish it.'
Source pages p. 362

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding bequeathing to an heir. The commentator explains that initially, making a will in favor of parents and relatives was obligatory based on the Quranic verse (2:180). However, when the inheritance shares were later prescribed in the Quran, this ruling was abrogated. The evidence is the hadith of Ibn Abbas stating that the Prophet said: 'Allah has given every rightful owner his right, so no will for an heir.' Thus, a will that gives an heir more than their prescribed share is invalid. However, if all other heirs give their consent, the will becomes valid, as they are effectively gifting their shares. The commentator cites the hadith from Ibn Abbas via Darqutni: 'A will for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs wish it.' The Hanafi position is that the prohibition is based on the hadith and ijma, and consent from all heirs can validate such a will.

Key Terms
وارث (warith): An heir who is entitled to a fixed share in the deceased's estate according to Quranic inheritance law.
اجازة (ijazah): Permission or consent given by the heirs to validate a will that would otherwise be invalid.
منسوخ (mansukh): Abrogated; a ruling that was previously in effect but has been superseded by a later revelation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is required for a will in favor of an heir to be valid according to this passage?
A) The heir must be a parent
B) The testator must be on his deathbed
C) The other heirs must give their consent
D) The will must be written

Key Takeaway
A will for an heir is invalid without unanimous consent of other heirs, based on hadith and abrogation of earlier obligation.

Wasiyyah — Bequest

The Limit of One-Third in Bequests to Non-Heirs
Stating that a will exceeding one-third of the estate is invalid without heirs' consent.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the maximum portion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs and explain when the consent of heirs is required.

Core Idea
A will cannot exceed one-third of the estate without the heirs' consent, as two-thirds is reserved for them.

In this lesson, we examine the well-established Hanafi ruling that a bequest to a non-heir is limited to one-third of the testator's estate. The source text presents the ruling and its principal evidence from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas. Understanding this limit is crucial for drafting valid wills and protecting the rights of legal heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What specific act is being ruled upon? (Bequeathing more than one-third). What is the hukm? (Not permissible without heirs' consent).
The act is 'wasiyyah' (will) for a non-heir exceeding one-third.
2
Locate the dalil
What proof does the author cite? The hadith of Sa'd in Bukhari and Muslim, and a statement from Ibn Abbas.
The hadith is ahad, transmission zanni, but meaning is clear.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
How does the proof establish the ruling? The Prophet allowed one-third and called it 'much', implying it should not be exceeded. The consent of heirs is needed for the excess because two-third belongs to them.
The phrase 'al-thuluth kathir' (one-third is much) indicates the limit.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Is there disagreement among schools? The limit of one-third is mutually agreed (muttafaq alayh). No ikhtilaf.
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the ruling
In a case where the testator bequeaths half to a friend, the first third is valid; the remaining sixth requires heirs' consent. Without consent, it is void.
This protects the heirs' right to two-thirds.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

میت وارث کے علاوہ کے لئے وصیت کرنا چاہے تو اپنے تہائی مال تک وصیت کر سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ کی وصیت کرے تو وہ وارثین کی اجازت کے بغیر نافذ نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ دو تہائی مال وارثین کا حق ہو گیا۔
او پر حدیث میں گزر گیا۔ عن عامر بن سعد عن ابيه قال مرضت فعادني النبي الله ... قلت فالثلث قال الثلث والثلث كثير او كبير قال واوصى الناس بالثلث فجاز ذلك لهم (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب الوصیۃ بالثلث ، ص۳۸۳، نمبر ۲۷۴۴ / مسلم شریف ، باب الوصیۃ بالٹکٹ ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۶۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ثلث سے زیادہ وصیت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ وہ ورثہ کا
صلى الله
حق ہے (۲) اس اثر میں اس کی پوری وضاحت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لو غض الناس الى الربع لان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال الثلث والثلث كثير ( و ) ( بخای شریف، باب الوصیۃ بالنلث ، ص ۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۲۷۴۳ را ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الوصیۃ بالثلث ، ص۳۹۰، نمبر حاشیہ : (الف) تم میں سے کسی کو موت آئے تو اللہ نے تم پر فرض کیا ہے کہ اگر مال چھوڑا ہوتو والدین اور رشتہ داروں کے لئے معروف کے ساتھ وصیت کرے۔ یہ متقین پر حق ہے ( ب ) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا مال اولاد کا تھا اور وصیت والدین کے لئے تو اللہ نے اس کو منسوخ کیا اور کر دیا مرد و عورت کا دو گنا۔ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا اللہ نے ہر ایک حق والے کوحق دیا پس وارث کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہے (د) آپ نے فرمایا وارث کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے مگر دوسرے ورثہ چاہیں تو جائز ہوگی (1) حضرت سعد فرماتے ہیں کہ میں بیمار ہوا تو حضور میری عیادت کے لئے تشریف لائے میں نے کہا تہائی وصیت کروں؟ فرمایا تہائی ٹھیک ہے تاہم یہ بھی زیادہ ۔ پس لوگوں کو تنہائی وصیت کرنے کی اجازت دی۔ پس یہ ان کے لئے جائز ہے (و) حضرت ابن عباس مفرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لوگ چوتھائی تک وصیت کریں تو بھی ٹھیک ہے اس لئے کہ حضور نے تہائی کو زیادہ کہا ہے۔
(3) And a will for more than one-third is not permissible. If the deceased wants to bequeath to a non-heir, he can bequeath up to one-third of his property. If he bequeaths more than that, it will not be enforced without the consent of the heirs, because two-thirds is the right of the heirs. The hadith has already passed: 'Amir ibn Sa'd from his father: I fell ill and the Prophet visited me... I said: (shall I bequeath) one-third? He said: one-third and one-third is much or great. He said: And the people were allowed to bequeath one-third, so that is permissible for them.' From this hadith, it is understood that one should not bequeath more than one-third, because that is the right of the heirs. (2) This effect clarifies it: Ibn Abbas said: 'If people were to reduce to one-fourth, because the Prophet said: one-third, and one-third is much.'
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the limit of one-third in a will. The commentator states that a will can only be made up to one-third of the testator's estate for non-heirs. Any amount beyond one-third requires the consent of the heirs, as the remaining two-thirds belongs to them by right. The evidence is the well-known hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, in which the Prophet allowed one-third but indicated it was already a large amount. The commentator also cites a statement from Ibn Abbas suggesting that even one-fourth would be acceptable, but the established ruling is one-third. The Hanafi position is that the limit is a maximum, not a minimum, based on this hadith from Bukhari and Muslim. The footnotes at the end repeat earlier explanations.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third of the estate; the maximum portion of the estate that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without consent of the heirs.
الثلث كثير (al-thuluth kathir): The phrase from the hadith meaning 'one-third is much', indicating that even one-third is a substantial portion, so one should not exceed it.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the maximum portion of the estate that can be bequeathed to non-heirs without the consent of the heirs?
A) One-fourth
B) One-third
C) One-half
D) Two-thirds

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a non-heir is valid only up to one-third of the estate; any excess requires the explicit consent of the heirs.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
6 min
The One-Third Limit in Wills (Wasiyyah)
Ruling on maximum one-third will with proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wills exceeding one-third and explain the proof from Sunnah.

Core Idea
A will for more than one-third is invalid without heirs' permission; the Prophet called one-third 'a lot.'

In this lesson, we examine the well-known one-third limit on testamentary bequests. The Qur'anic command to will for parents and relatives was abrogated, and the Sunnah fixed the maximum at one-third. We will explore the key proofs and the Hanafi position on excess.

Guided Path
1
State the rule
Read the first sentence: 'ولا تجوز بمازاد على الثلث' (And it is not permissible for more than one-third). Identify the act (wasiyyah) and the limit (one-third).
The rule applies to bequests to non-heirs.
2
Understand abrogation of the verse
The source mentions Quran 2:180 was abrogated by the inheritance verses (4:11-12). Wills for heirs are no longer obligatory; instead, fixed shares apply.
The hadith confirms: 'Allah has given every rightful person his right, so there is no will for an heir.'
3
Identify the proof for one-third
The hadith of Sa'd bin Abi Waqqas: the Prophet visited him in illness and permitted one-third, calling it 'a lot.' This establishes the maximum.
Other narrations show Ibn Abbas preferred even one-quarter.
4
Apply the exception for heirs
If all heirs consent, a will for an heir or for more than one-third can be valid, because they are waiving their own rights.
This is based on hadith: 'No will is valid for an heir unless the heirs wish.'
5
Conclude the Hanafi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) view: a will exceeding one-third is invalid without heirs' permission; the excess is treated as void, and the bequest is reduced to one-third.
This is the position of the Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۳) ولا تجوز بمازاد على الثلث.

الوصية للوالدين والاقربين بالمعروف حقا على المتقين (الف) ( آیت ۱۸۰، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اور اب یہ منسوخ ہو گیا اس کی دلیل یہ حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال كان المال للولد وكانت الوصية للوالدين فنسخ الله من ذلك ما احب فجعل للذكر مثل حظ الانثيين (ب) ( بخاری شریف، باب لا وصیتہ لوارث ، ص۳۸۳، نمبر ۲۷۴۷) اس حدیث میں ہے کہ وارثین کے لئے وصیت کرنا اب منسوخ ہو گیا (۲) دوسری حدیث میں ہے۔ سمعت ابا امامة قال سمعت رسول الله الله يقول ان الله قد اعطى كل ذي حق حقه فلا وصية لوارث (ج) (ابوداؤد شریف ، باب ما جاء فی الوصیة اللوارث، ص ۴۰، نمبر ۰ ۲۸۷ / ترمذی شریف باب ما جاء لا وصیتہ لوارث ص ۱۳۲، نمبر ۲۱۲۰) حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ وارث کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہے۔
البتہ اگر وارث اجازت دے تو اس کی اجازت سے کسی وارث کے لئے وصیت نافذ کر دی جائے گی۔ سب کی اجازت ہوگئی تو گویا کہ سب نے اپنا اپنا حصہ ایک وارث کو اپنی اپنی مرضی سے دے دیا۔ اس لئے اس کی گنجائش ہے (۲) حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الا الله لا يجوز لوارث وصية الا ان يشاء الورثة (ر) دارقطني ، کتاب الوصايا، ج رابع ص ۱۸۷ نمبر ۲۴۵۳ ر مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، اما جاء فی الوصیة للوارث، ج سادس ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۳۰۷۱۱) اس حدیث اور اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ باقی وارثین اجازت دے تو وارث کے لئے وصیت نافذ کر دی جائے گی۔
(۱۳۱۴۰ (۳) تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت جائز نہیں۔
میت وارث کے علاوہ کے لئے وصیت کرنا چاہے تو اپنے تہائی مال تک وصیت کر سکتا ہے۔ اس سے زیادہ کی وصیت کرے تو وہ وارثین کی اجازت کے بغیر نافذ نہیں ہوگی۔ کیونکہ دو تہائی مال وارثین کا حق ہو گیا۔ او پر حدیث میں گزر گیا۔ عن عامر بن سعد عن ابيه قال مرضت فعادني النبي الله ... قلت فالثلث قال الثلث والثلث كثير او كبير قال واوصى الناس بالثلث فجاز ذلك لهم (ه) ( بخاری شریف، باب الوصیۃ بالثلث ، ص۳۸۳، نمبر ۲۷۴۴ / مسلم شریف ، باب الوصیۃ بالٹکٹ ، ص ۱۳۸، نمبر ۱۶۲۸) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ ثلث سے زیادہ وصیت نہ کرے۔ کیونکہ وہ ورثہ کا
صلى الله
حق ہے (۲) اس اثر میں اس کی پوری وضاحت ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال لو غض الناس الى الربع لان رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال الثلث والثلث كثير ( و ) ( بخای شریف، باب الوصیۃ بالنلث ، ص ۱۳۸۳ نمبر ۲۷۴۳ را ابن ماجہ شریف ، باب الوصیۃ بالثلث ، ص۳۹۰، نمبر حاشیہ : (الف) تم میں سے کسی کو موت آئے تو اللہ نے تم پر فرض کیا ہے کہ اگر مال چھوڑا ہوتو والدین اور رشتہ داروں کے لئے معروف کے ساتھ وصیت کرے۔ یہ متقین پر حق ہے ( ب ) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا مال اولاد کا تھا اور وصیت والدین کے لئے تو اللہ نے اس کو منسوخ کیا اور کر دیا مرد و عورت کا دو گنا۔ (ج) آپ نے فرمایا اللہ نے ہر ایک حق والے کوحق دیا پس وارث کے لئے وصیت نہیں ہے (د) آپ نے فرمایا وارث کے لئے وصیت جائز نہیں ہے مگر دوسرے ورثہ چاہیں تو جائز ہوگی (1) حضرت سعد فرماتے ہیں کہ میں بیمار ہوا تو حضور میری عیادت کے لئے تشریف لائے میں نے کہا تہائی وصیت کروں؟ فرمایا تہائی ٹھیک ہے تاہم یہ بھی زیادہ ۔ پس لوگوں کو تنہائی وصیت کرنے کی اجازت دی۔ پس یہ ان کے لئے جائز ہے (و) حضرت ابن عباس مفرماتے ہیں کہ اگر لوگ چوتھائی تک وصیت کریں تو بھی ٹھیک ہے اس لئے کہ حضور نے تہائی کو زیادہ کہا ہے۔
(3) And it is not permissible for more than one-third. The will for parents and relatives is a right upon the righteous (Surah Baqarah 2:180). And now this has been abrogated. Its proof is this hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: The wealth was for the child, and the will was for the parents, then Allah abrogated from that what He willed, and made for the male the share of two females (Bukhari). This hadith states that making a will for heirs is now abrogated. (2) Another hadith: I heard Abu Umamah say: I heard the Messenger of Allah say: Allah has given every rightful person his right, so there is no will for an heir (Abu Dawud, Tirmidhi). From the hadith it is known that there is no will for an heir. However, if the heir gives permission, then with his permission a will for an heir may be executed. If all give permission, it is as if they all gave their share to one heir willingly. So it is permissible. (2) There is proof in hadith: From Ibn Abbas, he said: The Messenger of Allah said: No will is valid for an heir unless the heirs wish (Darqutni, Ibn Abi Shaybah). This hadith and athar show that if the other heirs permit, the will for an heir will be executed. (13140 (3) A will for more than one-third is not permissible. If the deceased wants to make a will for a non-heir, he may make a will up to one-third of his wealth. If he makes a will for more than that, it will not be executed without the permission of the heirs, because two-thirds of the wealth becomes the right of the heirs. The hadith passed above: From Amir bin Sa'd from his father: I fell ill, and the Prophet visited me... I said: One-third? He said: One-third, and one-third is a lot. And the people made wills for one-third, and that was permitted for them (Bukhari, Muslim). This hadith shows that one should not make a will for more than one-third, because it is the right of the heirs. (2) In this athar there is full clarification: From Ibn Abbas: If people reduced to one-quarter, because the Messenger of Allah said: One-third, and one-third is a lot (Bukhari, Ibn Majah). Hasiyah: (a) When death approaches one of you, Allah has prescribed a will for parents and relatives with goodness – a right upon the righteous. (b) Ibn Abbas said: Wealth was for the child, and the will was for the parents, then Allah abrogated that and made for the male two shares of the female. (c) He said: Allah has given every rightful person his right, so there is no will for an heir. (d) He said: A will for an heir is not valid unless the other heirs wish. (e) Sa'd said: I fell ill, and the Prophet visited me... I said: One-third? He said: One-third is okay, but it is also a lot. Then people were allowed to make a will for one-third, so it is permissible for them. (f) Ibn Abbas said: If people made a will for one-quarter, it would be fine, because the Prophet called one-third a lot.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It states that a will (wasiyyah) cannot be made for more than one-third of the estate. The author begins by mentioning the Quranic verse (2:180) that originally commanded wills for parents and relatives, but explains that this has been abrogated. The proof is from several hadith: (1) Ibn Abbas narrates that the rule of wealth going to children and will for parents was abrogated, and inheritance shares were fixed. (2) Abu Umamah reports that the Prophet said there is no will for an heir, meaning an heir cannot receive a will in addition to their fixed share. However, if all other heirs give permission, then a will for an heir may be executed, as stated in another hadith from Ibn Abbas. Then the passage specifically addresses the issue of wills for non-heirs: the testator may make a will up to one-third of his wealth. If he wills more than one-third, it is not valid without the heirs' consent because the remaining two-thirds belongs to them by right. The hadith of Sa'd bin Abi Waqqas confirms the one-third limit, with the Prophet even saying one-third is a lot. Ibn Abbas also indicates that even one-quarter is better. The Hanafi ruling is clear: the maximum for a will is one-third, and any excess requires heirs' approval.

Key Terms
الوصية (al-wasiyyah): A testamentary disposition of property after death.
الثلث (al-thuluth): One-third of the estate; the maximum portion that can be willed without heirs' permission.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens if a person makes a will for half of his wealth to a non-heir, and the heirs do not consent?
A) The will is valid and the non-heir takes half.
B) The will is invalid for the excess; the non-heir takes only one-third.
C) The will is entirely null and void.
D) The heirs must give permission after death.

Key Takeaway
A will for more than one-third is invalid without the consent of all heirs; the excess is void and the bequest is reduced to one-third.

Acceptance of Will is After Death
Ruling on timing of acceptance of a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the timing of acceptance or rejection of a will and identify the roles of the testator (musa), legatee (musa lahu), bequeathed property (musa bihi), and executor (wasi).

Core Idea
A will becomes effective only after death; acceptance before death is void.

This lesson clarifies a fundamental principle in Hanafi will law: the legal effect of a will begins at the testator's death. Any acceptance or rejection by the beneficiary during the testator's lifetime has no standing. We also define the key parties involved in a will.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
Read the passage and note the precise statement: acceptance or rejection of a will is valid only after the testator's death. Before death, it is void.
2
Define the four key terms
Extract the definitions of musa (testator), musa lahu (legatee), musa bihi (bequeathed property), and wasi (executor). Understand each role.
3
Apply to a concrete example
Work through the example given: Zaid tells Khalid to give his garden to Mahmoud after Zaid's death. Identify who is musa, wasi, and musa lahu.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement. It explains that the acceptance or rejection of a will is only valid after the testator's death. Before death, the will is not yet in effect; it is merely a promise. Therefore, if the beneficiary accepts or rejects during the testator's lifetime, it has no legal consequence. The passage also defines key terminology: musa (the testator who makes the will), musa lahu (the beneficiary), musa bihi (the property bequeathed), and wasi (the executor appointed to carry out the will). The example clarifies these roles. The Hanafi ruling is that a will becomes effective upon death, and the beneficiary's decision (acceptance or rejection) must occur after that point.

Key Terms
موصی (musi): The person who makes the will (testator).
موصی لہ (musa lahu): The person in whose favor the will is made (legatee).
موصی بہ (musa bihi): The property or item bequeathed.

D) The beneficiary must also reject before death for the will to be void.

Key Takeaway
A will becomes effective only after the testator's death; any acceptance or rejection before death is legally void.

The Ruling on Bequest to a Killer:  لا تجوز الوصية للقاتل
Ruling with evidence from hadith

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that a bequest to a killer is void (batil) and cite the hadith evidence.

Core Idea
A killer cannot benefit from his victim's estate—neither by inheritance nor by bequest.

This lesson addresses a critical prohibition in Islamic inheritance law: a person who kills the testator cannot receive a bequest from him. Even if the testator had made a bequest before the killing, the bequest becomes invalid upon the act of killing. The ruling is derived from explicit hadith and is firmly upheld in the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a bequest to a person who kills the testator. The ruling: 'لا تجوز' meaning the bequest is not permissible and is void (batil).
The killer is defined as someone who kills the testator, even indirectly, with intent or negligently.
2
Locate the dalil
Two hadith are cited: from Ali ibn Abi Talib (رضي الله عنه) and from Abu Huraira (رضي الله عنه), both recorded by Dar Qutni. The first states 'لا وصية لقاتل' and the second 'ليس لقاتل ميراث'.
Both hadith are ahad (zanni al-thubut) but are sufficient for establishing the ruling.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit negation 'لا وصية لقاتل' indicates that a bequest to a killer is invalid. The negation is general and unconditional, covering all forms of killing.
In Hanafi usul, 'لا' for negation of a genus indicates absolute prohibition and invalidity.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some other schools (e.g., Shafi'i) differentiate between intentional and accidental killing, but the Hanafi position applies to all types.
The Hanafi school relies on the apparent general meaning of the hadith.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
The Hanafi school adopts this position as mufta bihi (operative for fatwa) because of the strength of the general negation and lack of evidence for exception.
This is zahir al-riwayah, the standard ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الوصايا
[۱۳۱۴۱(۴) ولا تجوز الوصية للقاتل

Book of Wills. (4) A bequest for the killer is not permissible. A bequest for the killer is not permissible. If someone is killed for inheritance, it is not permissible to make a bequest for him. And if the deceased had made a bequest and that person killed the deceased, then that bequest becomes void. There is a hadith: From Ali ibn Abi Talib, the Messenger of Allah said: Indeed, no bequest for a killer. (a) Another hadith: From Abu Huraira from the Prophet, peace be upon him, he said: No inheritance for a killer. (b) (Dar Qutni in al-Aqdiya and al-Ahkam etc., vol. 4, p. 152, no. 4526/4525). This hadith indicates that there is no bequest for a killer and no inheritance for a killer. Footnote: (a) He said: no bequest for a killer. (b) He said: no inheritance for a killer.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the hadith. The matn states that a bequest to a killer is not permissible. The sharh explains that if a person kills someone for inheritance, he cannot receive a bequest from that victim. If the victim had already made a bequest to the killer, the bequest is invalidated by the killing. Two hadith are cited: one from Ali (رضي الله عنه) explicitly stating 'no bequest for a killer,' and another from Abu Huraira (رضي الله عنه) stating 'no inheritance for a killer.' These hadith are recorded by Dar Qutni. The footnote provides a brief translation of the hadith. The Hanafi position is that such a bequest is void (batil). The killer is deprived of both bequest and inheritance as a penalty for his crime.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will by which a person allocates property to another after death.
قاتل (qatil): A killer; specifically, someone who kills the testator directly or indirectly with intent to inherit.
موصى له (musa lahu): The beneficiary of a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The bequest is invalid (batil).
C) The bequest is valid only if the killer repents.
D) The bequest is valid but the killer cannot inherit.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to a killer is void (batil) in the Hanafi school, based on the explicit hadith that prohibits both bequest and inheritance for the killer.

Bequest Between Muslim and Non-Muslim: The Hanafi Permission
Ruling with evidence from Quran and practice that bequest is valid across religions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on bequest between Muslim and non-Muslim, cite the Quranic proof, and distinguish it from the prohibition of inheritance.

Core Idea
Bequest to a non-Muslim is kindness (ma'ruf), allowed; inheritance is blocked by difference of religion.

You already know that a Muslim cannot inherit from a disbeliever and vice versa. But does that mean all financial transfers are cut off? The Hanafi school opens a door: a bequest (wasiyyah) is permissible as a voluntary act of kindness. This lesson walks through the ruling, its Quranic basis, and the evidence from the Companions, so you can confidently apply this rule in real-life estate planning across religious lines.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Ruling
Identify the act (bequest) and its permissibility (ja'iz) in both directions: Muslim to disbeliever and disbeliever to Muslim. Note that inheritance is not allowed, but bequest is a separate category.
2
Locate the Quranic Proof
Find the verse from Surah al-Ahzab (33:6) cited in the text. The key exception clause is 'إلا أن تفعلوا إلى أوليائكم معروفا'. Recognize that this clause permits kindness to non-Muslim relatives.
3
Trace the Legal Link (Wajh al-Dalalah)
Explain how the verse proves the bequest ruling: the word 'معروفا' (kindness) is general and includes all forms of goodwill, including financial gifts through bequest. The exception shows that the general rule of inheritance exclusivity among Muslims does not block voluntary kindness.
Hanafi usul: 'amm (general) is qat'i until specified. Here the exception keeps the permission general.
4
Examine the Companion Practice
The athar of Safiyya (radiyallahu anha) making a bequest to her Jewish relative confirms the permissibility. One can apply qiyas: if a bequest to a Jew is allowed, then to any disbeliever it is allowed.
This athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
5
Contrast with Inheritance Rules
Note that inheritance (irth) between Muslim and non-Muslim is invalid because of the hadith 'The Muslim does not inherit from the disbeliever nor the disbeliever from the Muslim' (Bukhari). Bequest is different because it is voluntary and bound by the one-third limit.
The distinction is key: inheritance is a fixed right, while bequest is a gift.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

کافر مسلمان کا اور مسلمان کافر کا وارث نہیں بن سکتا لیکن ایک دوسرے کے لئے وصیت کرے تو جائز ہے۔
آیت میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ واولوا الارحام بعضهم اولى ببعض فى كتاب الله من المومنين والمهاجرين الا ان تفعلوا الى اولياء كم معروفا كان ذلك في الكتاب مسطورا (آیت ۶ ، سورۃ الاحزاب 33) اس آیت میں الا ان تفعلوا الی اولیاء کم معروفا سے اشارہ ہے کہ اولیاء اور خاندان والے کافر بھی ہوں تو ان کے ساتھ احسان کا معاملہ کر سکتا ہے۔ اور وصیت کرنا ایک قسم کا احسان کرنا ہے۔ اس لئے وصیت بھی کر سکتا ہے (و) اثر میں ہے۔ ان صفية اوصت لقرابة لها يهودي (و) (مصنف ابن ابی هیة 12 في الوصية لليهودي والنصراني من رأها جائزة ، ج سادس، ص ۲۱۳، نمبر ۳۰۷۵۴ سنن للبیهقی ، باب الوصیة للكفار ، ج سادس ،ض ۲۵۹، نمبر ۱۲۶۵۰) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ آدمی یہودی یا نصرانی کے لئے وصیت کر سکتا ہے۔ اور جب کفار کے لئے وصیت کر سکتا ہے تو کفار بھی مسلمان کے لئے وصیت کر سکتے ہیں۔
حاشیہ: (ج) رشتہ دار اللہ کی کتاب میں بعض بعض سے بہتر ہے مومنین اور مہاجرین سے مگر یہ کہ تم اپنے اولیاء کے ساتھ معروف کا معاملہ کرو، یہ اللہ کی کتاب میں لکھا ہوا ہے (1) حضرت صفیہ نے اپنے یہودی رشتہ دار کے لئے وصیت کی۔
And it is permissible for a Muslim to make a bequest to a disbeliever and for a disbeliever to a Muslim. And it is permissible for a Muslim to make a bequest to a disbeliever and for a disbeliever to a Muslim. A disbeliever cannot become an heir of a Muslim and a Muslim cannot become an heir of a disbeliever, but one can make a bequest for the other, that is permissible. In the Quran there is an indication: 'But those of kinship are more entitled in the Book of Allah than the believers and the emigrants, unless you do to your close associates a kindness. That is inscribed in the Book.' (Surah al-Ahzab, verse 6). In this verse, 'unless you do to your close associates a kindness' indicates that even if close relatives are disbelievers, one can treat them with kindness. Making a bequest is a kind of kindness, so one can make a bequest. (w) There is an athar: Safiyya made a bequest for her Jewish relative. (w) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 12, in the chapter on bequest to a Jew or Christian, he considered it permissible, vol. 6, p. 213, no. 30754; Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on bequest to disbelievers, vol. 6, p. 259, no. 12650). This athar shows that a person can make a bequest to a Jew or Christian. And if one can make a bequest to disbelievers, then disbelievers can also make a bequest to a Muslim. Footnote: (j) 'Relatives are more entitled in the Book of Allah than the believers and emigrants except that you do to your close associates a kindness; that is written in the Book of Allah.' (1) Lady Safiyya made a bequest for her Jewish relative.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the Quran and the practice of the Sahabah. The matn states that it is permissible for a Muslim to bequeath to a disbeliever and vice versa. The sharh explains that although inheritance between Muslim and disbeliever is not allowed (due to difference of religion), a bequest is a voluntary act of kindness (معروف) and thus permitted. The proof is from Surah al-Ahzab (33:6) where the exception 'إلا أن تفعلوا إلى أوليائكم معروفا' indicates that one may do good to non-Muslim relatives, and bequest is a form of goodwill. Additional evidence is that Safiyya (رضي الله عنها), the wife of the Prophet, made a bequest to her Jewish relative. The Hanafi position is that bequest between Muslim and disbeliever is valid.

Key Terms
مسلم (muslim): A person who submits to Allah and follows Islam.
كافر (kafir): A disbeliever; one who rejects Islam.
وصية (wasiyyah): A bequest or will.
معروف (ma'ruf): Goodness, kindness, or an acknowledged act of virtue.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, is it permissible for a Muslim to make a bequest to a non-Muslim relative?
A) No, because they cannot inherit.
B) Yes, it is permissible as a form of kindness.
C) Yes, but only if the non-Muslim is a spouse.
D) No, bequest is only for Muslims.

Key Takeaway
Bequest between Muslim and non-Muslim is permissible in the Hanafi school based on the Quranic verse permitting kindness to non-Muslim relatives and the practice of the Sahaba.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
6 min
Acceptance of Bequest After Death
Ruling with evidence for post-death acceptance

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the timing of acceptance of a bequest and apply the proofs (hadith and athar) to justify why acceptance after death is a condition.

Core Idea
Acceptance of a bequest after death is a condition for ownership; pre-death acceptance is void.

The Hanafi school holds that a bequest only transfers ownership after the testator's death. Therefore, the beneficiary's acceptance or rejection must occur after that point. Any expression of acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is legally ineffective. This lesson examines the ruling and its proofs from the practice of the Companions and the Prophet (peace be upon him).

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the acceptance (qabul) or rejection (radd) of a bequest by the beneficiary. The Hanafi ruling is that acceptance after death is valid and required; acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is invalid (batil).
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith of Bara' ibn Ma'rur: the Prophet returned the bequest to Bara's children, indicating that acceptance after death is the operative moment. Supporting proofs include the athar from Umar that the latter bequest is binding, and from Shuraih that heirs' permission during life can be revoked after death.
These proofs are from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba and Sunan al-Bayhaqi.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
In the hadith, the Prophet said, 'I return his one-third to his children.' As the beneficiary, he exercised his right to reject after death, showing that the right to accept/reject arises only after death. Similarly, Umar's ruling that the latter bequest takes precedence implies that the testator can change the bequest during life, but final acceptance is after death.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Some scholars (e.g., Shafi'is) consider acceptance during the testator's life valid if the testator confirms it. The Hanafi response is that ownership is not transferred until death, so acceptance before death is meaningless.
This ikhtilaf is recorded in the Hanafi texts.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is relied upon (mufta bihi) because the proofs clearly indicate that the bequest takes effect only after death. The hadith of Bara' is particularly strong in demonstrating the timing of acceptance.
No tarjih authority is explicitly cited, but the position is from Zahir al-Riwayah.

Source Text

وقبول الوصية بعد الموت فان قبلها الموصى له في حال الحياة او ردّها فذلك باطل

ان شاء وا اجازوا وان شاء وا لم يجيزو ا (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة فی الرجل يستأذن ورشته ان یوصی با کثر من النثلث ، ج سادس ص ۲۰۹، نمبر ۳۰۷۱۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ میت کے مرنے کے بعد رد کرنے یا قبول کرنے کا اعتبار ہے (۳) اس حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے۔ عبد الله بن ابي قتادة عن ابيه ان النبى الله حين قدم المدينة سأل عن البراء بن معرور فقالوا توفى و اوصی بشلثه لک قال قد رددت ثلثه على ولده (ج ) ( سنن سمیةقی ، باب الوصیة للرجل وقبوله ورده، ج سادس میں ۴۵۱ نمبر ۱۲۶۱۳) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ موصی لہ کو موصی کے مرنے کے بعد قبول کرنے یار د کر نے کا حق ہوتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) ابن ابی ربیعہ نے حضرت عمر کو لکھا آدمی ایک وصیت کرتا ہے پھر دوسری وصیت کرتا ہے تو کس کا اعتبار ہے۔ حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا اخیر والی زیادہ مضبوط ہے (ب) حضرت شریح نے فرمایا ایک آدمی نے وارث کے بارے میں وصیت کی اجازت مانگی تو مرنے والے نے تہائی سے زیادہ کی وصیت کر دی تو باقی سبھی ور شہ راضی ہو گئے۔ پھر جب انہوں نے قبر کی مٹی سے ہاتھ جھاڑا تو وہ اپنے اصل اختیار پر ہوں گے۔ اگر چاہے تو اجازت دے اور چاہے تو اجازت نہ دے (ج) جب حضور مدینہ تشریف لائے تو براء بن معرور کے بارے میں پوچھا۔ لوگوں نے کہا انتقال کر گئے ہیں اور آپ کے لئے تہائی کی وصیت کی ہے۔ آپ نے فرمایا یہ تہائی ان کے بچوں پر واپس کرتا ہوں۔
And acceptance of the bequest is after death. If the beneficiary accepts it during life or rejects it, that is invalid. The consideration of accepting a bequest is after death. So if the beneficiary accepted or rejected during the testator's lifetime, it is invalid. The one who makes the bequest is called the musee, the one for whom it is made is the musa lahu, the property bequeathed is the musa bihi, and the one entrusted to execute it is the wasee. For example, Zaid said to Khalid: 'After my death, give this garden to Mahmud.' So Zaid is the testator (musee), Khalid is the executor (wasi), Mahmud is the beneficiary (musa lahu), and the garden is the bequeathed property (musa bihi). The basic principle: Consideration is after the death of the testator for rejection or acceptance by the beneficiary. Acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is not considered. The meaning of bequest is to make the beneficiary owner after death. So ownership is created after death, so acceptance or rejection at that time matters. Before death, ownership is not transferred, so acceptance or rejection has no weight. (2) There is an athar: Ibn Abi Rabi'a wrote to Umar ibn al-Khattab about a man who makes a bequest and then another. He said: 'The latter is more binding.' (a) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, chapter on a man making a bequest then another after it, vol. 6, p. 211, no. 30728). This athar shows that the latter bequest is considered, and the first is nullified. (3) There is an athar that if a man seeks permission from his heirs to make a bequest exceeding one-third, and they permit, then after death they revoke, they may do so, and the excess bequest is annulled. The athar is from Shuraih: 'When a man seeks permission from his heirs regarding a bequest and he bequeaths more than one-third, and they agree, then when they dust off their hands from his grave, they are at the head of their affair; if they wish they may permit, and if they wish they may not.' (b) (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, vol. 6, p. 209, no. 30714). This shows that acceptance or rejection after death is what counts. (3) There is a hadith: Abdullah ibn Abi Qatada from his father: When the Prophet came to Medina, he asked about al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur. They said he had died and bequeathed one-third to him. He said: 'I return his one-third to his children.' (c) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on bequest and its acceptance and rejection, vol. 6, p. 451, no. 12613). This hadith shows that the beneficiary has the right to accept or reject after the testator's death. Footnotes: (a) Ibn Abi Rabi'a wrote to Umar: A man makes one bequest then another; which is valid? Umar said: The latter is stronger. (b) Shuraih said: A man sought permission from his heirs to bequeath more than one-third, so he did, and they all agreed. Then when they dusted off their hands from his grave, they are at their original discretion. If they wish, they permit; if they wish, they do not. (c) When the Prophet came to Medina, he asked about al-Bara' ibn Ma'rur. They said he had died and bequeathed one-third to him. He said: I return that one-third to his children.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof from the practice of the Companions. The matn states that acceptance of a bequest is only valid after death; any acceptance or rejection during the testator's lifetime is invalid. The sharh explains the terminology: musee (testator), musa lahu (beneficiary), musa bihi (bequeathed property), wasee (executor). It provides an example: Zaid tells Khalid to give a garden to Mahmud after his death. The basic principle is that ownership is transferred only after death, so acceptance must occur after death. The proof includes an athar from Umar (رضي الله عنه) that the latter of two conflicting bequests is binding, indicating that the testator can change the bequest during life, but final acceptance is after death. Another athar from Shuraih shows that heirs' permission during life can be revoked after death, confirming that acceptance after death is what matters. Finally, the hadith of Bara' ibn Ma'rur shows the Prophet returned a bequest to the children, implying that the beneficiary (the Prophet in this case) could reject after death. The Hanafi position is that acceptance after death is a condition for the validity of the bequest.

Key Terms
موصى له (musa lahu): The beneficiary of a bequest.
قبول (qabul): Acceptance of the bequest by the beneficiary.
رد (radd): Rejection of the bequest by the beneficiary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When must a beneficiary accept a bequest for it to be valid according to Hanafi fiqh?
A) During the testator's lifetime.
B) Immediately after the testator makes the bequest.
C) After the testator's death.
D) At any time, even before death.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance of a bequest must occur after the testator's death; any pre-death acceptance or rejection is legally void.

Recommendation to Bequeath Less than One-Third
Ruling that it is recommended to bequeath less than one-third of the estate

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the recommended bequest amount and explain the proof from the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas.

Core Idea
Bequeathing less than one-third is recommended because one-third is already a large portion of the estate.

This lesson covers the recommended amount for a bequest (wasiyyah) in Hanafi fiqh. The Prophet's guidance to Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas shows that even one-third is a significant portion, so it is better to bequeath less, especially when heirs are in need.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what act is being ruled upon and what category of hukm applies. Here, the act is making a bequest (wasiyyah), and the ruling is mustahabb (recommended) to bequeath less than one-third.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence cited. The author uses the hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas, where the Prophet said, 'One-third is large' (أو كبير الثلث والثلث كثير).
The hadith is transmitted by Bukhari and Muslim.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Understand how the dalil proves the ruling. The Prophet's statement indicates that one-third is a large amount, so bequeathing less is better to avoid burdening heirs.
The implication is not a command but a recommendation.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
Check if there is any disagreement. This ruling is muttafaq alayh (agreed upon) among the schools; all limit bequests to one-third without heirs' consent, and recommend less.
5
Evaluate the tarjih
Since the position is consistent, the mufta bihi (operative ruling) is that bequeathing less than one-third is recommended, and one-third is permissible but not ideal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويُستحب ان يوصى الانسان بدون الثلث
مستحب ہے کہ انسان تہائی سے کم کی وصیت کرے۔ حدیث میں فرمایا کہ تہائی مال تو بہت بڑی چیز ہے اس لئے بہتر ہے کہ تہائی مال سے کم کی وصیت کرے۔ خصوصا غریب ورثہ ہو تو ان کی رعایت پوری کرے (۲) حدیث میں ہے۔ عن عامر بن سعد عن ابيه قال مرضت فعادني النبي الله ... اريد ان اوصى وانما لي ابنة فقلت اوصى بالنصف؟ قال النصف كثير قلت فالثلث؟ قال الثلث والثلث كثير او كبير قال واوصى
And it is recommended for a person to bequeath without (less than) one-third. It is recommended that a person bequeath less than one-third. The hadith states that one-third of wealth is a large thing, so it is better to bequeath less than one-third, especially if the heirs are poor, so take care of them. (2) There is a hadith: 'Amir ibn Sa'd from his father: He said, I fell ill, so the Prophet visited me... I want to make a bequest, and I only have one daughter. I said, should I bequeath half? He said, half is too much. I said, one-third? He said, one-third, and one-third is large or much. He said, and bequeath...'
Source pages p. 365

Commentary
This is a ruling stating that it is recommended (mustahabb) to bequeath less than one-third of one's estate. The sharh explains that the Prophet said one-third is a large amount, so it is better to bequeath less, especially if the heirs are poor and need the wealth. The proof is the famous hadith of Sa'd ibn Abi Waqqas (رضي الله عنه), who wanted to bequeath half, then one-third, and the Prophet said 'one-third is large' (or 'much'), indicating that even one-third is a significant portion. The implication is that bequeathing less than one-third is preferable. The Hanafi position is that bequeathing up to one-third is permissible, but less is better.

Key Terms
ثلث (thulth): One-third of the estate; the maximum limit for bequest without heirs' consent.
مستحب (mustahabb): Recommended; an act that is desirable but not obligatory or necessary.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) One-half of the estate.
B) One-third of the estate.
C) Less than one-third of the estate.
D) The entire estate.

Key Takeaway
It is recommended (mustahabb) to bequeath less than one-third of one's estate, as the Prophet indicated that one-third is a large amount.

Acceptance of Bequest and the Exception When the Legatee Dies Before Acceptance
Ruling with proof on acceptance of bequest and its exception.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule requiring acceptance for a bequest, identify the exceptional case where acceptance is not required, and evaluate the evidence from the athar of Imam Ali.

Core Idea
Acceptance is required for a bequest, except when the legatee dies after the testator but before accepting.

This lesson examines a key principle in Hanafi wasiyyah law: the requirement of the legatee's acceptance. Unlike inheritance, which transfers automatically, a bequest is a voluntary disposition that requires the donee's consent. However, there is a well-known exception: if the legatee dies after the testator but before having the opportunity to accept, the property passes to the legatee's heirs without explicit acceptance. The Hanafi school supports this with a reported ruling of Imam Ali (radiyallahu anhu).

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi rule
Identify the ruling that acceptance is required for a bequest to be valid. Understand that ownership does not transfer until the legatee accepts.
This contrasts with inheritance which is automatic.
2
Identify the exceptional case
Locate the exception: if the testator dies, then the legatee dies before acceptance, the property enters the ownership of the legatee's heirs. This is the only exception where acceptance is excused.
The legatee must have been alive at the time of testator's death; if he dies earlier, no right arises.
3
Examine the evidence (dalil)
Consider the athar from Imam Ali: a man made a bequest to another, who then died before receiving it. Ali ruled that the bequest goes to the legatee's heirs. This shows that the legatee's right vested immediately upon testator's death, and then passed to his heirs.
This evidence is zanni in thubut and dalalah but sufficient for a fiqh ruling.
4
Compare with opposing views
Imam al-Shafi'i and Imam Zafar hold that acceptance is never required; the bequest transfers automatically like inheritance. Understand the basis of their analogy and the Hanafi response distinguishing bequest from inheritance.
The practical difference: if legatee rejects, Hanafi: property stays with testator; Shafi'i: property already transferred and rejection does not revert it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الا في مسئلة واحدة وهى ان يموت الموصى ثم يموت الموصى له قبل القبول فيدخل الموصى به فی ملک ورثته. ... القبول فيدخل الموصى به فی ملک ورثته [ ۱۳۸ (۱۱) و من اوصى الى عبد او كافر او فاسق اخرجهم القاضى من الوصية ونصب غيرهم.
Except in one case: that the testator dies, then the legatee dies before acceptance, so the bequeathed property enters into the ownership of the legatee's heirs.
Source pages p. 367

Commentary
This passage states a ruling on the acceptance of a bequest. The Hanafi position requires the legatee's acceptance for ownership to transfer, unlike inheritance which transfers automatically. However, there is one exception: if the testator dies first, then the legatee dies before having a chance to accept or reject, the bequeathed property becomes the property of the legatee's heirs. This is because the legatee was alive at the time of the testator's death and the property is considered to have entered his ownership pending acceptance. The passage also cites an athar from Imam Ali supporting this ruling. The opposing view of Imam Shafi'i and Imam Zafar is mentioned: they hold that acceptance is not required and ownership transfers automatically upon the testator's death. The Hanafi response relies on the nature of bequest as a gift (hiba) which requires acceptance.

Key Terms
الموصى له (al-muṣā lahu): The person to whom a bequest is made; the legatee.
القبول (al-qabūl): Acceptance by the legatee of the bequest; a necessary condition for ownership in Hanafi fiqh.
الوصية (al-waṣiyyah): A bequest; a disposition of property to take effect after death, up to one-third of the estate.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the testator revokes the bequest.
B) When the legatee rejects the bequest.
C) When the legatee dies before acceptance after the testator's death.
D) When the legatee is a minor.

Key Takeaway
Acceptance is generally required for a bequest, but if the legatee dies after the testator before accepting, the property passes to the legatee's heirs.

Judge's Duty to Remove Unfit Executors
Ruling with proof on executor qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a slave, disbeliever, or fasiq as executor and explain the judge's obligation to remove them.

Core Idea
A judge must remove an executor who is a slave, disbeliever, or fasiq because they lack legal capacity or trustworthiness.

This passage from the Fiqh text establishes a critical limitation on a testator's freedom in choosing an executor. While one may appoint whom they wish, the sharīʿah protects the interests of the estate and heirs by empowering the judge to vet and replace unfit executors. The ruling is grounded in both legal capacity (ahliyyah) and the Quranic prohibition of taking disbelievers as guardians. Understanding this ensures that executors are both legally capable and morally upright.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disqualified persons
Name the three categories: slave, disbeliever (kāfir), and open sinner (fāsiq). Recognize that each lacks a necessary qualification: a slave lacks independent legal capacity; a disbeliever cannot be guardian over a Muslim; a fāsiq is untrustworthy.
These are disqualifications irrespective of the testator's preference.
2
Understand the judge's role
The judge (qāḍī) has the authority and duty to remove such executors from their position and appoint suitable replacements. This is wajib upon the judge.
The judge acts as a protector of the estate and heirs.
3
Connect the Quranic proof
The primary dalil is the verse (4:144) prohibiting taking disbelievers as guardians (awliyā'). This extends to executors because they act as guardians over the will and estate.
The verse is qaṭʿī al-thubūt and qaṭʿī al-dalāla.
4
Note the legal wisdom
The ruling ensures that the executor is fully capable (free, Muslim, upright) to manage the estate in accordance with Islamic law and in the best interest of the heirs.
This protects both the deceased's wishes and the beneficiaries' rights.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من اوصى الى عبد او كافر او فاسق اخرجهم القاضى من الوصية ونصب غيرهم.
And whoever appoints a slave, a disbeliever, or a sinful person as executor, the judge shall remove them from executorship and appoint others.
Source pages p. 368

Commentary
This passage states that if a testator appoints as executor a slave, a disbeliever (kafir), or a person who is openly sinful (fasiq), the judge has the authority to remove such individuals and appoint suitable replacements. The reason: a slave lacks legal capacity to act independently without the master's permission; a disbeliever cannot be a guardian over a Muslim as per the Quranic prohibition (4:144); and a sinful person is untrustworthy. The passage also cites athar from Saeed ibn al-Musayyib and Sufyan al-Thawri supporting this. This ruling ensures that the interests of the heirs and the proper execution of the will are protected.

Key Terms
الوصي (al-waṣī): The executor of a will; a person appointed to administer the testator's estate and execute the will.
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking moral integrity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under Hanafi fiqh, can a judge remove a slave appointed as executor?
A) No, because the testator's choice is final.
B) Yes, because a slave lacks independent legal capacity.
C) Only if the master agrees.
D) No, if the slave is a Muslim.

Key Takeaway
The judge has the authority and duty to remove any executor who lacks legal capacity or trustworthiness, including slaves, disbelievers, and sinners.

Appointing One's Slave as Executor with Adult Heirs
Ruling on validity of appointing own slave as executor when adult heirs exist

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing a slave as executor when adult heirs exist, explain the reasoning based on harm (dirar), and identify the exception for minor heirs.

Core Idea
A slave cannot supervise free adults; appointing him as executor harms adult heirs and invalidates the will.

This lesson examines a specific ruling in wills (wasiyyah): the appointment of one’s own slave as executor while the heirs include free adults. The Hanafi school deems such an appointment invalid (fasid) due to the slave’s lack of capacity and the potential harm to heirs. The passage also provides an exception when all heirs are minors, highlighting a balance between necessity and legal capacity.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling and its condition
Identify that the appointment is not valid (lam tasihh) when there are adult (free) heirs present.
The condition is the presence of adult heirs, not just any heirs.
2
Explain the illah (effective cause)
The slave cannot supervise a free adult; this would be a form of harm (dirar) to the adult heirs, which is prohibited.
Harm (dirar) is the underlying reason for invalidity.
3
Link the illah to the dalil
The author cites the athar of Ibn Abbas, who interpreted Quran 4:12 as prohibiting harm in wills. The phrase 'ghayra mudarrin' (without harming) is the proof.
The proof is a Hadith mursal or athar, considered zanni but binding in this context.
4
Identify the exception
If all heirs are minors, a slave may be appointed as executor out of necessity (darurah) because minors cannot supervise themselves.
The exception shows that the ruling is based on harm, not absolute prohibition.

۱۳۱۴۹ (۱۲) ومن اوصى الى عبد نفسه وفى والورثة كبارٌ لم تصح الوصية。
میت کے ورثہ میں بالغ آدمی موجود ہے پھر بھی اپنے غلام کو وصی بنایا تو یہ اس کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اوپر گزرا کہ غلام وصی نہیں بن سکتا۔ اور یہاں تو غلام کو وصی مان لیں تو بالغ آزاد پر اس کی نگرانی ہو جائے گی اور غلام بالغ آزاد پر نگرانی نہیں کر سکتا اس لئے غلام کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے (۲) اس صورت میں آزاد بالغ کی حق تلفی بھی ہے کہ آزاد اور بالغ ہوتے ہوئے غلام کو وصی اور نگران بنایا۔ اس لئے غلام کو وصی بنانا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ اثر میں ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال الضرار في الوصية من الكبار ثم تلى غير مضار وصيه من الله (الف) ( آیت ۱۲ سورۃ النسا ۴ ، مصنف ابن ابی هیبت ، ۲۷ من کان یوسی و سیستمها ، ج سادس ص ۲۲۹، نمبر ۳۰۹۲۴) اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ اولاد میں سے بھی بڑے کو وصیت کرنی چاہئے چہ جائیکہ غلام کو وصیت کرے۔ و اگر ورثہ میں صرف چھوٹے بچے ہوں تو غلام کونگران اور وصی بنا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ چھوٹا بچہ نگرانی کیسے کرے گا۔ پھر اس کی حفاظت کون کرے گا۔ اس لئے اس مجبوری کے دور ہونے تک غلام وصی رہ سکتا ہے۔
حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت ابن عباس نے فرمایا وصیت کرنے میں نقصان دینا گناہ کبیرہ ہے۔ پھر آیت کا ٹکڑا پڑھا غیر مضار وصیۃ من اللہ
[(12) Whoever appoints his own slave as executor while the heirs are adults, the appointment is not valid.] [The deceased has adult heirs, yet he appointed his slave as executor; this appointment is not valid. It passed earlier that a slave cannot be an executor. And here, if we consider the slave as executor, he would supervise a free adult, and a slave cannot supervise a free adult. Therefore, appointing a slave as executor is not valid. (2) In this case, there is also a violation of the right of the free adult, as a free adult having a slave appointed as executor and supervisor. Therefore, appointing a slave as executor is not valid. There is an athar: from Ibn Abbas, he said: 'Causing harm in a will is among the major sins,' then he recited: 'without harming the heir' from Allah (Surah an-Nisa, verse 12). From this athar, it is understood that one should appoint an adult among the children as executor, let alone a slave. And if the heirs are only minor children, then a slave can be made a guardian and executor, because how can a minor child supervise? Who will protect him? Therefore, the slave can remain executor until this necessity is removed.] [Footnote (a): Ibn Abbas said: 'Causing harm in a will is a major sin,' then he recited the verse portion: 'without harming the heir from Allah.'
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. The ruling states that if a person appoints his own slave as executor (wasi) while the heirs include adult free persons, the appointment is invalid. The author explains the reason: a slave lacks the legal capacity to supervise a free adult, as a slave is himself under the authority of his master. Furthermore, it would be a form of harm (dirar) to the adult heirs, which is prohibited in the Quran as indicated by the athar from Ibn Abbas. The athar cites the verse 'ghayra mudarrin wasiyyatan min Allah' (not harming the heir, an ordinance from Allah). The author also notes an exception: if all heirs are minors, appointing a slave is permissible out of necessity, as a slave can act as guardian until the minors reach maturity. The proof is the athar from Ibn Abbas, which establishes that causing harm in a will is a major sin. The commentary follows the author's order: first the ruling, then the reason, then the exception.

Key Terms
وصی (wasi): The person appointed to execute the will of the deceased.
عبد (abd): A slave, who is owned by another and lacks full legal capacity.
كبار (kibar): Adult heirs who are free and mature.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) When the heirs are all adults
B) When the heirs are all minors
C) When the slave is literate
D) It is never permissible

Key Takeaway
The appointment of a slave as executor when free adult heirs exist is invalid due to the prohibition of harm (dirar) and the slave's lack of capacity; however, necessity permits it when all heirs are minors.
