Appointing an Incapable Executor: The Judge's Duty to Add a Co-Executor
Ruling with proof on incapable executor

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on appointing an incapable executor, explain the dalil from the athar, and apply the rule to determine the judge's intervention.

Core Idea
An incapable executor is not removed; a capable co-executor is added to fulfill the will.

What happens when a testator appoints an executor who cannot carry out the duties? The Hanafi school provides a balanced solution: the judge does not dismiss the testator's choice but adds a capable assistant. This lesson examines the ruling and its proof from the practice of the early Muslims.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State precisely what the judge must do: add another person to the incapable executor, making them co-executors.
The ruling is wajib on the judge to protect the will.
2
Understand the reasoning
Why addition rather than removal? To preserve the testator's appointment and ensure the will is executed.
The testator's choice is respected; the incapable person is not dismissed.
3
Analyze the dalil
The athar from Amir says the executor is like a parent; if accused or deficient, the judge removes or adds another. Here, incapacity is a deficiency warranting addition.
The athar is zanni in thubut and dalala, but relied upon by Hanafi scholars.
4
Apply the rule
Consider a scenario: testator appoints an elderly, bedridden executor. The judge must add a capable co-executor to manage the estate.
The ruling applies to any incapacity: illness, incompetence, lack of resources.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۵۰] (۱۳) ومن اوصى الى من يعجز عن القيام بالوصية ضم اليه القاضي غيره۔
کسی نے ایسے آدمی کو وصیت کی جو اس کو انجام دینے سے عاجز ہے تو قاضی اس کے ساتھ اس کے علاوہ کو شامل کر دے۔ موصی نے ایسے آدمی کو وصی بنایا جو وصیت کو کما حقہ انجام نہیں دے سکتا تو قاضی کسی اچھے آدمی کو اس کے ساتھ شامل کر دے تا کہ دھیت اچھی طرح انجام پاسکے۔ پہلے اثر گزر چکا ہے۔ عن عامر قال الوصى بمنزلة الوالد، واذا اتهم الوصى عزل او جعل معه غيره (ب) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۴۱م من قال وصیتۃ العبد حیث جعلها ، ج سادس، ص ۲۲۴، نمبر ۳۰۸۶۵ / مصنف عبد الرزاق الوصية حيث يضعها صاحبها الخ ، ج تاسع ، ص ۹۵، نمبر ۶ (۱۶۴۸) اس اثر میں ہے کہ وصی متہم ہو یا کوئی خامی ہو تو اس کو معزول کر دے یا اس کے ساتھ کسی دوسرے کو شامل کرے۔اس لئے یہاں وصیت انجام دینے سے عاجز ہے تو دوسرے کو اس کے ساتھ شامل کر دے۔ تا کہ موصی کی بات بھی رہ جائے اور وصیت بھی اچھی طرح انجام پا جائے۔
[(13) Whoever appoints a person who is incapable of carrying out the will, the judge shall add another to him.] [Someone appointed a person who is incapable of executing the will; so the judge adds another with him. The testator appointed a person as executor who cannot execute the will properly; so the judge adds a good person with him so that the trust can be properly fulfilled. A previous athar has passed: from Amir, he said: 'The executor is in the position of a parent; if the executor is accused, he is removed or another is made with him.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah, etc.) This athar indicates that if the executor is accused or has a deficiency, the judge removes him or adds another with him. Therefore, here since he is incapable of executing the will, another is added with him, so that the testator's instruction remains and the will is properly executed.]
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This is a ruling with proof. The rule: if a testator appoints an executor who is incapable of carrying out the will (e.g., due to illness, incompetence, or lack of resources), the judge must appoint another person to assist or act jointly. The reason is to ensure the will is properly executed. The author cites an athar from Amir (a tabi'i) that the executor is like a parent; if he is untrustworthy or deficient, the judge removes him or adds a co-executor. This principle applies here: since the executor is incapable, the judge adds a capable person to prevent the will from being neglected. The author emphasizes that the testator's choice is respected (his appointment remains), but a capable person is added to fulfill the duty.

Key Terms
عاجز (ajiz): Incapable of fulfilling the duties of executor due to physical, mental, or practical limitations.
ضم (damm): The judge adds another person to the executor, making them co-executors.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The judge must add a capable co-executor to an incapable executor, preserving the testator's choice while ensuring the will is fulfilled.

Appointing Two Executors: Joint Action, Dispute, and Exceptions
Ruling on multiple executors with intra-Hanafi dispute and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule on joint executors, identify the intra-Hanafi dispute, and apply the exceptions for urgent and specific tasks.

Core Idea
Two executors must act jointly; one cannot act alone unless for urgent needs or specific tasks.

When a testator appoints two executors, the Hanafi school generally requires them to act together, reflecting the testator's trust in their collective judgment. However, Imam Abu Yusuf held that each has independent authority. This lesson examines the majority position, the evidence from an athar of Umar, and the exceptions where one executor may act alone to prevent harm or because the task is predefined.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule
Identify the default ruling from Abu Hanifa and Muhammad: two executors must act jointly; one cannot act without the other.
This is the mufta bihi position.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Recognize that Abu Yusuf differs, allowing each executor full authority to act alone. Understand the reasoning: the testator's delegation grants independence.
Abu Yusuf's view is a minority within the school.
3
Analyze the evidence
Examine the athar from Umar on proportional sharing in wills and manumissions. This supports the principle of joint responsibility by analogy.
The evidence is a qawl Sahabi, used as a dalil naqli.
4
List the exceptions
Identify two categories: (a) urgent matters like shroud, burial, food and clothing for minor children; (b) specific tasks like returning a deposit, executing a specific will, freeing a specific slave, paying a debt, or litigation.
These exceptions allow one executor to act alone due to necessity or lack of need for deliberation.
5
Apply the rule to scenarios
Given a practical case, determine whether an executor's lone action is valid by checking if it falls under the exceptions or requires joint action.
Management decisions (e.g., selling property) generally require both executors.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۵۱] (۱۴) ومن اوصى الى اثنين لم يجز لاحدهما ان يتصرف عند ابي حنيفة ومحمد رحمهما الله دون صاحبه [۳۱۵۲] (۱۵) الا فى شراء كفن الميت وتجهيزه و طعام اولاده الصغار و كسوتهم [۳۱۵۳] (۱۶) وردّ وديعة بعينها وتنفيذ وصية بعينها وعتق عبد بعينه وقضاء دين وخصومة في حقوق الميت。
موسی نے دو آدمیوں کو وصیت نافذ کرنے کا وصی بنایا۔ تو ایک آدمی وصیت نافذ کرنا چاہے تو طرفین کے نزدیک نہیں کر سکتا۔ بلکہ دونوں ملکر کام انجام دیں گے۔ دونوں کو وصی بنایا تو گویا کہ موسی نے دونوں کی رائے پر اعتماد کیا۔ ایک کی رائے پر اعتماد نہیں کیا۔ اس لئے دونوں ملکر انجام دیں گے (۲) ایک اثر سے استدلال کیا جا سکتا ہے۔ عن عمر قال اذا كانت وصية وعتاقة تحاصوا (الف) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبۃ ۴۲ فی الرجل یوصی بوصیة فیها عتابہ ، ج سادس، ص ۲۲۴، نمبر ۳۰۸۶۶) اس اثر میں ہے کہ میت نے ایک تہائی مال کی وصیت کی اور ایک غلام کو بھی آزاد کیا اور دونوں ملا کر ایک تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت ہو جاتی ہے تو دونوں کو حصے کر کے ایک تہائی کے اندر تقسیم کی جائے گی۔ پس جس طرح یہاں حصے کئے جائیں گے اسی طرح دو آدمیوں کو وصیت کی تو دونوں کو حصے کریں گے۔ لیکن انتظام کا حصہ کر نہیں سکتے تو دونوں مل کر انجام دیں گے۔
قائد امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ دونوں کو پورا پورا اختیار ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی ایک بھی انجام دے دے تو جائز ہو جائے گا۔ [۳۱۵۲] (۱۵) مگرمیت کے کفن خریدنے میں اس کی تجہیز و تشفین میں اور چھوٹے بچوں کے کھانے اور اس کے کپڑے میں۔ تری میت کے کفن لانے اور اس کی تجہیز و تکفین کرنے کے لئے دو آدمیوں کو وصی بنایا تو ایک آدمی بھی کفن خرید کر لا سکتا ہے اور تجہیز و تکفین کر سکتا ہے۔
یہ کام جلدی کرنے کا ہے۔ اور دیر کرنے سے میت پھول پھٹ سکتی ہے۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ پڑوس کے لوگ بھی جلدی سے اس کا انتظام کر سکتے ہیں۔ اس لئے اس مسئلے میں دونوں وصیوں کا جمع ہونا ضروری نہیں ہے۔ ایک آدمی بھی کام انجام دے سکتا ہے۔ یہی حال چھوٹے بچوں کے کھانے اور ان کے کپڑوں کا ہے کہ دو آدمیوں کو وصی بنایا تو ایک آدمی بھی کھانا اور کپڑا لا سکتا ہے۔ کیونکہ دونوں کے جمع ہونے کا انتظار کریں گے تو بچہ بھوک سے مر جائے گا یا سردی سے ٹھٹھر جائے گا۔
اصول دو آدمیوں کو وصی بنایا تو دونوں کو جمع ہونا چاہیئے لیکن جہاں جلدی ہو یا مجبوری ہوتو ایک وصی بھی کام انجام دے سکتا ہے۔ [۳۱۵۳] (۱۶) خاص امانت کو واپس کرنے کی وصیت اور خاص وصیت کو نافذ کرنے اور متعین غلام کو آزاد کرنے اور قرض ادا کرنے اور میت کے حقوق میں نالش کرنے کی وصیت میں۔
یہ پانچ چیزوں کی وصیت ایسی ہے کہ دو آدمیوں کو وصی بنایا تو ایک آدمی بھی انجام دے سکتا ہے۔ دوسرے کو مشورے اور کام میں شریک نہ بھی کرے تب بھی جائز ہو جائے گا۔ اس لئے کہ ان میں سے بعض کام تو وہ ہے کہ اس میں رائے مشورے کی ضرورت ہی نہیں ہے۔ کام متعین ہے صرف اس کو کر دینا ہے۔ اس لئے کوئی ایک بھی کر دے گا تو کافی ہے۔ مثلا متعین امانت کو واپس کرنے کی وصیت دو آدمیوں کو کی ۔ اب اس
حاشیہ : (ب) حضرت عمرؓ نے فرمایا اگر وصیت بھی ہو اور آزاد کرنا بھی ہو تو حصہ حصہ کر کے حساب کرو۔
[(14) Whoever appoints two executors, it is not permissible for one of them to act without his partner according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (may Allah have mercy on them). [3152] (15) Except in purchasing the shroud of the deceased, preparing him for burial, and the food and clothing of his minor children. [3153] (16) And returning a specific deposit, executing a specific will, freeing a specific slave, paying a debt, and litigation in the rights of the deceased.] [Musa appointed two men as executors to execute the will. So if one man wants to execute the will, according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) he cannot; rather both will do the work together. When he appointed both as executors, it is as if the testator trusted the opinion of both, not the opinion of one. Therefore, both will do it together. (2) An athar can be used as evidence: from Umar, he said: 'If there is a will and a manumission, they (the beneficiaries) will share proportionally.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shaybah...) This athar indicates that if the deceased makes a will of one-third and also frees a slave, and together they exceed one-third, then they will be proportionally reduced to one-third. So just as they share here, similarly for two executors, they will share the responsibility. But management cannot be divided; so both will act together. Abu Yusuf said: Both have full authority; so if one acts alone, it is valid. (15) Except in buying the shroud of the deceased, preparing his burial, and the food and clothing of his minor children. If two executors are appointed, one may buy the shroud and perform the burial. This is urgent; delay may cause the body to bloat. Therefore, neighbors can also do it quickly. So in this matter, both executors need not gather; one can do it. Similarly for the food and clothing of minor children: if two executors are appointed, one may bring food and clothes, because waiting for both would cause the child to starve or freeze. The principle: when two executors are appointed, they should gather; but where there is urgency or necessity, one executor may act. (16) In the will to return a specific deposit, execute a specific will, free a specific slave, pay a debt, and litigation in the rights of the deceased. These five matters are such that if two executors are appointed, one may execute them even without consulting the other. Because some of these matters do not require opinion or consultation; the task is specific, just to be done. So if one does it, it is sufficient. For example, a will to return a specific deposit made to two executors...] [Footnote (b): Umar said: 'If there is a will and a manumission, then calculate proportionally.'
Source pages p. 369

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling on appointing two executors, an intra-Hanafi dispute, and two categories of exceptions. The general rule: when two executors are appointed, they must act jointly; one cannot act alone according to Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Muhammad. Their reasoning is that the testator relied on the combined judgment of both, not one individually. An athar from Umar is cited to support proportional sharing in similar contexts. Imam Abu Yusuf differs, holding that each executor has full authority to act independently. The text then provides two exceptions: (15) urgent matters like purchasing the shroud, preparing the body for burial, and providing food and clothing for minor children—where delay could cause harm (body decay, child starvation). (16) specific, defined tasks such as returning a specific deposit, executing a specific will, freeing a specific slave, paying a debt, and litigation—these require no deliberation, so one executor can perform them. The author emphasizes the principle: joint action is the default, but necessity or specificity allows individual action. The footnote from Umar reinforces the idea of proportional allocation in overlapping claims.

Key Terms
وصیان (wasiyyan): Two executors appointed jointly to carry out a will.
تحاصوا (tahasu): They proportionally share in the limited fund (one-third of the estate) when multiple claims exceed it.
کفن (kafan): Shroud for the deceased.
وديعة (wadi'ah): A deposit entrusted to the deceased that must be returned to its owner.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, when may one of two executors act alone?
A) Never
B) Only in urgent matters like burial and food for children
C) Only in urgent matters and specific tasks like paying a debt returning a deposit
D) Only if the other executor gives written permission

Key Takeaway
Two executors must act together unless the task is urgent (e.g., burial, feeding children) or a specific defined action (e.g., paying a debt, returning a deposit).

When One Executor May Act Alone
Rulings on when a single executor may execute a will without the other

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the situations in which a single executor may act alone under Hanafi law and apply the underlying principle of necessity to new scenarios.

Core Idea
An executor may act alone when consultation is unnecessary or when delay risks loss of the deceased's right.

The appointment of two executors does not always require their joint action. This lesson examines specific cases where a single executor can execute the will independently, based on the nature of the task and the principle of necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general principle
The commentator states that where consultation is not needed, one executor can act. Recognize this as the overarching rule.
Consultation (mashwarah) is a key concept differentiating tasks.
2
Analyze the examples
Examine each example given: returning a deposit, delivering a specific sum, freeing a specific slave, collecting a specific debt. Notice that all are specific, mechanical tasks.
These tasks do not require discretion.
3
Apply to litigation
The final example involves filing a lawsuit. The text gives two reasons: the task must be done, and delay risks loss. Understand that necessity permits one executor to act.
This is an exception based on urgency.
4
Extract the commentator's summary
The commentator distills two rules: (1) where consultation is not needed, one executor can act; (2) where gathering both is difficult and urgent, one can act. Memorize these principles.
These summarize the entire passage.

Debt and litigation regarding the rights of the deceased. Whoever bequeaths one-third of his wealth to a man and to another, consultation is not needed. Simply returning the deposit is enough, so any one executor can do it, it will be valid. Partnership of the other is not required. Or if he appoints two men as executors to execute a specific will, e.g. he said: 'Give five dirhams to Zaid, both of you,' then consultation between them is not needed. So if one executor gives it, it will be permissible. Or if he appoints two men to free a specific slave, e.g. 'Free my slave Khalid, both of you,' then also consultation is not needed. So if one executor frees him, it will be permissible. Or if Zaid owes me five dirhams, I appoint you both to collect this debt, then one executor can also collect it, it is permissible. Because consultation between the two executors is not needed. Or if there is a lawsuit regarding the rights of the deceased, for which he appointed two men as executors, e.g. Zaid before dying appointed two executors: 'My gifted property is with so-and-so, take it,' but he is not giving. Now to file a lawsuit in this matter, one executor can also file a lawsuit with the judge and obtain a decision for the deceased's right to the gift. The reason is that this task must be done. Another reason is that sometimes it is impossible for both executors to gather, and delaying risks loss of the deceased's right. So if one executor files a lawsuit and obtains a decision for the deceased's right, it will be permissible. Principle: Where consultation is not needed, any one of the two executors can execute the will. (2) Where it is difficult for both executors to gather and the task is urgent, then also one executor may do it, it will be permissible.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage is a series of rulings regarding when a single executor may act without the other. The text begins by stating the general principle: when consultation is not required, one executor suffices. It then gives several examples: returning a deposit (amanah) does not require consultation because it is a simple act; executing a specific bequest of cash, freeing a specific slave, or collecting a specific debt—all these are determined actions where the joint decision is not needed. Finally, it addresses litigation (khusumah) regarding the deceased's rights. Even if both were appointed, one can go to court alone because the task is obligatory and delay might harm the deceased’s rights. The commentator summarizes two principles: (1) where consultation is not required, one executor can act; (2) where gathering both is impossible or urgent, one may also act. This is a ruling statement without explicit textual proof; the reasoning is based on necessity and the nature of the tasks.

Key Terms
وصی (waṣī): An executor appointed by the testator to carry out the will after death.
مشورہ (mashwarah): Consultation or joint decision between two executors.
وصیت (waṣiyyah): A will or bequest made by a person regarding his property after death.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
A single executor may act alone when the task does not require consultation or when necessity demands immediate action to prevent loss.

Two One-Third Bequests: Equal Division When Heirs Disapprove
Ruling when two one-third bequests exceed one-third and heirs do not approve

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling that when two equal bequests exceed the one-third limit and heirs do not consent, the available one-third is divided equally between the beneficiaries, and explain the evidence from al-Zuhri's athar.

Core Idea
When two one-third bequests exceed the limit, the available third is shared equally — proportional to intended shares.

Imagine a testator leaves two bequests, each of one-third of his estate. The total exceeds the permissible one-third, and the heirs do not consent to the excess. The Hanafi school provides a clear rule: the available one-third is divided equally between the two beneficiaries. This lesson unpacks the reasoning, the application, and the prophetic tradition that supports this ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and legal question
Recognize that the testator made two separate one-third bequests, totalling two-thirds, and that the heirs refused the excess. The legal question is how to fulfill the bequests within the permissible one-third.
2
Recall the one-third rule
Remember that without heirs' permission, a testator cannot bequeath more than one-third of the estate. This limit is a right of the heirs.
3
Determine the effect of heirs' disapproval
Because the heirs do not approve the excess, only one-third of the estate is available for bequests. The excess bequest (the second third) is effectively void or requires abatement.
4
Apply proportional division
Since both bequests were intended to be equal (one-third each), the available one-third is divided equally between the two beneficiaries. Each receives half of the one-third, i.e., one-sixth of the estate.
If the intended shares were unequal, division would be proportional to the amounts specified, not necessarily equal.
5
Examine the dalil from al-Zuhri
The passage cites an athar (report) from al-Zuhri where a man bequeathed a horse (equal to one-third) and also named two beneficiaries for one-third. Al-Zuhri ruled that the one-third should be divided according to their shares. This supports proportional distribution.
The athar is from Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, considered a reliable source. Its chain is mursal but accepted in Hanafi usul.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(17) Someone bequeathed one-third of his wealth to one man and one-third to another, and the heirs did not permit. Then the one-third will be divided equally between them. The rule has passed that without the heirs' permission, one cannot bequeath more than one-third. Here, there are two bequests of one-third each, so two-thirds was bequeathed. The heirs only allow one-third. So the one-third of the wealth will be divided between the two beneficiaries. For example, if it is 100 dirhams, one-third is 33.33 dirhams, i.e., thirty-three dirhams and thirty paise. Dividing it equally between two gives 16.66, sixteen dirhams and sixty-six paise. The Arabic text: 'By one-third of his wealth, and if the heirs do not permit, then the third is half-half between them.' There is an athar: From al-Zuhri concerning a man who bequeathed a horse to a man and specified it and said: 'One-third of my wealth is for so-and-so and so-and-so,' and the horse was one-third of his wealth. Al-Zuhri said: 'I think that his one-third be divided according to their shares.' (Mushannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 38, a man bequeathed a horse to a man and bequeathed to another one-third of his wealth, and the horse was one-third of his wealth, vol. 6, p. 224, no. 30858). In this athar, the horse was one-third of the testator's wealth, and besides that there was also one-third of the wealth. Footnote: (a) Hadrat Zuhri said: A man bequeathed a horse to a man and specified the horse and said: 'My wealth is for so-and-so and so-and-so,' and the horse was exactly one-third of his wealth. So Hadrat Zuhri said: I think that the one-third be divided into portions.
Source pages p. 371

Commentary
This passage presents the ruling for a specific scenario: a testator makes two bequests, each for one-third of his wealth. Since the total bequest would be two-thirds, and the heirs do not consent to more than one-third, the available one-third is divided equally between the two beneficiaries. The reasoning is that the one-third limit is a right of the heirs, and when exceeded, the excess is invalid, but the available third is shared proportionally based on the intended shares. Here, since both intended shares are equal, the division is equal. The passage then provides a proof in the form of an athar (report) from Imam al-Zuhri (a Tabi'i), who was asked about a similar case where a man bequeathed a horse (which was one-third of his wealth) and also said 'one-third of my wealth to so-and-so and so-and-so.' Al-Zuhri ruled that the one-third should be divided according to their shares. This supports the Hanafi position that when multiple bequests compete and exceed the one-third limit, the available third is distributed proportionally among the beneficiaries according to the amounts intended, provided the heirs do not approve the excess. The commentary provides a numerical example for clarity.

Key Terms
تہائی (thuluth): One-third of the estate, which is the maximum a testator can bequeath without heirs' permission.
موصی لہ (mūṣā lahu): The beneficiary of a bequest (wasiyyah).
ورثہ (warathah): The legal heirs of the deceased.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to X and one-third to Y, and the heirs do not approve, how is the bequest fulfilled?
A) Only one of them gets the one-third by lottery.
B) They each get one-sixth (half of the one-third).
C) They each get one-third of the one-third (one-ninth of the estate).
D) The bequest is invalid entirely.

Key Takeaway
When multiple bequests exceed the one-third limit and heirs do not consent, the available one-third is divided proportionally according to the intended shares; if equal, equally.

Bequest of One-Third and One-Sixth: Proportional Reduction
Ruling when one is bequeathed one-third and another one-sixth, heirs disapprove

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional division of the bequest when bequests exceed one-third and heirs disapprove, and state the evidence from the athar.

Core Idea
When bequests exceed one-third, they are reduced proportionally—not equally.

In this lesson, we examine the Hanafi ruling when a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to one person and one-sixth to another, and the heirs do not grant permission. Since the total exceeds the permissible one-third, the available third must be divided proportionally. The passage provides the calculation method and cites an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri as evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two bequests
Recognize that the testator bequeathed one-third (1/3) to one person and one-sixth (1/6) to another.
Total bequest = 1/3 + 1/6 = 1/2 of the estate.
2
Apply the one-third limit
Without heir consent, only one-third of the estate can be given as bequests. Since 1/2 > 1/3, the bequests must be reduced.
The available one-third is what can be distributed.
3
Determine the ratio
The original bequests are in a 2:1 ratio (1/3 : 1/6 = 2:1). The reduction preserves this ratio within the available one-third.
Thus the available third is divided into 3 parts: 2 parts to the 1/3 beneficiary, 1 part to the 1/6 beneficiary.
4
Confirm with the athar
The athar from al-Hasan states: 'They all reduce proportionally' (yatahasun). This supports proportional reduction over equal reduction or prioritization.
The word يتحاصون is key to the Hanafi method.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان اوطى لاحدهما بالثلث والأخر بالسدس فالثلث بينهما اثلاثا - ۳۱۵۶ (۱۹) وان اوطى لاحدهما بجميع تشریح ایک آدمی کے لئے پورے مال کی تہائی کی وصیت کی جو سو درہم میں سے 33.33 تیمیس درہم تیس پیسے ہوں گے۔ اور دوسرے کے لئے پورے مال کے چھٹے حصے کی وصیت کی جو سو درہم میں سے 16.666 یعنی سولہ درہم اور چھیاسٹھ پیسے ہوں گے۔ اب دونوں وصیتوں کو ملائیں تو آدھے مال کی وصیت ہوگی۔ اور قاعدہ یہ ہے کہ صرف تہائی مال کی وصیت جائز ہے۔ اس لئے دونوں موصی لہ کو اپنے اپنے حصہ سے ایک ایک تہائی کم ملے گی۔ جس کے لئے پوری ایک تہائی مال کی وصیت کی تھی یعنی سو درہم میں سے 33.33 درہم ملنے والے تھے ان کو اس میں سے ایک تہائی کم کر کے 22.22 بائیس درہم اور بائیس پیسے ملیں گے۔ اور جن کو پورے مال کے چھٹے حصے کی وصیت کی تھی اس کو ایک تہائی کم کر کے 11.11 گیارہ درہم گیارہ پیسے ملیں گے۔ او پر اثر گزر چکا ہے کہ وصیت زیادہ کر دی تو حصے پر تقسیم ہوگی (۲) عن الحسن انه قال فـي رجل اوصى بدرهم وبالسدس ونحوه قال يتحاصون جميعا (الف) (مصنف ابن ابي شيبة ، ۳۸ رجل او می لرجل بفرس و اوصی ا لآخر بثلث مالہ وکان الفرس ثلث ماله ج سادس ، ص ۲۴ نمبر ۳۰۸۶۰) اس اثر میں ہے کہ زیادہ وصیت کر دی ہو تو سب کو حصے پر تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ اوپر کا حساب کلکیولیٹر پر سیٹ کرلیں۔ حساب کی دوسری شکل : جس کے لئے تہائی مال کی وصیت کی اس کے لئے چھٹے حصے سے دوگنی وصیت کی۔ اس لئے 33.33 یعنی تنیس درہم تیس پیسے کو تین حصوں میں تقسیم کریں تو 11.11 گیارہ درہم گیارہ پیسے ہوں گے۔ اور اس کا دو گنا 22.22 یعنی بائیس درہم بائیس پیسے تہائی وصیت والے کو ملے گا۔ اور ایک گنا یعنی تیس میں سے ایک تہائی 11.11 گیارہ درہم گیارہ پیسے چھٹے حصے والے کو ملے گا ۔ کیونکہ چھٹا حصہ تہائی کا آدھا ہے۔ اخت اثلاثا : تین تہائی کریں ان میں سے دو تہائی ایک کو دیں اور ایک تہائی دوسرے کو دیں اس کو ا ثلاث کہتے ہیں۔
And if he bequeaths to one of them one-third and to the other one-sixth, then the one-third is divided between them in thirds. (Rule 19) And if he bequeaths to one of them the whole... Explanation: A man bequeaths one-third of the entire estate to one person, which from 100 dirhams is 33.33 dirhams (thirty-three dirhams and thirty paise). And to the other he bequeaths one-sixth of the entire estate, which from 100 dirhams is 16.666 (sixteen dirhams and sixty-six paise). Now adding the two bequests gives half of the estate. The rule is that only one-third of the estate can be bequeathed without permission. So both beneficiaries will get one-third less from their respective shares. He who was bequeathed a full one-third of the estate (33.33 dirhams) will get one-third less, i.e., 22.22 dirhams (twenty-two dirhams and twenty-two paise). And he who was bequeathed one-sixth of the estate will get one-third less, i.e., 11.11 dirhams (eleven dirhams and eleven paise). The athar has already passed that when bequest is excessive, it is divided proportionally. (2) From al-Hasan, he said concerning a man who bequeathed a dirham and one-sixth and the like: 'They all reduce proportionally.' (Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 38, a man...). In this athar, when the bequest is excessive, all are divided proportionally. Set the calculation on a calculator. Another form of calculation: He who was bequeathed one-third was given double the one-sixth. So divide 33.33 (thirty-three dirhams thirty paise) into three parts: 11.11 (eleven dirhams eleven paise). Two times that (22.22) goes to the one who was bequeathed one-third, and one times that (11.11) goes to the one who was bequeathed one-sixth, because one-sixth is half of one-third. The term 'athlasa' means to divide into three parts, giving two-thirds to one and one-third to the other.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling when a testator bequeaths one-third of his estate to one person and one-sixth to another, and the heirs do not approve. The total bequest would be one-half (1/3 + 1/6 = 1/2), which exceeds the permissible one-third. Therefore, the available one-third is divided proportionally according to the intended shares. Since the one-third is double the one-sixth, the division is in the ratio 2:1. Thus, the beneficiary of the one-third gets two-thirds of the available one-third, and the beneficiary of the one-sixth gets one-third of the available one-third. The passage provides a numerical example and cites an athar from al-Hasan al-Basri to support the principle of proportional reduction (yatahasun). This is consistent with the Hanafi method of reducing multiple legacies when the one-third limit is exceeded.

Key Terms
ثلاثا (athlasā): Dividing into three parts; here it means the available third is divided into three shares, two for the one-third beneficiary and one for the one-sixth beneficiary.
يتحاصون (yatahasūn): They reduce proportionally; all legatees share the available third in proportion to their intended bequests.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Half of the one-third
B) Two-thirds of the one-third

When bequests exceed one-third and heirs disapprove, the available third is divided proportionally among the beneficiaries according to the ratio of their original bequests.

Whole Estate and One-Third Bequest: Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on distribution when one is bequeathed the whole and another one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two Hanafi positions on distributing the available one-third and apply the proportional reduction method (Sahibayn) to similar cases.

Core Idea
Two legatees, one for the whole estate, another for one-third: equal or proportional division of the one-third?

When a testator bequeaths his entire estate to one person and one-third to another, exceeding the legal limit of one-third, the heirs' consent is required. If they do not approve, only one-third of the estate is available. How should this one-third be split? This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa and his two main disciples, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, on the method of apportionment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core case and limit
Note that bequests beyond one-third are void without heirs' approval. Here, two bequests total 1 + 1/3 = 4/3 of the estate, so only one-third is available.
The one-third limit is a default rule.
2
State Abu Hanifa's position
Abu Hanifa said the one-third is divided equally (half-half) between the two legatees. Each gets 1/6 of the estate.
His reasoning: both bequests are reduced to one-third, making them equal.
3
State the Sahibayn's position
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad said the one-third is divided into four parts (arbā'an). The whole-estate legatee gets three parts (1/4 of the estate) and the one-third legatee gets one part (1/12).
This is proportional abatement: each bequest is reduced to a quarter of its intended amount.
4
Understand the practical difference
Under Abu Hanifa: each gets 1/6. Under the Sahibayn: one gets 1/4, the other gets 1/12. The difference matters for the actual shares.
The Sahibayn's method aligns with the general principle of proportional reduction (yahussan).
5
Identify the mufta bihi position
Later Hanafi practice often adopts the proportional method of the Sahibayn for multiple bequests, but the text does not explicitly give tarjih.
The footnote from al-Hasan supports proportional division.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۱۵۶ (۱۹) وان اوطى لاحدهما بجميع ماله وللأخر بالثلث فلم تجز الورثة فالثلث بينهما ارباعا عند ابي يوسف ومحمد وعند ابي حنيفة فالثلث بينهما نصفان اگر دونوں میں سے ایک کے لئے تمام مال کی وصیت کی اور دوسرے کے لئے تہائی مال کی ، اور ورثہ نے اجازت نہیں دی تو تہائی دونوں کے درمیان چار حصوں پر ہوگا امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے نزدیک۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ تہائی دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت حسن نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی درہم کی وصیت کرے اور چھٹے حصے کی تو سب حصے کئے جائیں گے۔
Rule 19: And if he bequeaths to one of them his entire estate and to the other one-third, and the heirs do not approve, then the one-third is divided between them in fourths according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and according to Abu Hanifa the one-third is half-half between them. Explanation: If a man makes a bequest of his entire estate to one person and one-third to another, and the heirs do not approve, then the one-third will be divided into four parts according to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, and Imam Abu Hanifa said it will be divided half-half. Footnote: (a) al-Hasan said: If a man bequeaths a dirham and one-sixth, then all are divided proportionally.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a case where a testator bequeaths his entire estate to one person and one-third to another, and the heirs do not approve the excess. Since bequests beyond one-third are invalid without heirs' consent, only one-third of the estate is available for distribution. The disagreement is how to apportion this one-third between the two legatees. Abu Hanifa holds that the two bequests (whole estate and one-third) are treated as competing claims, and since each is intended to receive the whole one-third? Actually, the intended shares are full estate (1) and one-third (1/3), so their intended proportions are 1:1/3 or 3:1. But Abu Hanifa's view is that the one-third is divided equally (half-half). The reasoning is that the bequest of the entire estate is reduced to one-third because that is the legal limit, and the other bequest is also one-third, so both become one-third claims, thus equal. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that the bequest of the entire estate is reduced to one-third, but the other bequest was one-third already, so the total intended is two-thirds? Actually, the total intended bequest is 1 + 1/3 = 4/3. Since only one-third is available, the reduction factor is (1/3) / (4/3) = 1/4. So each bequest is reduced to one-fourth of the intended amount. The bequest of the whole becomes 1/4 of the whole? Wait: We need to think carefully. The Hanafi rule: Multiple bequests are reduced proportionally to fit within one-third. Here, the first bequest is for the entire estate (1), the second is for one-third (1/3). Total intended = 1 + 1/3 = 4/3. Since only one-third (1/3) is available, each bequest gets (1/3)/(4/3) = 1/4 of the intended. So the first gets 1/4 of 1 = 1/4 of the estate, the second gets 1/4 of 1/3 = 1/12 of the estate. But the dispute is stated as: 'the one-third is divided between them in fourths' vs 'half-half'. In fourths means the one-third is divided into four parts: one fourth (1/12 of estate) goes to one and three fourths (1/4 of estate) to the other? Actually, if the first gets 1/4 of the estate and the second gets 1/12, then the ratio is 3:1. So the first gets three quarters of the available third, the second gets one quarter. So indeed, the one-third is divided into four parts: three to the first, one to the second. That matches 'ارباعا' (in fourths). Abu Hanifa says half-half, i.e., each gets 1/6 of the estate. The Sahibayn's view is the proportional reduction method (yahussan) applied strictly. The footnote from al-Hasan supports the proportional method. The mufta bihi position is that of the Sahibayn for this case? The text does not specify tarjih here, but later authorities often follow the proportional method.

Key Terms
ارباعا (arbā'an): In fourths; here it means the one-third is divided into four equal shares, three to one and one to the other.
نصفان (nisfān): Two halves; i.e., equal division of the one-third.
حس (huss): Proportional abatement or reduction when bequests exceed one-third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad, when a testator bequeaths his entire estate to one person and one-third to another, and the heirs do not approve, what is the distribution of the available one-third?
A) Each gets half of the one-third.
B) The one who was bequeathed the whole estate gets three-fourths of the one-third, and the one who was bequeathed one-third gets one-fourth.
C) The one who was bequeathed the whole estate gets one-fourth of the one-third, and the other gets three-fourths.
D) The entire one-third goes to the one who was bequeathed the whole estate.

Key Takeaway
When bequests exceed one-third and heirs object, the available one-third is distributed proportionally (Sahibayn) rather than equally (Abu Hanifa) in the relied-upon position.

Equal Division of One-Third Between Two Legatees
Ruling on dividing one-third equally when two legacies are of the same proportion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the rule of proportional abatement when multiple bequests exceed one-third and identify the condition for equal division.

Core Idea
When two bequests each claim the entire one-third, they share it equally—heirs' consent determines the fate of excess.

In Islamic inheritance law (wasiyyah), a testator may leave multiple bequests. If the total exceeds the permitted one-third and the heirs do not consent, the Hanafi rule is proportional abatement within the one-third. This lesson examines the specific case where each bequest is exactly one-third, leading to equal division between the two legatees.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Problem
Two bequests, each of one-third of the estate, are made. Together they exceed the one-third limit.
2
Heirs' Non-Consent
The heirs do not consent to the excess; thus the bequests are limited to the one-third that is effective.
3
Apply the Rule
Since both bequests are of equal proportion (each is one-third), the available one-third is divided equally between the two legatees.
4
Recognize the Proof
The commentator cites the statement of Zuhri, a prominent Tabi'i, who instructed dividing the one-third between them, supporting the Hanafi position of proportional distribution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة فالثلث بينهما نصفان. کسی کے لئے وصیت کر دی تو حضرت زہری نے فرمایا کہ تہائی مال کو دونوں کے درمیان حصے کر دو۔
He bequeathed one-third of his property and the heirs did not consent, so the third is divided between them in halves. Some made a bequest; then Hadhrat Zuhri said: Divide the one-third of the property between the two.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This is a ruling from the matn: When a testator bequeaths a one-third share to two different persons (each equivalent to one-third of the whole estate, thus exceeding the permissible one-third limit), and the heirs do not consent to the excess, the one-third that is effective is divided equally between the two legatees. The commentary cites a statement from Zuhri (a prominent Tabi'i) supporting this proportional division. The proof is based on the principle that the bequest can only take effect from one-third of the estate, and when multiple legacies compete, they share the one-third proportionally. This ruling is an application of the general rule that when total bequests exceed one-third, they abate proportionally within the one-third. The report from Zuhri serves as a proof (athar) for this practice.

Key Terms
وصية (wasiyya): A bequest of property made by a person to take effect after death, limited to one-third of the estate unless heirs consent to more.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Equally (half and half)
C) Only the first bequest takes effect
D) The one-third is invalidated entirely

Key Takeaway
When two bequests of equal proportion compete for the same one-third, the one-third is divided equally between them.

Proportional Division When Bequests Are One-Third and One-Sixth
Ruling on dividing one-third proportionally when bequests are one-third and one-sixth

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to calculate the proportional shares of two legatees when one is bequeathed one-third and the other one-sixth, given that the heirs do not consent.

Core Idea
When total bequests exceed one-third, the one-third is divided proportionally based on the face values.

This lesson covers a common scenario in Islamic inheritance where a testator makes multiple bequests that together exceed the one-third limit. Without heir consent, the one-third available must be divided among the legatees in proportion to the amounts prescribed. We will see how this proportional division works with a numerical example and learn the underlying principle.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prescribed bequests
Note the fractions of the estate each legatee is entitled to if the will were fully executed. Here: one-third (1/3) and one-sixth (1/6).
The total is 1/2, exceeding the 1/3 limit.
2
Find the ratio of the bequests
Convert to a common denominator: 1/3 = 2/6, 1/6 = 1/6. Ratio = 2:1.
One-third is double one-sixth.
3
Divide the one-third proportionally
The one-third is divided into shares equal to the sum of ratio parts (2+1=3). The first legatee gets 2/3 of the one-third (2/9 of estate), the second gets 1/3 of the one-third (1/9 of estate).
Alternatively: multiply one-third by each ratio part divided by total parts.
4
Verify with an example
If estate is 100 dirhams, the one-third is 33.33. The first legatee receives 2/3 of 33.33 = 22.22 dirhams; the second receives 1/3 = 11.11 dirhams.
These amounts are in the ratio 2:1.
5
Principle check
Confirm that the division respects the rule that no bequest can force more than one-third without heir consent.
The total paid is one-third, not exceeding it.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وان أوصى لأحدهما بالثلث والآخر بالسدس فالثلث بينهما أثلاثا. وان أوصى لأحدهما بجميع ماله وللآخر بثلث ماله ولم تجز الورثة فالثلث بينهما على أربعة أسهم عند أبي يوسف ومحمد رحمهما الله تعالى وقال أبو حنيفة ملیں گے۔ وعن الحسن أنه قال في رجل أوصى بدرهم وبالسدس ونحوه قال يتحاصون جميعا. اس اثر میں ہے کہ زیادہ وصیت کر دی ہو تو سب کو حصے پر تقسیم کر دی جائے گی۔ حساب کی دوسری شکل: جس کے لئے تہائی مال کی وصیت کو ملے گا۔ کیونکہ چھٹا حصہ تہائی کا آدھا ہے۔ (۱۹) اگر دونوں میں سے ایک کے لئے تمام مال کی وصیت کی اور دوسرے کے لئے تہائی مال کی، اور ورثہ نے اجازت نہیں دی تو تہائی دونوں کے درمیان چار حصوں پر ہوگا امام ابو یوسف اور امام محمد کے نزدیک۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ نے فرمایا کہ تہائی دونوں کے درمیان آدھا آدھا ہوگا۔ حاشیہ: حضرت حسن نے فرمایا کوئی آدمی درہم کی وصیت کرے اور چھٹے حصے کی تو سب حصے کئے جائیں گے۔ اس اصول پر متفرع ہے کہ تہائی سے زیادہ وصیت کرنا بیکار جائے گا۔ اور اس کے لئے تہائی ہی وصیت باقی رہے گی۔
If he bequeaths to one of them one-third and to the other one-sixth, then the one-third is divided between them into three parts. If he bequeaths to one of them all his property and to the other one-third of his property, and the heirs do not consent, then the one-third is divided between them into four shares according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa said the one-third is divided between them in halves. Commentary: He bequeathed one-third of the whole estate to one person, which out of 100 dirhams is 33.33 dirhams, and to the other one-sixth of the whole estate, which is 16.666 dirhams. When combined, they amount to half the estate. The rule is that only a one-third bequest is valid. So each legatee will receive one-third less than his share. The one who was bequeathed the full third would have received 33.33 dirhams, now reduced by one-third to 22.22 dirhams. The one who was bequeathed one-sixth would have received 16.666 dirhams, now reduced by one-third to 11.11 dirhams. And it is reported that al-Hasan said regarding a man who bequeathed a dirham and one-sixth and the like: they all share proportionally. This report indicates that when bequests exceed the limit, they are divided proportionally. Another calculation: The one who was bequeathed one-third has twice the share of the one bequeathed one-sixth. So 33.33 dirhams is divided into three parts: two parts (22.22) go to the first, one part (11.11) to the second. Because one-sixth is half of one-third. (19) If he bequeaths to one his entire estate and to another one-third, and the heirs do not consent, then according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the one-third is divided into four shares; Abu Hanifa said it is divided into halves. Footnote: al-Hasan said that if a man bequeaths a dirham and one-sixth, they all share proportionally. Then, Abu Hanifa said that any bequest exceeding one-third is void; it cannot be made. So the legatee's bequest reduces to one-third. Hence, the one who was bequeathed the entire estate is treated as having a bequest of one-third, and the other also one-third; they are equal, so the one-third is divided equally between them, each receiving half of 33.33 dirhams, i.e., 16.66 dirhams. The principle is that bequeathing more than one-third is invalid, and only the one-third remains effective.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios. First, when one legatee is bequeathed one-third of the estate and another one-sixth, the total prescribed shares are one-third + one-sixth = one-half, which exceeds the permitted one-third. Since the heirs do not consent, the effective one-third must be divided proportionally according to the face value of each bequest. The ratio is 2:1 (one-third is double one-sixth), so the one-third is divided into three equal shares: two to the first, one to the second. The commentary provides a numerical example with 100 dirhams. Second, when one legatee is bequeathed the entire estate (which is one-third in effect? Actually it's the whole, but since only one-third can be willed, the bequest of the whole is treated as a bequest of one-third subject to abatement) and another is bequeathed one-third, the total prescribed shares are one-third (for total estate) + one-third = two-thirds? Actually careful: the testator bequeaths the whole estate (which in itself is a bequest of 100% but only 1/3 is permissible) to one person, and another third of the estate to another. The total prescribed proportion is 1 (whole) + 1/3 = 4/3, but this is not the same. The matn says: 'if he bequeaths to one his entire property and to another one-third of his property, and the heirs do not consent, then the one-third is divided between them into four shares according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa said the one-third is divided equally.' The commentary explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the bequest of the whole estate is void beyond one-third, so it reduces to a bequest of one-third. Thus both legatees effectively have a bequest of one-third each, so they share the one-third equally. The two companions consider the bequest of the whole estate as having a weight of three units compared to the one-third bequest (since the whole is three times one-third), so they divide the one-third into four shares: three for the first, one for the second. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The athar from Hasan al-Basri (reported in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) supports proportional abatement generally. The passage also states the principle that a bequest exceeding one-third is invalid (batil) and reverts to one-third.

Key Terms
أثلاثا (athlathan): In three parts; the one-third is divided into three equal shares.
تحاصوا (tahasu): They share proportionally; when multiple bequests exceed one-third, they abate proportionally.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 1/2
B) 1/3
C) 1/4
D) 1/6

Key Takeaway
When multiple bequests exceed one-third without heir consent, the one-third is divided proportionally according to the ratio of the prescribed bequests.

Division When Bequests Are the Entire Estate and One-Third: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on dividing the one-third

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on dividing the one-third when the testator bequeaths the entire estate to one and one-third to another, and calculate the shares according to each view.

Core Idea
When one bequest is the entire estate and another is one-third, the one-third is divided either equally (Abu Hanifa) or in a 3:1 ratio (Sahibayn).

This lesson explores an intra-Hanafi dispute on a specific wasiyyah scenario. When a testator bequeaths his entire estate to one person and one-third to another, and heirs do not consent, how should the available one-third be divided? The answer depends on how one views the bequest of the whole estate: does it become a simple one-third bequest or retain weight equal to three times the other bequest? We will examine both proofs.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Legatee A is bequeathed the entire estate. Legatee B is bequeathed one-third. Heirs do not consent to the excess over one-third.
Only one-third of the estate is available for bequests.
2
Understand Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa argued that the bequest of the whole estate is only effective for one-third; the rest is void. Thus both legatees effectively have one-third bequests, so they are equal. The one-third is divided equally (each gets 1/6 of the estate).
Key principle: excess above one-third is invalid, so the whole becomes a one-third.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad argued that the bequest of the whole estate carries weight proportional to three one-thirds (since the whole is three times one-third). The other bequest is one-third. The total 'parts' are 4:3 for the whole estate legatee, 1 for the one-third legatee. The one-third is divided into 4 shares: 3 to the first, 1 to the second.
This gives the whole estate legatee 1/4 of the estate, and the other 1/12.
4
Compare the results numerically
For a 100 dirham estate: Abu Hanifa gives both 16.66 dirhams each. Sahibayn give 25 dirhams to the whole estate legatee and 8.33 dirhams to the one-third legatee.
Difference is significant in practical outcome.

If he bequeaths to one of them one-third and to the other one-sixth, then the one-third is divided between them into three parts. If he bequeaths to one of them all his property and to the other one-third of his property, and the heirs do not consent, then the one-third is divided between them into four shares according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa said the one-third is divided between them in halves. Commentary: He bequeathed one-third of the whole estate to one person, which out of 100 dirhams is 33.33 dirhams, and to the other one-sixth of the whole estate, which is 16.666 dirhams. When combined, they amount to half the estate. The rule is that only a one-third bequest is valid. So each legatee will receive one-third less than his share. The one who was bequeathed the full third would have received 33.33 dirhams, now reduced by one-third to 22.22 dirhams. The one who was bequeathed one-sixth would have received 16.666 dirhams, now reduced by one-third to 11.11 dirhams. And it is reported that al-Hasan said regarding a man who bequeathed a dirham and one-sixth and the like: they all share proportionally. This report indicates that when bequests exceed the limit, they are divided proportionally. Another calculation: The one who was bequeathed one-third has twice the share of the one bequeathed one-sixth. So 33.33 dirhams is divided into three parts: two parts (22.22) go to the first, one part (11.11) to the second. Because one-sixth is half of one-third. (19) If he bequeaths to one his entire estate and to another one-third, and the heirs do not consent, then according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, the one-third is divided into four shares; Abu Hanifa said it is divided into halves. Footnote: al-Hasan said that if a man bequeaths a dirham and one-sixth, they all share proportionally. Then, Abu Hanifa said that any bequest exceeding one-third is void; it cannot be made. So the legatee's bequest reduces to one-third. Hence, the one who was bequeathed the entire estate is treated as having a bequest of one-third, and the other also one-third; they are equal, so the one-third is divided equally between them, each receiving half of 33.33 dirhams, i.e., 16.66 dirhams. The principle is that bequeathing more than one-third is invalid, and only the one-third remains effective.
Source pages p. 372

Commentary
This passage covers two scenarios. First, when one legatee is bequeathed one-third of the estate and another one-sixth, the total prescribed shares are one-third + one-sixth = one-half, which exceeds the permitted one-third. Since the heirs do not consent, the effective one-third must be divided proportionally according to the face value of each bequest. The ratio is 2:1 (one-third is double one-sixth), so the one-third is divided into three equal shares: two to the first, one to the second. The commentary provides a numerical example with 100 dirhams. Second, when one legatee is bequeathed the entire estate (which is one-third in effect? Actually it's the whole, but since only one-third can be willed, the bequest of the whole is treated as a bequest of one-third subject to abatement) and another is bequeathed one-third, the total prescribed shares are one-third (for total estate) + one-third = two-thirds? Actually careful: the testator bequeaths the whole estate (which in itself is a bequest of 100% but only 1/3 is permissible) to one person, and another third of the estate to another. The total prescribed proportion is 1 (whole) + 1/3 = 4/3, but this is not the same. The matn says: 'if he bequeaths to one his entire property and to another one-third of his property, and the heirs do not consent, then the one-third is divided between them into four shares according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad, and Abu Hanifa said the one-third is divided equally.' The commentary explains Abu Hanifa's reasoning: the bequest of the whole estate is void beyond one-third, so it reduces to a bequest of one-third. Thus both legatees effectively have a bequest of one-third each, so they share the one-third equally. The two companions consider the bequest of the whole estate as having a weight of three units compared to the one-third bequest (since the whole is three times one-third), so they divide the one-third into four shares: three for the first, one for the second. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute. The athar from Hasan al-Basri (reported in Musannaf Ibn Abi Shayba) supports proportional abatement generally. The passage also states the principle that a bequest exceeding one-third is invalid (batil) and reverts to one-third.

Key Terms
أثلاثا (athlathan): In three parts; here used for the number of parts in the Sahibayn's division (4 parts total? Actually, the one-third is divided into 4 shares, not into three parts. The term appears in the first scenario only.)

Key Takeaway
In the intra-Hanafi dispute, Abu Hanifa divides equally, while the Sahibayn divide the one-third in a 3:1 ratio, with the latter being the mufta bihi in later practice.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate
8 min
Abu Hanifa's Principle: Legatee Cannot Receive More Than One-Third
Ruling on the one-third limit with an example of multiple bequests

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that bequests exceeding one-third are void without consent and apply the principle of proportional abatement within the one-third limit.

Core Idea
A bequest exceeding one-third is void unless heirs consent; multiple bequests are abated within the one-third limit.

This lesson examines Imam Abu Hanifa's strict adherence to the one-third limit in wasiyyah (bequests). The rule, based on the Prophet's hadith 'al-thuluth wa al-thuluthu kathir', restricts bequests to one-third of the estate without heirs' consent. When multiple bequests compete and exceed one-third, they must be proportionally reduced. We will explore the proof and the method of abatement, noting a subtle intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn.

Guided Path
1
State the one-third rule and its proof
Identify the hadith 'al-thuluth wa al-thuluthu kathir' as the primary evidence. Understand that the Prophet (ﷺ) set one-third as the maximum for bequests without consent, and this is a zanni dalil in thubut and dalalah.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and other sources.
2
Identify the exceptions mentioned
The text lists three exceptional cases: muhabat (favor), sa'ayah (effort), and darahim mursalah (discretionary dirhams). Note that these are contexts where Abu Hanifa might allow the legatee to receive more than one-third, but the passage does not elaborate beyond naming them.
The exact scope of these exceptions is not detailed in this passage.
3
Analyze the example of multiple bequests
Consider the scenario: testator bequeaths whole estate (100 dirhams) to one legatee and one-third (33.33 dirhams) to another. The total bequests (133.33) exceed the one-third limit (33.33). Therefore, the bequests must be abated to fit within the one-third.
The example is from the Urdu commentary.
4
Apply the proportional abatement method
Using the Sahibayn's method, calculate each legatee's share proportionally. The first legatee's claim is three times the second (since whole is three times one-third). Thus, the total shares are 4, with the first getting 3/4 of the one-third (24.999 dirhams) and the second getting 1/4 (8.33 dirhams). This ensures the sum equals the one-third limit.
Abu Hanifa's own view may differ: he would likely void the whole-estate bequest and only give the first legatee one-third, but the passage uses the Sahibayn's method for illustration.
5
Reaffirm the general principle
The passage concludes that Abu Hanifa does not allow any legatee to take more than one-third of the estate. Any bequest exceeding one-third is void and reverts to a bequest of one-third (with appropriate abatement). This is the operative rule in fatwa.
The muta'akhirin generally follow the proportional abatement method of the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
(۲۰) ولا يضرب أبو حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى للموصى له بما زاد على الثلث إلا في محابات وسعاية ودراهم مرسلة. تشریح: ایک آدمی کے لئے پورے مال کی وصیت کی مثلا سو درہم اس کے پاس تھے تمام ہی کی وصیت زید کے لئے کر دی۔ پھر دوسرے آدمی کے لئے اس کی تہائی یعنی 33.33 درہم کی وصیت کر دی تو مجموعہ 100+33.33=133.33 درہم کی وصیت کر دی۔ حالانکہ قاعدہ گزر چکا ہے کہ ورثہ اجازت نہ دے تو پورے مال کی تنہائی ہی وصیت کر سکتا ہے۔ یعنی پورا مال سو درہم ہے تو اس میں سے 33.33 درہم ہی وصیت کر سکتا ہے۔ اس لئے اب دیکھنا ہوگا کہ 33.33 میں سے پورے مال کی وصیت کئے جانے والے کے کتنے حصے ہوں گے اور تہائی مال وصیت کئے جانے والے کے کتنے حصے ہوں گے۔ اس حساب سے تقسیم کی جائینگی۔ حصص کا حساب: جس کو پورے مال یعنی 100 درہم کی وصیت کی وہ تہائی 33.33 کا تین گنا ہے۔ اس لئے تین گنا وہ اور ایک گنا تہائی وصیت والے کی مجموعہ چار گنا ہوا۔ اس لئے حساب ربع یعنی چوتھائی سے کیا جائے گا۔ جس کی وصیت تین گنی تھی اس کو تین ربع دیں اور جس کی وصیت ایک تہائی یعنی ایک گنی تھی اس کو ایک ربع دیں۔ اور پورے 100 درہم کی تہائی 33.33 درہم کو چار حصوں میں تقسیم کرے۔ ہر حصہ 8.33 درہم کا ہوگا۔ اب جس کی وصیت تین گنی تھی یعنی پورے مال کی تھی اس کو تین ربع دیں جو 24.999 درہم ہوئے۔ اور جس کی وصیت پورے مال میں سے تہائی کی تھی اس کو 8.33 درہم ملیں گے۔ حاصل یہ ہے کہ تین ربع پورے مال والے کو اور ایک ربع تہائی مال والے کو ملے گا۔ اور مجموعہ 33.33 درہم ہوگا۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ نہیں دلواتے موصى له کو تہائی سے زیادہ محابات اور سعایت میں اور دراہم مرسلہ میں۔ یہ مسئلے اس اصول پر ہیں کہ میت تہائی سے زیادہ آدھے کا یا پورے مال کی وصیت کرے تو وہ باطل ہے وہ لوٹ کر تہائی مال کی وصیت پر۔
And Abu Hanifa does not give the legatee more than one-third except in cases of muhabat (favor) and sa'ayah (effort) and darahim mursalah (discretionary dirhams). Commentary: A man bequeathed all his property, for example 100 dirhams, to Zayd, and to another man bequeathed one-third of his property, i.e., 33.33 dirhams, so total bequests become 133.33 dirhams. However, the rule is that without heirs' consent, only one-third of the estate can be bequeathed, i.e., 33.33 dirhams. So we must see what share of the 33.33 dirhams each legatee receives. Calculation: The one who was bequeathed the whole estate has a claim three times that of the one who was bequeathed one-third (since whole is three times one-third). So the total shares are four: three for the first, one for the second. Thus division is by quarters: the whole-estate legatee gets three quarters (24.999 dirhams), the one-third legatee gets one quarter (8.33 dirhams). And Abu Hanifa does not allow the legatee to take more than one-third in cases of muhabat and sa'ayah and darahim mursalah. These cases are based on the principle that if the deceased bequeaths more than one-third (e.g., half or whole estate), it is void and reverts to a bequest of one-third.
Source pages p. 373

Commentary
This lesson presents a general principle of Imam Abu Hanifa: he does not permit the legatee to receive more than one-third of the estate in certain situations, specifically in cases of muhabat (favor), sa'ayah (effort), and darahim mursalah (discretionary dirhams). The exact scope of these exceptions is not fully elaborated but likely refers to special circumstances where the one-third can be exceeded with consent or other mechanism. The commentary then gives a reverse example to that of section (19): here, the testator bequeaths the whole estate (which is effectively a bequest of one-third only, since excess is void) and also one-third of the estate to another. The calculation follows the Sahibayn's view (proportional division into four shares), and the passage notes that Abu Hanifa does not give the legatee more than one-third even in such cases, implying that the whole-estate bequest is void beyond one-third, and the legatee is only entitled to one-third (equal division). However, the numerical calculation in the commentary seems to follow the Sahibayn's method (3:1 ratio), which contradicts Abu Hanifa's position unless it is a separate discussion. The final line reaffirms that bequests exceeding one-third are void (batil) and revert to one-third. The hadith 'al-thuluth wa al-thuluthu kathir' (one-third, and one-third is a lot) from Sunan Abi Dawud is referenced as the basis for the one-third limitation.

Key Terms
محابات (muhabat): Favor, preferential treatment in bequests beyond the one-third limit.
سعاية (sa'ayah): Effort or earning; possibly a type of bequest related to compensation for services.
دراهم مرسلة (darahim mursalah): Dirhams that are left discretionary; perhaps unallocated funds in a bequest.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what happens if a testator bequeaths more than one-third of his estate without the heirs' consent?
A) The entire bequest is valid
B) The bequest is reduced to one-third
C) The bequest is void entirely
D) The heirs must pay the excess from their own shares

Key Takeaway
Bequests exceeding one-third without heirs' consent are void; when multiple bequests compete, they are abated proportionally (mufta bihi) to fit within the one-third limit.

Wasiyyah — Bequest
intermediate

Three Types of Wills: Muhabat, Sa'aya, and Murasla Dirhams
Explaining three will scenarios with proportional division

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that a will exceeding one-third implicitly is not void but proportionally divided, and calculate the shares in the three scenarios of Muhabat, Sa'ayah, and Murasla Dirhams.

Core Idea
An implicit will exceeding one-third is not void; the one-third is distributed proportionally.

When a testator leaves a will for a specific amount or transaction that turns out to exceed one-third of the estate, the common assumption is that the will becomes void. However, Hanafi fiqh distinguishes between explicit and implicit wording. If the testator does not say 'half' or 'all' but merely specifies amounts or actions, the will remains valid, and the one-third of the estate is divided proportionally among the beneficiaries. This lesson unpacks three classic scenarios: underpriced sale (Muhabat), freeing slaves (Sa'ayah), and unspecified dirham bequests (Murasla Dirhams). Understanding this rule is crucial for drafting wills and calculating estate distributions correctly.

Guided Path
1
Understand the core principle
Key rule: If a testator uses explicit wording ('I will half my wealth' or 'I will all my wealth') and that exceeds one-third, the will becomes void to the extent of the excess and reduces to one-third. But if the testator specifies amounts (e.g., 'Give Zayd 30 dirhams') without referring to the whole or half, the will is not void. If those amounts later exceed one-third of the estate, the one-third is divided proportionally among the legatees.
This is the position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) and the relied-upon view.
2
Analyze the Muhabat scenario (underpriced sale)
A testator owns a slave worth 30 dirhams and wills: 'Sell this slave to Zayd for 10 dirhams.' The 20 dirham discount is an implied donation. If the slave is the only asset, the will implies a donation of 20 dirhams (more than half the estate? 20 > 15? Actually 20 > 15, so it's more than one-third? But the testator didn't say 'half' or 'all'). According to the Sahibayn, the will is valid. One-third of the estate (10 dirhams) is the will portion. So Zayd receives the donation of 10 dirhams (the one-third of the implied donation? Actually the calculation: the slave is sold for 10 dirhams, but the testator's donation is 20 dirhams. One-third of 30 is 10, so the donation is honoured only up to 10 dirhams. Thus Zayd gets a discount of 10 dirhams (the will) and must pay 20 dirhams for the slave. (The text says: remaining 20 dirhams must be paid by the buyer.)
If there is another asset (e.g., another slave), the one-third of total estate is divided proportionally between the two implied donations.
3
Examine the Sa'ayah scenario (freeing slaves)
A testator wills to free two slaves: one worth 30 dirhams, the other worth 60 dirhams. He does not say 'free half of them' or 'free all'. After his death, the estate consists only of these two slaves. The will to free both consumes the entire estate, which exceeds one-third. But because the testator did not use explicit language, the will is not void. Instead, one-third of the total value (90 dirhams) = 30 dirhams is applied to the will. This one-third is divided proportionally: for the 30-dirham slave, one-third of his value (10 dirhams) is freed; the remaining two-thirds (20 dirhams) he must earn (sa'ayah) to pay the heirs. For the 60-dirham slave, one-third (20 dirhams) is freed, and he must earn 40 dirhams.
The slaves are not freed entirely; they become partially free and must work to purchase the remaining portion of their freedom.
4
Apply the Murasla Dirhams scenario (unspecified dirham bequests)
A testator wills: 'Give Zayd 30 dirhams and 'Umar 60 dirhams.' He does not say 'give half' or 'give all'. His total estate is 90 dirhams. The total bequest (90) equals the estate, so it exceeds one-third (30). However, because the wording is not explicit, the will is valid. One-third of the estate (30 dirhams) is divided proportionally: total willed amount = 90. Zayd's share of the one-third = (30/90)*30 = 10 dirhams. 'Umar's share = (60/90)*30 = 20 dirhams. The remaining 60 dirhams go to the legal heirs.
The same principle applies: if the testator had said 'I will half my wealth', the will would have been void to the excess and reduced to one-third equally, but here the proportional division gives each legatee according to their intended ratio.
