Explicit and Implicit Revocation of a Will
Explains that explicit words or actions indicating revocation nullify a will

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish explicit revocation from implicit revocation of a will and apply the Hanafi ruling that both are valid.

Core Idea
Actions that clearly contradict a will effectively revoke it, just like explicit words.

Revocation of a will (ruju') is an important legal act. A testator may change their mind, and Islamic law recognizes two clear ways to do so: explicit verbal revocation or implicit revocation through actions that clearly indicate the intent to cancel the bequest. This lesson unpacks both methods and their legal proof from the Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of revocation
The passage explicitly divides revocation into explicit (صراحة) and implicit (دلالة). Explicit means clear words; implicit means actions that clearly indicate the intent to revoke.
2
Understand explicit revocation
Explicit revocation occurs when the testator says in plain words, e.g., 'I take back my will.' This is straightforward and leaves no room for doubt.
3
Understand implicit revocation
Implicit revocation occurs when the testator performs an action that is fundamentally inconsistent with the will, such as selling or freeing a slave that was bequeathed. The passage argues that such actions clearly show the testator no longer intends the will to stand.
4
Trace the legal proof
The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) joined his index and middle fingers to indicate closeness. This shows that gestures and actions can convey meaning like speech. By qiyas (analogy), actions indicating revocation are as valid as explicit words.
The hadith is from Sahih al-Bukhari, Kitab al-Li'an, no. 530.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۱۷۴ (۳۷) واذا صرَّح بالرجوع او فعل ما يدل على الرجوع كان رجوعا. اس اثر سے معلوم ہوا کہ وصیت منسوخ کر سکتا ہے۔ (۳۱۷۲) (۳۷) اگر صراحتہ رجوع کرے یا ایسا کام کرے جو ر جوع پر دلالت کرتا ہو تو رجوع ہو جائے گا۔ صراحة رجوع کی صورت یہ ہے کہ صاف لفظوں میں کہے کہ میں اس وصیت کو واپس لیتا ہوں۔ اور دلالتہ رجوع کی صورت یہ ہے کہ مثلا کہے کہ اس غلام کو فلاں کے لئے وصیت کرتا ہوں اور پھر اس کو بیچ دے یا آزاد کر دے تو دلالتہ پتا چلا کہ وہ وصیت سے رجوع کرنا چاہتا ہے ورنہ غلام کو بیچتا یا آزاد کیوں کرتا۔ اس لئے بیچنا اور آزاد کرنا اس بات پر دلالت ہے کہ وہ وصیت کو ختم کرنا چاہتا ہے۔ حدیث میں ہے کہ اشارہ سے کہا تو صراحت کی طرح ہو گیا۔ سمعت من سهل بن سعد الساعدي صاحب رسول الله الله يقول قال رسول الله الا الله بعثت انا والساعة كهذه من هذه او كهاتين وقرن بين السبابة والوسطى (الف) بخارى شریف، باب اللعان ، ص ۷۹۸ نمبر ( ۵۳۰) اس حدیث میں شہادت کی انگلی اور درمیانی انگلی کو ملا کر اشارہ فرمایا کہ قیامت اس طرح قریب ہے تو اشارے سے بھی کبھی بات کی وضاحت کی جاتی ہے۔ اس پر قیاس کر کے دلالت سے بھی کسی چیز کا پتالگایا جاسکتا ہے۔
3174 (37) And if he explicitly revokes or does an action that indicates revocation, it is revocation. From this effect it is known that a will can be annulled. (3172) (37) If he explicitly revokes or does an action that indicates revocation, then it will be revocation. The form of explicit revocation is that he says in clear words: I take back this will. The form of implicit revocation is that he says, for example, I bequeath this slave to so-and-so, then he sells him or frees him, then by implication it is known that he wants to revoke the will; otherwise why would he sell or free the slave? Therefore selling and freeing indicate that he wants to terminate the will. In a hadith, it is said that speaking by gesture is like explicit statement. I heard from Sahl ibn Sa'd al-Sa'idi, the companion of the Messenger of Allah, saying: The Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, I and the Hour have been sent like this and that' or 'like these two', and he joined his index and middle fingers. (Bukhari, Chapter of Li'an, p. 798, no. 530). In this hadith, by joining the index and middle fingers he gestured that the Hour is near. So sometimes a matter is clarified by gesture. By analogy, something can be understood by implication.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof about revocation of a will. It states that revocation can be either explicit (verbal) or implicit (by actions that clearly indicate the testator's intent to revoke). Explicit revocation is when the testator says in clear words that he is taking back the will. Implicit revocation occurs when the testator does an action inconsistent with the will, such as selling or freeing a slave that was bequeathed; this action shows he no longer wishes the will to stand. The proof is a hadith where the Prophet (peace be upon him) gestured with his fingers to convey meaning; this shows that actions and gestures can be as effective as explicit speech in conveying intent. Thus, any clear indication of revocation, whether verbal or through actions, is legally sufficient to nullify a will.

Key Terms
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation of a will, i.e., canceling or taking back the bequest.
دلالت (dalalah): Implication or indication; evidence of intent derived from actions or context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The testator says 'I never made a will'
B) The testator sells the property that was bequeathed in the will
C) The testator tears up the will document
D) The testator writes a new will without mentioning the previous one

Key Takeaway
Revocation of a will can be achieved either by explicit words or by any action that clearly shows the testator's intent to cancel the bequest, as actions are legally equivalent to speech when intent is clear.

Denial of a Will: Not Revocation – An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
States rule and counterview on denial as revocation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between denial (jahd) and revocation (ruju') of a will and state the Hanafi position on whether denial constitutes revocation.

Core Idea
Denial that a will ever existed is not revocation; revocation requires acknowledging the will and then cancelling it.

This lesson examines a subtle intra-Hanafi dispute: if a testator denies ever making a will, does that denial count as revoking the will? The ruling turns on the precise legal definition of revocation. We will explore the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and Imam Abu Yusuf, and understand why the relied-upon view treats denial and revocation as distinct acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act under dispute
The act is 'jahd al-wasiyyah' – the testator's statement that he never made a will. We must determine whether this statement has the legal effect of revoking the will (ruju').
2
Define revocation (ruju')
Ruju' means to take back or annul a will that one has previously made. It presupposes that the will existed and that the testator is now cancelling it.
Revocation implies an existing act and a conscious decision to undo it.
3
Compare denial with revocation
Denial asserts that the will never came into existence. In denial, there is no acknowledgment of a prior will. Thus, the core element of ruju' – retroactive cancellation – is missing.
Denial is a negation of the past, not a cancellation of a known act.
4
Analyze Imam Abu Hanifa's position
Imam Abu Hanifa holds that denial is not revocation. His proof: ruju' requires admitting the will's prior existence, which denial does not. Without that admission, the definition of ruju' is not met.
The text sides with this view as the basis of the ruling.
5
Analyze Imam Abu Yusuf's counterview
Imam Abu Yusuf argues that denial is a stronger form of revocation. If milder cancellation counts as ruju', then total negation should count even more. He sees an implicit intent to nullify the will.
His reasoning is based on the intensity of rejection, not on the technical definition.
6
Determine the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school is that denial does not constitute revocation. The will remains valid despite the testator's denial. This is the view adopted by the author of the matn.
The practical consequence: beneficiaries can still claim under the will.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۷۵] (۳۸) ومـن جـحـد الـوصـيـة لـم يـكـن رجوعا. یوں نہیں کہتا کہ میں نے وصیت کی ہے لیکن اس کو ختم کرتا ہوں بلکہ یوں کہتا ہے کہ میں نے کبھی وصیت کی ہی نہیں ہے۔ تو اس سے رجوع نہیں ہوگا۔ رجوع کا مطلب ہے کہ پہلے وصیت کی تھی اب اس کو ختم کر رہا ہوں۔ اور انکار میں یہ ہے کہ میں نے کبھی وصیت کی ہی نہیں تو انکار میں رجوع کا معنی نہیں پایا جاتا ہے اس لئے اس سے رجوع نہیں ہوگا۔ امام ابو یوسف فرماتے ہیں کہ انکار میں بھی رجوع کا معنی پایا جاتا ہے۔ کیونکہ رجوع کا معنی ہے کہ پہلے وصیت کی تھی اب واپس لیتا ہوں۔ اور انکار میں ہے کہ کبھی نہیں ہے۔ تو انکار میں رجوع کی بات کی شدت ہے اس لئے رجوع کا معنی پایا گیا۔ اس لئے رجوع ہو جائے گا۔
[3175] (38) And whoever denies the will, it is not revocation. He does not say: I made a will but I cancel it; rather he says: I never made a will. So that is not revocation. The meaning of revocation is that he had previously made a will and now he terminates it. Denial is that he never made a will, so the meaning of revocation is not found in denial; therefore it is not revocation. Imam Abu Yusuf says that the meaning of revocation is also found in denial. Because the meaning of revocation is that he had made a will and now he takes it back. In denial, he says it never existed. So in denial there is an intensity of revocation, thus the meaning of revocation is found. Therefore it will be revocation.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage presents a intra-Hanafi dispute regarding whether denial of a will constitutes revocation. The text first states the rule: denying that one made a will does not count as revocation. The reasoning is that revocation requires acknowledging the prior existence of the will and then annulling it. Denial, by contrast, asserts that the will never existed in the first place. Therefore, the concept of revocation is not found in denial. However, Imam Abu Yusuf argues that denial is a stronger form of revocation: if revocation means taking back what was given, then denying it ever existed is an even more emphatic rejection. Thus, in his view, denial should be considered revocation. The text does not explicitly resolve the dispute, but the structure and presentation suggest the first view (Imam Abu Hanifa's) is the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
جحد (jahd): Denial; asserting that one never made a will.
رجوع (ruju'): Revocation; taking back or annulling a will that has been made.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why does Imam Abu Hanifa consider denial of a will not to be revocation?
A) Because denial is a form of lying, which is forbidden
B) Because revocation requires acknowledging the prior existence of the will, which denial does not
C) Because denial is always made under duress
D) Because the will must be in writing to be revoked

Key Takeaway
Denial of a will is not revocation; the will stands unless explicitly revoked.

Defining 'Neighbors' in a Will: Hanafi, Sahibayn, and Shafi'i Views
Defines neighbors in a will, presenting three views

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definitions of 'neighbor' in a will and distinguish between the views of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam al-Shafi'i, citing the evidence for each.

Core Idea
In a will for 'neighbors,' the Hanafi school disagrees on the definition—attached houses or mosque vicinity?

This passage addresses a practical question: when a testator says 'for my neighbors,' who exactly receives the bequest? The Hanafi school has an internal disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two disciples (the Sahibayn), and the Shafi'i school offers a different definition. Understanding this dispute clarifies how a will's beneficiaries are determined and highlights the role of hadith interpretation in deriving legal definitions.

Guided Path
1
State Imam Abu Hanifa's definition of neighbors in a will
Identify the condition: only those whose houses are physically attached (mulasiq) to the testator's house. Cite the hadith about the nearest neighbor by door.
This is the primary Hanafi view presented in the matn.
2
Identify the Sahibayn's alternative definition within the Hanafi school
Note that Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani define neighbors as all who hear the call to prayer from the local mosque, based on hadiths about the obligation of neighbors to attend congregational prayer.
This expands the potential beneficiaries.
3
Present the Shafi'i view on the extent of neighborly rights
Imam al-Shafi'i defines neighbors as those within forty houses in all directions, citing the hadith about Jibril's advice to the Prophet to treat neighbors up to forty houses.
This is the broadest definition among the three.
4
Apply the thamarah al-khilaf: determine who receives the bequest under each definition
Given a testator living in a specific house, work through who qualifies under Abu Hanifa (immediate adjoining houses), the Sahibayn (all within mosque earshot), and al-Shafi'i (40-house radius).
The practical distribution differs significantly.
5
Reflect on how the text handles internal Hanafi disagreement
The text presents Abu Hanifa's view first, then acknowledges the Sahibayn's view with its proofs, but does not explicitly resolve the ikhtilaf. This is common in later Hanafi works where multiple opinions are preserved.
The mufta bihi position in practice is Abu Hanifa's, as indicated by the matn.

[3176] (39) Whoever makes a will for his neighbors, they will be the attached neighbors according to Imam Abu Hanifa. According to Imam Abu Hanifa, the neighbors entitled to the will are those whose house is attached to the testator's house. There is a hadith: From Aisha, she said: O Messenger of Allah, I have two neighbors; to which of them should I give a gift? He said: To the one whose door is nearer to you. (Bukhari, Chapter on Neighbors' Proximity, p. 300, no. 2259). In this hadith, there are two neighbors. It indicates that only attached neighbors are considered. Footnote: (from previous page) Umar said: If someone frees a slave during his terminal illness, that is also a will; he may revoke it if he wishes. (a) He said: I and the Hour have been sent like this and that, or like these two, and he joined his index and middle fingers. (b) He said: I have two neighbors; to whom should I give a gift? He said: To the one whose door is nearer to you. The attached ones according to Abu Hanifa. (39) And whoever makes a will for his in-laws, the will... The whole neighborhood is not called neighbors; rather only those whose houses are attached on either side are neighbors, and they receive the bequest. In common usage, these are called neighbors. The Sahibayn say that all who are associated with the mosque of that locality are neighbors and will receive the bequest. They say that those within range of the mosque's call to prayer are neighbors. Evidence: From Abu Huraira, the Prophet said: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' (a) and its explanation: From Ali: 'Whoever is a neighbor of the mosque and hears the caller calling and does not answer without excuse, there is no prayer for him.' (Dar Qutni, Chapter on Urging the Neighbor of the Mosque to Pray in it Except with Excuse, vol. 1, p. 1399, no. 1539/1538; Bayhaqi, Chapter on Severity of Abandoning Congregation without Excuse, vol. 3, p. 81, no. 4945). From this hadith it is known that all mosque-goers are neighbors. Therefore they all get a share. Imam al-Shafi'i says that neighbors are counted up to forty houses: ten on the right, ten on the left, ten in front, ten behind. Hadith: From Aisha that the Prophet said: 'Jibril advised me about the neighbor up to forty houses: ten from here, ten from here, ten from here, ten from here.' Isma'il said: on his right, left, front, and behind. (Bayhaqi, Chapter on a Man Saying One-Third of My Wealth to So-and-So, etc., vol. 6, p. 1351, no. 12612). From this hadith it is known that up to forty houses are neighbors and they all receive a share in the will. Jiran: plural of jar (neighbor), al-mulasiq: attached, adjoining.
Source pages p. 384

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute over the definition of 'neighbors' in a will. It first states the Hanafi position according to Imam Abu Hanifa: only those whose houses are physically attached to the testator's house are considered neighbors. This is supported by a hadith where the Prophet advised giving gifts to the neighbor whose door is nearer. The commentary contrasts this with the view of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), who define neighbors as all those who hear the call to prayer from the local mosque, citing hadiths about the obligation to attend congregation prayer. They argue that such people are considered neighbors in a broader sense. Lastly, it presents the Shafi'i position, which defines neighbors as those within forty houses in all directions, based on a hadith about Jibril's advice regarding neighbors. The passage thus shows the practical consequence: the beneficiaries of a will for 'neighbors' differ depending on which school's definition is adopted.

Key Terms
الجيران (al-jiran): Neighbors; those who are legally entitled to a bequest when the testator says 'for my neighbors'.
الملاصق (al-mulasiq): Attached, adjoining; the condition for being a neighbor according to Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'neighbors' in a will depends on the school followed; the Hanafi mufta bihi restricts it to physically attached houses, but other views extend it further.

Who Are Included as 'In-Laws' in a Will
Explains that 'in-laws' in a will means the wife's blood relatives who are mahram

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the distribution of a bequest to 'in-laws' and explain the evidence from the hadith of Juwayriyah.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'in-laws' includes all of the wife's mahram blood relatives, not just immediate family.

When someone makes a will for their 'in-laws,' the Hanafi school interprets this broadly. This lesson examines the legal definition of 'ashar (in-laws) and the proof from the hadith of Juwayriyah that establishes this inclusive ruling. Understanding this helps ensure the testator's intent is fulfilled correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The testator makes a bequest to 'his in-laws.' The Hanafi ruling states that this is valid and the bequest is distributed among all of the wife's blood relatives who are mahram (i.e., with whom marriage is permanently prohibited).
The exact wording: 'to your in-laws' (sassaral).
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Juwayriyah, where the Prophet married her, and the companions called all her blood relatives his 'ashar, freeing them.
The hadith is narrated by Aisha (may Allah please her).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The companions included all blood relatives of Juwayriyah, not just immediate family, showing that 'ashar encompasses a wide set of mahram relatives.
Approximately one hundred people were freed.
4
Define the scope
Identify who qualifies: any blood relative of the wife who is a mahram, such as her parents, siblings, nephews, uncles, aunts, etc.
The key is the relative must be a blood relative and marriage to them is permanently prohibited.
5
Consider application
Apply the rule to a scenario: if the wife has a brother and a step-brother (not blood relative), only the brother is included.
This protects the testator's likely intent to benefit close blood relatives.

[۳۱۷۷] (۴۰) جس نے وصیت کی اپنے سسرال والوں کے لئے تو بیوی کے ہر ذی رحم محرم کے لئے ہوگی۔ وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی کہ میرے سسرال والوں کے لئے وصیت کرتا ہوں تو بیوی کے تمام ذی رحم محرم مثلا ماں ، باپ، بھائی ، بہن ، بھتیجا بھیجی وغیرہ شامل ہوں گے۔ حضرت جوریہ کی حدیث میں ان تمام کو اصحار کہا گیا ہے اور تقریبا ایک سو آدمی ان کے اصحار میں شامل ہو کر آزاد ہوئے ، حدیث کا نکھرا یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت وقعت جورية بنت الحارث بن المصطلق في سهم ثابت بن قيس بن شماس ... ان رسول . الله قد تزوج جويرية فارسلوا ما في ايديهم من السبى فاعتقوهم وقالوا اصهار رسول الله الله ، فما رأينا حاشیہ : (الف) پ نے فرمایا مسجد کے پڑوسی کے لئے نماز نہیں ہوگی مگر مسجد میں (ب) حضرت علی نے فرمایا جو مسجد کے پاس ہو اور مؤذن کی اذان سنتا ہو اور بغیر عذر کے مسجد میں نہ آئے تو اس کی نماز ہی نہیں ہوتی (ج) آپ نے فرمایا حضرت جبرئیل نے مجھے کو جالیس گھر تک پڑوی کی نصیحت کی دس یہاں سے ، دس یہاں سے، دس یہاں سے اور دس یہاں ہے ۔ اسمعیل فرماتے ہیں دس دائیں جانب ، دس بائیں جانب ، دس سامنے اور دس پیچھے سے۔
[3177] (40) Whoever makes a will for his in-laws, it will be for every blood relative of the wife who is mahram. If the testator makes a will for his in-laws, then all the wife's blood relatives who are mahram, such as mother, father, brother, sister, nephew, etc., are included. In the hadith of Juwayriyah, all of them are called ashar (in-laws), and approximately one hundred people among her in-laws were freed. The hadith text: From Aisha: Juwayriyah bint al-Harith ibn al-Mustaliq fell into the share of Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas... The Messenger of Allah married Juwayriyah, so they sent what was in their hands of captives and freed them, saying: 'In-laws of the Messenger of Allah.' So we have not seen... Footnote: (a) He said: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque.' (b) Ali said: 'Whoever is a neighbor of the mosque and hears the caller calling and does not answer without excuse, there is no prayer for him.' (c) He said: 'Jibril advised me about the neighbor up to forty houses: ten from here, ten from here, ten from here, ten from here.' Isma'il said: ten on the right, ten on the left, ten in front, ten behind.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling that when a testator makes a will for his 'in-laws' (ashar), it includes all blood relatives of his wife who are mahram (i.e., with whom marriage is permanently prohibited). This includes parents, siblings, nephews, and others from the wife's side. The proof is the hadith of Juwayriyah (may Allah be pleased with her), where after the Prophet married her, the companions freed their captives, calling them the in-laws of the Messenger of Allah. This shows that the term 'ashar extends to a large group of blood relatives. The passage also inadvertently includes footnotes from earlier discussions about neighbors, which appear to be misplaced in the OCR but do not affect the core ruling.

Key Terms
اصهار (ashar): In-laws; the wife's blood relatives who are mahram to the husband.
ذو رحم محرم (dhu rihim mahram): A blood relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (mahram).

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'in-laws' is distributed among all mahram blood relatives of the wife, as proven by the hadith of Juwayriyah.

Who Is a Neighbor for a Bequest? The Hanafi Intra-Madhhab Dispute
Defining neighbors in a bequest: an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three definitions of 'neighbor' in a bequest (Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, al-Shafi'i), explain the dalil for each, and identify the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf) in distributing a bequest.

Core Idea
In a bequest to neighbors, Abu Hanifa limits it to adjoining houses; the Sahibayn include all mosque affiliates; al-Shafi'i counts forty houses.

When a testator says 'I bequeath to my neighbors,' who is included? This seemingly simple question sparked a rich dispute among Hanafi imams and across madhhabs. Understanding the precise definitions and their proofs is crucial for correctly executing a bequest. In this lesson, we will dissect the positions of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn), and Imam al-Shafi'i, and see how each derives his ruling from the sources.

Guided Path
1
State the disputed issue
Identify the legal question: When a testator makes a bequest 'to my neighbors,' who qualifies as a neighbor for receiving the bequest?
The issue is the scope of the term 'jar' (neighbor) in the context of wasiyyah.
2
Identify the Hanafi (Abu Hanifa) position and its basis
State Abu Hanifa's view: only those whose houses directly adjoin the testator's house. Note that he relies on common usage (urf) and the literal meaning of الملاصق (adjoining).
This is the mufta bihi position in the Hanafi school.
3
Identify the opposing views and their proofs
State the Sahibayn's view: all those connected to the local mosque, i.e., those who can hear the adhan. They support this with the hadith 'لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد'. Also state al-Shafi'i's view: forty houses in all directions, based on the hadith about Gabriel's advice to the Prophet regarding the neighbor up to forty houses.
Both opposing views rely on ahad hadith, which are zanni al-thubut and al-dalala.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to each proof
Explain Abu Hanifa's response: the mosque hadith is about the obligation of prayer in congregation, not about defining neighbors for bequests; the forty-house hadith is about general neighborly rights, not specifically bequests. Thus, neither hadith overrides the common understanding of 'neighbor' in the context of a bequest.
The Hanafi response shows that the dalil from the Sahibayn is not applicable (ghayr munkab) for this specific issue.
5
Determine the practical difference
Calculate the number of recipients under each view. Under Abu Hanifa, only the owners of adjoining houses (e.g., 2-4 houses). Under Sahibayn, all families who hear the adhan (could be dozens). Under al-Shafi'i, exactly forty houses (or families) in all directions. The estate shares differ accordingly.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf – the practical consequence of the scholarly disagreement.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الملاصقون عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالی ۳۱۷۷ (۴۰) و من اوطى لاصهاره فالوصية محلے کو پڑوسی نہیں کہا جائے گا بلکہ گھر کے دونوں طرف جن لوگوں کا گھر ملا ہوا ہے وہی پڑوسی ہیں اور انہیں لوگوں کو وصیت کی چیز ملے گی (۲) محاورے میں بھی انہیں لوگوں کو پڑوسی کہتے ہیں۔ صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ اس محلے کی مسجد سے جتنے لوگ متعلق ہیں سب پڑوسی ہیں اور سب کے لئے وصیت کی چیز ہوگی۔ وہ فرماتے ہیں کہ مسجد کی اذان کی آواز جہاں تک جاتی ہو وہاں تک کے لوگ پڑوس میں داخل ہیں ۔حدیث میں اس کا ثبوت ہے ۔عن ابی هريرة قال قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم لا صلوة لجار المسجد الا في المسجد (الف) اور اس کی تفسیر میں یہ ہے۔ عن علی قال من كان جار المسجد فسمع المنادي ينادى فلم يجبه من غير عذر فلا صلوة له (ب) (دار قطنی ، باب الحث لجار المسجد على الصلوة فيه الا من عذر، ج اول ص ۱۳۹۹ نمبر ۱۵۳۹/۱۵۳۸ارسفن للبیہقی ، باب ما جاء من التشديد فی ترك الجماعة من غیر عذر، ج ثالث ص ۸۱ نمبر ۴۹۴۵) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ مسجد والے سارے ہی پڑوس ہیں۔ اس لئے سب کو وصیت میں سے حصہ ملے گا۔ قائد امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ چالیس گھر تک پڑوسی شمار کئے جائیں گے، دس گھر دائیں ، دس گھر ہا ئیں ، دس گھر آگے ، دس گھر پیچھے کے لوگ ۔ حدیث یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة ان النبی الله قال اوصانی جبریل علیه السلام بالجار الى اربعين دارا عشرة من ههنا وعشرة من ههنا عشرة من ههنا وعشرة من ههنا قال اسمعيل عن يمينه وعن يساره وقباله وخلفه (ج) (سنن البيهقي ، باب الرجل يقول ثلث مالی الی فلان الخ ، ج سادس، ص ۱۳۵۱، نمبر ۱۲۶۱۲) اس حدیث سے معلوم ہوا کہ چالیس گھر تک پڑوی ہے سب کو وصیت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ جیران : جار کی جمع ہے پڑوسی، الملاصق : ملا ہوا متصل۔
The adjoining ones according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, (reference 3177, number 40): And whoever makes a bequest to his in-laws, the bequest will not be called neighbors for the locality; rather, those whose houses adjoin on both sides are the neighbors, and those people will receive the bequest. (2) In common parlance, these people are also called neighbors. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) say that all the people connected with the mosque of that locality are neighbors, and the bequest will be for all of them. They say that the people as far as the sound of the mosque's adhan reaches are included in the neighborhood. There is proof of this in the hadith: From Abu Hurairah, he said: The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, said: 'There is no prayer for the neighbor of the mosque except in the mosque' (الف). And its interpretation is: From Ali, he said: Whoever is a neighbor of the mosque and hears the caller calling but does not respond without an excuse, there is no prayer for him. (ب) (Dar Qutni, chapter on encouragement for the neighbor of the mosque to pray in it except with excuse, vol. 1, p. 1399, no. 1539/1538, and Bayhaqi, chapter on severity for abandoning congregation without excuse, vol. 3, p. 81, no. 4945). From this hadith it is understood that all mosque-goers are neighbors. Therefore, all will receive a share of the bequest. Qaid Imam Shafi'i says that up to forty houses are counted as neighbors: ten houses on the right, ten on the left, ten in front, and ten behind. The hadith: From Aisha, that the Prophet, peace be upon him, said: 'Gabriel, peace be upon him, advised me concerning the neighbor up to forty houses: ten from here, ten from here, ten from here, and ten from here.' Isma'il said: on his right, on his left, in front, and behind. (ج) (Sunan al-Bayhaqi, chapter on a man saying a third of my wealth to so-and-so, etc., vol. 6, p. 1351, no. 12612). From this hadith it is understood that up to forty houses are neighbors, all will receive a share of the bequest. Jiran: plural of jar, neighbor; al-mulasiq: adjoining, connected.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab dispute about the definition of 'neighbors' for the purpose of a bequest. The text first states the position of Imam Abu Hanifa: only those whose houses physically adjoin the testator's house are considered neighbors; they alone receive the bequest. This is also the common usage. The two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) disagree and define neighbors as all those associated with the local mosque, specifically those who can hear the adhan. They support this with a hadith that emphasizes the obligation of prayer in congregation for the mosque neighbor, arguing that the hadith's 'neighbor of the mosque' includes all such persons, thus they all share in the bequest. The text then notes that a similar hadith is also used by Imam al-Shafi'i to define neighbors as forty houses in all directions. The passage ends with lexical definitions: جيران (jiran) is the plural of جار (jar, neighbor), and الملاصق (al-mulasiq) means adjoining or connected. The dispute here is practical: if someone says 'I bequeath to my neighbors,' the recipients differ according to each view. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) limits it to contiguous neighbors, while the Sahibayn use the mosque affiliation, and al-Shafi'i uses a fixed radius. The text does not explicitly state which view is mufta bihi, but Abu Hanifa's view is given first and is the standard Hanafi position.

Key Terms
الملاصق (al-mulāṣiq): The person whose house directly adjoins the testator's house.
جار المسجد (jār al-masjid): A person living close enough to the mosque that the adhan reaches him.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, who qualifies as a neighbor for a bequest?
A) All residents of the locality
B) Those whose houses adjoin the testator's house
C) Those who hear the mosque adhan
D) All people up to forty houses in all directions

Key Takeaway
The definition of 'neighbor' in a bequest differs among scholars; the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa) limits it to adjoining houses, while Sahibayn and al-Shafi'i use broader criteria based on mosque or distance.

Bequest to In-Laws (Ashar) – Scope of Inclusion
Determining who is included in a bequest to in-laws

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which relatives are included in a bequest to 'ashar (in-laws) according to the Hanafi school and cite the hadith of Juwayriyyah as proof.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'ashar includes all the wife's dhi rahm muhrim, as demonstrated by the hadith of Juwayriyyah.

This passage clarifies a common ambiguity: when someone bequeaths to 'ashar, who exactly is included? The Hanafi ruling, based on prophetic practice, expansively includes all of the wife's blood relatives within the prohibited degrees. The hadith of Juwayriyyah shows that the Companions considered her entire clan as 'ashar of the Prophet.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making a bequest to 'ashar. The Hanafi ruling is that it includes every dhi rahm muhrim (blood relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited) of the testator's wife.
This is not about the permissibility of the bequest itself (which is mubah), but about interpreting the term 'ashar.
2
Locate the dalil
The proof is the hadith of Juwayriyyah (RA) narrated in Abu Dawud. The Companions freed all of her blood relatives, calling them 'ashar of the Messenger of Allah.
The hadith is ahad, but accepted in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The Companions referred to all of Juwayriyyah's blood relatives (approximately 100 households) as 'ashar, establishing that the term encompasses the entire clan of the wife, not just her immediate family.
This usage is taken as the 'urf (custom) of the Shariah.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given a testator with a wife, her mother, brother, and sister, all are included. If the testator has no wife, the bequest is invalid because the term has no referent.
This step solidifies the rule.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
۳۱۷۷ (۴۰) جس نے وصیت کی اپنے سسرال والوں کے لئے تو بیوی کے ہر ذی رحم محرم کے لئے ہوگی۔ وصیت کرنے والے نے وصیت کی کہ میرے سسرال والوں کے لئے وصیت کرتا ہوں تو بیوی کے تمام ذی رحم محرم مثلا ماں ، باپ، بھائی ، بہن ، بھتیجا بھیجی وغیرہ شامل ہوں گے۔ حضرت جوریہ کی حدیث میں ان تمام کو اصحار کہا گیا ہے اور تقریبا ایک سو آدمی ان کے اصحار میں شامل ہو کر آزاد ہوئے ، حدیث کا نکھرا یہ ہے۔ عن عائشة قالت وقعت جورية بنت الحارث بن المصطلق في سهم ثابت بن قيس بن شماس ... ان رسول . الله قد تزوج جويرية فارسلوا ما في ايديهم من السبى فاعتقوهم وقالوا اصهار رسول الله الله ، فما رأينا لامرأة كانت اعظم بركة على قومها منها اعتق في سببها مائة اهل بيت من بني المصطلق (الف) (ابوداؤد شریف، باب في بيع المكاتب اذ انسخت المکاتبة ، ص۱۹۲، نمبر ۳۹۳۱) اس حدیث میں حضرت جوریہ کے تمام ذی رحم محرم کو اصھار یعنی سسرالی رشتہ قرار دیا گیا جو سو آدمی تھے۔ اس لئے ذی رحم محرم داخل ہوں گے۔ اصحار : صھر کی جمع ہے اس کا معنی داماد یا بہنوئی ہے۔ لیکن آگے فتن کے مقابلے میں یہاں اس کا ترجمہ بیوی کے جو خاندان ہیں وہ مراد ہیں۔
(3177) (40) Whoever makes a bequest for his in-laws, it will be for every dhi rahm muhrim (blood relative within prohibited degrees) of the wife. The testator said: I bequeath to my in-laws, so all the wife's dhi rahm muhrim, such as mother, father, brother, sister, nephew, niece, etc., are included. In the hadith of Juwayriyyah, all of these were called 'ashar (in-laws), and approximately one hundred men among her in-laws were freed. The text of the hadith is: From Aisha, she said: Juwayriyyah bint al-Harith ibn al-Mustaliq fell into the share of Thabit ibn Qays ibn Shammas... The Messenger of Allah married Juwayriyyah, so they sent the captives in their hands and freed them, saying: 'They are the in-laws of the Messenger of Allah.' We have not seen a woman who was a greater blessing to her people than her; one hundred households of Banu al-Mustaliq were freed because of her. (الف) (Abu Dawud, chapter on sale of a mukatib when the contract is rescinded, p. 192, no. 3931). In this hadith, all of Juwayriyyah's dhi rahm muhrim were called 'ashar (in-laws), who were one hundred people. Therefore, dhi rahm muhrim are included. Ashar: plural of shahr; its meaning is son-in-law or brother-in-law. But in contrast to 'akhtan (sons-in-law), here the intended meaning is the wife's family.
Source pages p. 385

Commentary
This passage provides a ruling with proof on bequest to in-laws (اصهار). The ruling: if someone says 'I bequeath to my in-laws,' it includes every dhi rahm muhrim (blood relative within the prohibited degrees of marriage) of the testator's wife. This includes the wife's parents, siblings, and their children. The proof is the hadith of Juwayriyyah (RA), where after the Prophet (SAW) married her, the companions referred to all her blood relatives as his in-laws (اصهار) and freed them. This demonstrates that 'in-laws' in the context of a bequest encompasses all the wife's dhi rahm muhrim, not just her immediate family. The text also clarifies the linguistic meaning: اصهار (ashar) is the plural of صهر (sihr), which can mean son-in-law or brother-in-law, but here it refers to the wife's family. The ruling is based on this hadith and the common understanding. Note that this is the Hanafi position; the text does not mention any disagreement.

Key Terms
اصهار (aṣhār): In-laws; specifically the blood relatives of the wife (dhi rahm muhrim).
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥm muḥrim): A blood relative with whom marriage is permanently prohibited (e.g., mother, sister, daughter).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only his wife's parents
B) His wife's brother
C) His own sister
D) His wife's mother, brother, and sister

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to in-laws (ashar), the Hanafi ruling includes all the wife's dhi rahm muhrim, not just her immediate family.

Bequest to Sons-in-Law: General Scope
Determining who is included in a bequest to sons-in-law

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the general Hanafi ruling on who is included in a bequest to 'akhtan' and explain the qiyas used to derive it.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'sons-in-law' includes husbands of all female blood relatives, not just daughters.

When a testator makes a bequest to his 'akhtan' (sons-in-law), a question arises: does this include only the husbands of his daughters, or also husbands of other close female relatives? This passage clarifies the general Hanafi position and the reasoning behind it, citing qiyas from a hadith. We will also note a regional variation from Farghana.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) to 'akhtan'. The ruling (hukm) is that the term is interpreted to include the husband of every female dhi rahm muhrim (blood relative within prohibited degrees) of the testator.
'Dhi rahm muhrim' refers to female relatives whom one cannot marry due to blood relationship.
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) from the hadith of Juwayriyyah (رضي الله عنها). In that hadith, the term 'ashar (in-laws) included all of Juwayriyyah's dhi rahm muhrim relatives.
The hadith was discussed in the previous lesson; it establishes the broad meaning of 'ashar.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal link)
Just as 'ashar includes all blood relatives from the wife's side, 'akhtan (sons-in-law) analogously includes husbands of all blood relatives from the testator's side. The common illa (effective cause) is that both terms refer to relationships through marriage to one's female blood relatives.
The illa is 'khafiyyah' (hidden), extracted via tahqiq al-manat.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (dispute)
In Farghana, local custom restricts 'khatan' to only the husband of the daughter. Accordingly, some Hanafi scholars (e.g., author of al-Hidayah) limit the bequest to daughters' husbands in that region.
This is an intra-Hanafi variation based on 'urf (custom).
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The general Hanafi position (zahir al-riwayah) is the relied-upon view. The regional custom may override if clearly intended by the testator, but the default is the broader inclusion.
No explicit tarjih is given; the text simply reports the difference.

۱۳۱۷۸ (۴۱) کسی نے وصیت کی دامادوں کے لئے تو ہر ذی رحم محرم عورت کا شوہر تن میں داخل ہے۔ ختن کا ترجمہ داماد ہے اس لئے تمام ذی رحم محرم عورت مثلا بیٹی کا شوہر ، بہن کا شوہر، پھوپھی کا شوہر اور خالہ کا شوہر یہ سب متن میں داخل ہوں گے۔ اور ہر ایک کو وصیت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ کونے کے محاورے میں ان تمام لوگوں کو فتن یعنی داماد کہتے ہیں (۲) اوپر حضرت جوریہ کی حدیث میں حضرت جویریہ کے تمام ذی رحم محرم شامل ہوئے۔ اس پر قیاس کر کے خفتن میں اپنی ذی رحم محرم کے تمام عورتوں کے شوہر داماد میں داخل ہوں گے۔ فانی لیکن صاحب ہدایہ کے شہر فرغانہ میں خفتن صرف بیٹی کے شوہر کو کہتے ہیں اس لئے صرف بیٹیوں کے شوہروں کو وصیت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ اختان : ختن کی جمع ہے عورت کی طرف سے رشتے جیسے سر، سالہ، داماد، یہاں بیٹی کا شوہر مراد ہے۔
(13178) (41) If someone makes a bequest for his sons-in-law, then the husband of every dhi rahm muhrim woman is included in the text. The translation of 'khatan' is son-in-law; therefore, the husbands of all dhi rahm muhrim women, for example, the husband of the daughter, the husband of the sister, the husband of the paternal aunt, and the husband of the maternal aunt — all of these are included in the text. And each will receive a share of the bequest. In common parlance, all these people are called 'akhtan (sons-in-law). (2) In the above hadith of Juwayriyyah, all of Juwayriyyah's dhi rahm muhrim were included. By analogy (qiyas) on that, in 'akhtan, the husbands of all the women among one's own dhi rahm muhrim are included as sons-in-law. However, in the city of Farghana, according to the author of al-Hidayah, 'khatan' specifically refers only to the husband of the daughter; therefore, only the husbands of daughters will receive a share of the bequest. Akhtan: plural of khatan; relationships from the wife's side, such as father-in-law, mother-in-law, son-in-law; here the intended meaning is the husband of the daughter.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a bequest made to 'akhtan (sons-in-law). The primary ruling: a bequest to 'akhtan includes the husband of every female dhi rahm muhrim of the testator. This means the husbands of the testator's daughter, sister, paternal aunt, maternal aunt, etc. The evidence is based on qiyas (analogy) from the hadith of Juwayriyyah (mentioned in the previous lesson). Just as the term 'ashar (in-laws) included all of Juwayriyyah's blood relatives, similarly the term 'akhtan (sons-in-law) includes the husbands of all the testator's female blood relatives within prohibited degrees. However, the text notes a regional difference: in Farghana, the author of al-Hidayah states that 'khatan' is used only for the husband of the daughter. According to that local custom, only daughters' husbands would be included. The passage then gives the lexical definition of اختان (akhtan) as the plural of ختن (khatan), meaning relationships from the wife's side, but here specifically the husband of the daughter. The commentary explains that the analogy from the Juwayriyyah hadith is the basis for broadening the inclusion. This is an example of istihsan (juristic preference) by analogy.

Key Terms
ختن (khatan): Son-in-law; specifically the husband of a woman related to the testator by blood.
اختان (akhtān): Plural of khatan; sons-in-law.

Bequest to Relatives (Aqarib)
Determining who is included in a bequest to relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'aqarib in a bequest and identify which relatives are included and excluded.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'relatives' excludes parents and children because they are direct, not indirect, relatives.

This passage clarifies the scope of a bequest made to 'aqarib. In Hanafi law, the term 'aqarib is interpreted to include only collateral blood relatives (dhi rahm muhrim), excluding ascendants and descendants. The ruling is based on linguistic usage and a Quranic verse, ensuring the bequest reaches extended family rather than immediate heirs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the bequest scenario
Recognize that the testator has said 'I bequeath to my relatives' without specifying individuals.
The ruling applies when the term 'aqarib is used generically.
2
Define 'aqarib legally
According to Hanafi fiqh, 'aqarib means dhi rahm muhrim – blood relatives within the prohibited degrees of marriage, excluding in-laws.
Dhi rahm muhrim includes siblings, aunts, uncles, nieces, nephews, grandparents, grandchildren? Wait, parents and children are excluded. So it's collateral lines.
3
Apply the exclusion of parents and children
Parents and children are not considered 'aqarib because they are direct, not indirect, relatives in common usage.
The Quran (4:36) lists parents separately from 'aqraba, supporting this distinction.
4
Apply the principle of proximity
The bequest is distributed to the nearest relative first; if none, then to the next of kin.
If multiple relatives of equal degree exist, they share the bequest (minimum two).
5
Confirm the evidence chain
The ruling relies on linguistic custom (urf) and the Quranic verse, with children analogized (qiyas) to parents.
This ensures consistency in excluding all direct ascendants/descendants.

(3179) (42) Whoever makes a bequest for his relatives, the bequest will be for the nearest then the nearest of the dhi rahm muhrim. And parents and children will not be included. And it will be for two or more. In this issue, the meaning of 'aqarib' (relatives) is defined. Three things are said: The first thing is that if someone makes a bequest for relatives, it will be for the dhi rahm muhrim relative. Relatives by marriage (in-laws) will not be included. And among them, it will go to the nearest relative; if there is none, then the next of kin will receive the bequest. The second thing said is that parents and children are not included in 'aqarib. Because in common usage, 'aqarib refers to those who are indirect relatives. And parents and children are not indirect relatives but direct relatives. Therefore, they will not be included in a bequest to relatives. (2) In the Quranic verse, parents are mentioned separately, and 'aqraba' (kin) is mentioned after it, indicating that parents are not included in 'aqraba. Its significance is even greater. And children are analogized to this.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage defines the scope of a bequest made to 'aqarib (relatives). The ruling: if someone says 'I bequeath to my relatives,' it applies to dhi rahm muhrim (blood relatives within prohibited degrees), excluding parents and children. The bequest is distributed to the nearest relative first, then the next nearest, and so on. At least two relatives are required (the bequest is shared among them). The passage gives three key points: (1) Only blood relatives (dhi rahm muhrim) qualify; in-laws are excluded. (2) Parents and children are not considered 'relatives' in this context because they are direct, not indirect, relatives — common usage distinguishes them. (3) The Quranic verse (e.g., 4:36) mentions parents and then kin separately, showing they are distinct categories. By analogy, children are also excluded. The evidence is based on linguistic usage (urf) and the Quran. This ruling ensures that the bequest goes to extended family rather than immediate ascendants or descendants, who typically have fixed shares in inheritance.

Key Terms
اقارب (aqārib): Relatives; specifically dhi rahm muhrim excluding parents and children.
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥm muḥrim): Blood relative within prohibited degrees of marriage.

In Hanafi law, a bequest to 'relatives' (aqarib) applies only to collateral blood relatives (dhi rahm muhrim), excluding parents and children, and is distributed to the nearest first.

Bequest for Sons-in-Law (Akhṭān): Scope of 'Khatan'
Explains inclusion of all mahram in-laws in a bequest to akhtān

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the scope of a bequest to 'akhtān' and identify the evidence (dalil) that supports the broader interpretation.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'akhtān' includes all husbands of mahram women, not just the daughter's husband, based on hadith and qiyas.

The term 'khatan' (son-in-law) can be ambiguous. When a testator bequeaths to his 'akhtān', does it include only the husband of his daughter, or also husbands of other mahram women like sisters and aunts? The Hanafi school addresses this using a hadith of the Prophet ﷺ and analogical reasoning (qiyas). In this lesson, you will learn the default ruling and the evidence behind it, as well as a valid scholarly difference regarding local custom.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) made to 'akhtān' (sons-in-law). The ruling concerns who is included in that bequest. The Hanafi position is that all husbands of mahram women are included.
The term 'khatan' is defined as husband of a mahram relative.
2
Locate the primary evidence (dalil)
The hadith of Juwayriyya (رضي الله عنها) shows that the Prophet freed all her mahram relatives (amounting to one hundred people) because of his marriage to her. This indicates that in-laws are considered relatives in Sharia.
The hadith is from Sunan Abi Dawud and is ahad (zanni al-thubut).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal implication)
The Prophet's action demonstrates that all mahram relatives through marriage are considered 'sons-in-law' in a general sense. By qiyas, a bequest to 'akhtān' includes every husband of a woman who is mahram to the testator.
This analogy extends the ruling from freeing slaves to bequests.
4
Note the scholarly difference (ikhtilaf)
Some Hanafi scholars in the region of Farghana restrict 'khatan' to the husband of the daughter only, based on local custom ('urf).
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the madhhab.
5
Evaluate the tarjih (preferred position)
The broader interpretation is mufta bihi because the hadith and qiyas provide stronger evidence than local custom, unless the testator's intent is clearly limited by custom.
Sadr al-Hind's view (broader) is relied upon.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

[13178 (41) کسی نے وصیت کی دامادوں کے لئے تو ہر ذی رحم محرم عورت کا شوہر تن میں داخل ہے۔ ختن کا ترجمہ داماد ہے اس لئے تمام ذی رحم محرم عورت مثلا بیٹی کا شوہر ، بہن کا شوہر، پھوپھی کا شوہر اور خالہ کا شوہر یہ سب متن میں داخل ہوں گے۔ اور ہر ایک کو وصیت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ کونے کے محاورے میں ان تمام لوگوں کو فتن یعنی داماد کہتے ہیں (۲) اوپر حضرت جوریہ کی حدیث میں حضرت جویریہ کے تمام ذی رحم محرم شامل ہوئے۔ اس پر قیاس کر کے خفتن میں اپنی ذی رحم محرم کے تمام عورتوں کے شوہر داماد میں داخل ہوں گے۔ فانی لیکن صاحب ہدایہ کے شہر فرغانہ میں خفتن صرف بیٹی کے شوہر کو کہتے ہیں اس لئے صرف بیٹیوں کے شوہروں کو وصیت میں حصہ ملے گا۔ اختان : ختن کی جمع ہے عورت کی طرف سے رشتے جیسے سر، سالہ، داماد، یہاں بیٹی کا شوہر مراد ہے۔
Whoever bequeaths to his sons-in-law, then the son-in-law is the husband of every woman who is a mahram relative. In this hadith, all the mahram relatives of Juwayriyya were considered in-laws, who were a hundred people. So mahram relatives are included. Ashar: plural of suhr, meaning son-in-law or brother-in-law. But here, in contrast to fitan, it refers to the wife's family. [13178 (41) If someone bequeaths to sons-in-law, then the husband of every mahram woman is included in the text. The translation of khatan is son-in-law, so all husbands of mahram women—e.g., husband of daughter, sister, paternal aunt, maternal aunt—are included in the text. And each will get a share in the bequest. In the dialect of Kuna, all these are called fitan, i.e., son-in-law. (2) In the hadith of Juwayriyya above, all her mahram relatives were included. By analogy, in khatan, the husbands of all mahram women are included as son-in-law. However, in the city of Farghana, Sadr al-Hind says that khatan refers only to the husband of the daughter, so only husbands of daughters get a share. Akhtan: plural of khatan, relationships from the wife's side, like father-in-law, mother-in-law, son-in-law; here it means daughter's husband.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from a hadith. It addresses the scope of the term 'khatan' (sons-in-law) in a bequest. The matn states that whoever bequeaths to his akhtan, the bequest includes the husband of every woman who is a mahram relative. The sharh explains that the hadith of Juwayriyya supports this, as all her mahram relatives were freed because of the Prophet's marriage. The term 'ashar' (in-laws) is derived from this. The local dialect of Kuna uses 'fitan' to include all in-laws, while in Farghana, 'khatan' is limited to the daughter's husband. This linguistic difference affects who receives the bequest. The Hanafi position generally follows the broader interpretation, as the hadith and qiyas indicate inclusion of all mahram husbands. The key lesson is that the intent of the testator is interpreted according to common usage, but the default in Sharia is inclusion of all mahram relatives unless specified otherwise.

Key Terms
ختن (khatan): Son-in-law, specifically the husband of one's daughter or other mahram female relative.
أختان (akhtān): Plural of khatan; relatives by marriage from the wife's side.

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'akhtān' includes all husbands of mahram women, not just the daughter's husband, based on hadith and qiyas.

Defining 'Aqārib' in Hanafi Bequest Law
Defines scope of 'aqārib' in bequests with three rulings and evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of 'aqārib' in bequests, identify which relatives are excluded, and explain the Quranic evidence for excluding parents and children.

Core Idea
A bequest to 'aqārib' goes only to mahram blood relatives, not parents/children, and must be for at least two.

A bequest (waṣiyyah) can be made to anyone, but when a testator uses the term 'aqārib' (relatives), Hanafi fiqh defines it precisely. This lesson unpacks that definition, the three rulings derived from the matn, and the Quranic and analogical proofs. Understanding this ensures the testator's intention aligns with Sharia.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn's three rulings
The matn states: (1) bequest goes to nearest mahram blood relative, then next; (2) parents and children are excluded; (3) at least two recipients. Note each ruling separately.
These rulings are derived from the term 'aqārib' and principles of inheritance.
2
Analyze the Quranic evidence
Surah al-Baqarah 2:180 mentions 'walidayn' (parents) and 'aqrabīn' separately. This separation proves parents are not part of 'aqārib'. The same applies to children by qiyas.
The word 'aqrabīn' is a plural form; its scope is restricted by the context.
3
Apply the qiyas for children
Children are analogous to parents: both are direct, not indirect relatives. Therefore, they are also excluded from 'aqārib'.
The illa (effective cause) is being a direct descendant/ascendant.
4
Understand the 'at least two' rule
The plural 'aqārib' indicates at least two. In Hanafi inheritance law, plural forms can apply to two. Bequest (sister of inheritance) follows this.
Had it been one, the singular 'qarīb' would be used.
5
Apply the distribution priority
Among eligible relatives, the nearest in degree inherits first; if none, then the next. The Prophet's companion Ibn Tawus confirmed that bequests to distant relatives are invalid if nearer ones exist.
This ensures the wealth stays with the closest bloodline.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و من اوصى لاقاربه فالوصية للاقرب فالاقرب من كل ذى رحم محرم منه ولا يدخل فيهم والوالدان والولد وتكون للاثنين فصاعدا [ ۳۱۷۹ (۴۲) جس نے وصیت کی قربت داروں کے لئے تو وصیت اقرب فالا قرب کے لئے ہوگی ذی رحم محرم میں سے۔ اور ان میں والدین اور اولا د داخل نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور دو یا اس سے زیادہ کے لئے ہوگی۔
اس مسئلے میں اقارب کا مفہوم متعین کیا ہے۔ اور تین باتیں کہی ہیں۔ پہلی بات یہ ہے کہ اقارب کے لئے وصیت کی تو ذی رحم محرم رشتہ دار کے لئے وصیت ہوگی۔ دامادگی کے رشتے والے داخل نہیں ہوں گے۔ اور اس میں بھی جو قریب کے رشتہ دار ہوں گے ان کو ملے گا۔ وہ نہ ہوں تو ان کے بعد کے رشتہ داروں کو وصیت ملے گی۔ دوسری بات یہ کہی کہ اقارب میں والدین اور اولا د داخل نہیں ہیں۔ کیونکہ محاورے میں اقارب اس کو کہتے ہیں جو بالواسطہ رشتہ دار ہوں۔ اور والدین اور بچے بالواسطہ رشتہ دار نہیں ہیں بلکہ براہ راست رشته دار ہیں۔ اس لئے وہ اقارب کی وصیت میں داخل نہیں ہوں گے (۲) آیت میں بھی والدین کو الگ بیان کیا ہے اور اقربہ کو اس پر عطف کر کے الگ بیان کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدین اقربہ میں داخل نہیں۔ اس کی اہمیت اس سے بھی زیادہ ہے۔ اور اسی پر اولاد کو قیاس کیا جائے گا۔ حاشیہ : (الف) حضرت عائشہ فرماتی ہیں کہ جور یہ بنت حارث ثابت بن قیس کے حصے میں گئی حضور نے جویریہ سے شادی کی تو لوگوں نے اپنی قیدیوں کو چھوڑ دیا اور ان کو آزاد کر دیا۔ صحابہ کہنے لگے حضور کے سسرال کے لوگ ہیں۔ کسی عورت کو اپنی قوم کے لئے اتنی برکت والی نہیں دیکھی۔ اس کے سبب سے بنی مصطلق کے سو گھر والے آزاد ہوئے۔
آیت یہ ہے۔ کتب علیکم اذا حضر احدكم الموت ان ترك خيرا الوصية للوالدين والاقربين بالمعروف حقا على المتقين (الف) ( آیت ۱۸۰، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ یسئلونک ماذا ينفقون قل ما انفقتم من خير فللوالدين والاقربين والیتمی (ب) ( آیت ۲۱۵ سورة البقرة (۲) ان دونوں آیتوں میں والدین کو خرچ کرنے کے لئے الگ ذکر کیا اور اقر بین کو الگ ذکر کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدین اقر بین میں داخل نہیں ہیں۔
اور تیسری بات یہ کہی کہ اقارب جمع ہے اقرب کی اس لئے میراث کے قاعدے سے کم سے کم دو دو کے لئے وصیت ہوگی ایک کے لئے نہیں۔ قاعدہ تو یہی ہے کہ جمع کا صیغہ تین کے لئے آتا ہے لیکن میراث میں جمع کا صیغہ دو کے لئے آتا ہے۔ اور وصیت میراث کی بہن ہے۔ اس لئے کم از کم دو کو شامل ہوگی۔ اور جس طرح میراث میں اقرب کو دیا جاتا ہے وہ نہ ہو تب اس کے بعد والوں کو دیا جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح وصیت میں اقرب کو دی جائے گی۔ وہ نہ ہوں تب اس کے بعد والوں کو دی جائے گی۔ عن ابن طاؤس عن ابيه قال كان لا يرى الوصية الا لذوى الارحام اهل الفقر، فان اوصى بها لغيرهم نزعت منهم فردت اليهم (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶ امن قال برد علی ذی القرابة ، ج سادس ،ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۷۴ ۳۰۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دور والوں کے لئے وصیت کی ہو تب بھی اس کو ساقط کر کے قریب والوں کو دی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح قریب کے ہوتے ہوئے دور والوں کو نہیں دی جائے گی ۔ اشارہ اس آیت میں بھی ہے۔ یسئلونک ماذا ينفقون قل ما انفقتم من خير فللوالدين والاقربین والیتمی (آیت ۲۱۵ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں والاقربین اسم تفضیل کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہے جس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ زیادہ قریب والوں کو پہلے وصیت کا مال دے۔
Whoever bequeaths to his relatives, then the bequest is for the nearest then the next nearest of every mahram relative, and parents and children are not included, and it is for two or more. [3179 (42) Whoever bequeaths to close relatives, then the bequest will be for the nearest, then the next nearest, from among the mahram relatives. And parents and children are not included in them. And it will be for two or more.
In this issue, the meaning of 'aqārib' is defined. Three things are said: First, if bequest is for relatives, it will be for mahram blood relatives. In-laws are not included. And among them, the nearest will receive; if not, then the next. Second, parents and children are not included in relatives because in common parlance 'aqārib' refers to indirect relatives. Parents and children are direct relatives, so they are not included. This is supported by the Quran: 'Prescribed for you when death approaches any of you, if he leaves wealth, a bequest for parents and near relatives' (2:180) where parents are mentioned separately from near relatives. Third, 'aqārib' is plural of 'aqrab', so by the rule of inheritance, the bequest is for at least two, not one. In inheritance, plural is used for two. And bequest is the sister of inheritance. So it includes at least two. And as in inheritance, the nearest is given, then the next, so in bequest. Ibn Tawus from his father: he did not see bequest except for poor mahram relatives; if bequest is made for others, it is taken from them and returned to them. This effect shows that even if bequest is made for distant ones, it is cancelled and given to the near ones. Similarly, if near ones exist, distant ones do not receive. There is also indication in the verse: 'They ask you what to spend. Say: Whatever good you spend, then it is for parents, near relatives, and orphans' (2:215). The use of 'al-aqrabīn' (superlative form) indicates that the nearest should be given first.
Source pages p. 386

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Quran and a companion's statement. It specifies the meaning of 'aqārib' (relatives) in a bequest. The matn states that the bequest goes to the nearest mahram relative (by blood, excluding in-laws), and parents and children are not included because they are direct relatives. Also, the bequest must be for at least two persons, based on the principle that plural in inheritance applies to two. The sharh elaborates three points: (1) The recipients are mahram blood relatives only, not in-laws. (2) Parents and children are excluded, proven by the Quranic verses that list parents separately from 'aqrabīn'. (3) The bequest goes to at least two recipients, by analogy with inheritance where the plural 'aqārib' covers two. The effect of Ibn Tawus shows that if a bequest is made to distant relatives while near ones exist, it is invalid and given to the near ones. The lesson is that the testator's intention is interpreted according to Sharia definitions, not customary usage. The ruling ensures that the bequest reaches the deserving blood relatives.

Key Terms
أقارب (aqārib): Plural of 'aqrab'; blood relatives who are mahram, excluding parents, children, and in-laws.
ذو رحم محرم (dhū raḥim maḥram): A blood relative whom one cannot marry due to consanguinity (e.g., sister, aunt, niece).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the matn, who is NOT included in a bequest to 'aqārib'?
A) Paternal uncle
B) Maternal aunt
C) Daughter
D) Cousin

Key Takeaway
A bequest to 'aqārib' under Hanafi law is strictly for mahram blood relatives (excluding parents/children), distributed to the nearest first, and must involve at least two recipients.

Priority of Paternal Uncles Over Maternal Uncles in Bequest to Relatives
Ruling on priority of uncles in bequest to relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that in a bequest to 'relatives', paternal uncles take precedence over maternal uncles, based on the principle of nearness and the hadith on giving residue to the nearest male agnate.

Core Idea
Paternal uncles, as agnates, have priority over maternal uncles in bequests to relatives.

This lesson examines a specific case in wasiyyah: when a testator bequeaths to his 'aqārib (relatives) and has both paternal and maternal uncles, who gets the bequest? The Hanafi ruling, based on the principle of giving to the nearest relative (aqrab) and the hadith, gives it to the paternal uncles. We'll unpack the proof and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The testator bequeaths to 'relatives' and has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. The ruling: the bequest goes to the two paternal uncles only.
This is the default interpretation when the will does not specify which uncles.
2
Locate the dalil
The hadith from Ibn Abbas (Bukhari and Muslim): 'Give the fixed shares to those entitled, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative.'
The hadith establishes priority for the nearest male agnate.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Paternal uncles are 'asaba (agnates) and are closer in kinship than maternal uncles (who are dhawu arham). Thus, they are the 'nearest male relative' in this context.
The principle: inheritance proximity guides interpretation of general bequests to relatives.
4
Note the scope
This ruling applies when the testator does not specify which uncle; the default follows inheritance rules of proximity.
If no paternal uncles exist, maternal uncles may then be considered.
5
Evaluate the consequence
Maternal uncles are excluded entirely if paternal uncles exist. The bequest is given solely to the paternal uncles.
This is a strict application of the principle of asaba priority.

و اذا اوصى بذلك وله عمان و خالان فالوصية لعميه عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. صاعد : اس کا لفظی ترجمہ ہے چھڑتے ہوئے، یہاں مراد ہے اس سے زیادہ ، یعنی دو یا اس سے زیادہ تین ، چار۔ [۱۳۱۸۰ (۴۳) اگر وصیت کی یہی اور اس کے لئے دو بچے اور دو ماموں ہیں تو وصیت اس کے دو چچاؤں کے لئے ہوگی امام ابو صیفہ کے نزدیک۔
شر او پر قاعدہ گزرا کہ وصیت پہلے اقرب کو دی جائے گی وہ نہ ہو تب اس کے بعد والے کو دی جائے گی۔ اب کسی نے اقارب کے لئے وصیت کی اور اس کے لئے دو بچے ہیں اور دو ماموں ہیں تو وصیت چچاؤں کے لئے ہوگی ۔ اقرب کے قاعدے کے اعتبار سے چا اقرب ہیں اور عصبہ بھی ہیں۔ اور ماموں کا درجہ بعد کا ہے۔ اس لئے چچاؤں کو وصیت ملے گی (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله الله الحقوا الفرائض باهلها فما بقى فلا ولى رجل ذكر
And if he bequeaths that and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. Sa'id: its literal translation is 'ascending'; here it means 'more than', i.e., two or more, three, four. [13180 (43) If he bequeaths this and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest will be for his two paternal uncles according to Imam Abu Hanifa.
The rule has passed that the bequest is first given to the nearest; if not, then to the next. Now, someone bequeaths to relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest will be for the paternal uncles. By the rule of nearness, paternal uncles are nearer and they are also 'asaba (agnates). Maternal uncles are of a lower rank. So the paternal uncles get the bequest. (2) There is indication in the hadith: from Ibn Abbas that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Give the fixed shares to those entitled, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative.'
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from a hadith and qiyas. It applies the general principle of priority of the nearest relative to the case of uncles. The matn states that when the testator has both paternal uncles (amm) and maternal uncles (khal), the bequest goes to the paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa. The sharh explains that paternal uncles are both closer in kinship and are 'asaba (agnates) in inheritance, while maternal uncles are dhawu arham and fall behind. The hadith 'Give the fixed shares to those entitled, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' supports giving priority to the nearer agnate. This ruling ensures that the bequest follows the principles of inheritance in determining proximity. The testator's will is thus interpreted in line with Sharia priorities.

Key Terms
عم (ʿamm): Paternal uncle, brother of the father.
خال (khāl): Maternal uncle, brother of the mother.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Maternal uncles only
C) Paternal uncles only
D) It depends on their distance

Key Takeaway
In a bequest to relatives without specification, paternal uncles (as agnates) take precedence over maternal uncles.

Bequest to Relatives: Priority of the Nearest
Ruling with proof for preferring paternal uncles over maternal in bequest

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule of prioritizing the nearest relative in a bequest and identify the proofs from Quran and athar.

Core Idea
When bequeathing to relatives, the closest in lineage receive priority, just as in inheritance.

This passage addresses a critical question in the law of bequest (wasiyyah): if a person leaves a will for his relatives (aqarib), how should the bequest be distributed among them? The Hanafi school, following the Quranic term 'al-aqrabin' (the nearest), establishes that the bequest must go to the closest relatives first, in order of lineage priority. We will examine the Quranic proofs, the logic from inheritance, and the specific case of paternal versus maternal uncles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Ruling
State the Hanafi position: when a bequest is made to relatives (aqarib), it must be given to the nearest relative(s), then to the next nearest, etc. In the case of a man with paternal and maternal uncles, the bequest goes to the paternal uncles because they are closer in lineage and are asaba (residuary heirs).
The ruling is derived from the principle that bequest follows inheritance priority.
2
Locate the Dalil (Quran)
Identify the two Quranic verses cited: Surah Al-Baqarah 2:180 and 2:215. Note that both verses mention 'al-aqrabin' (near relatives) separately from parents, indicating that parents are not included in 'aqarib'. Also, the superlative form 'aqrab' implies closeness.
2:180 is the primary proof for the obligation of bequest to near relatives.
3
Analyze the Wajh al-Dalalah
Explain how the verses prove the priority of the nearest relative. The separate mention of parents shows they are excluded from 'aqarib'. The word 'al-aqrabin' (superlative) indicates that bequest should begin with the closest, then the next closest, in order. This is reinforced by the hadith 'Give the shares to their owners, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative.'
The Hanafi interpretation relies on the linguistic indication of the superlative.
4
Apply to the Given Case
Apply the rule to the scenario: a man has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles. Since paternal uncles are closer in lineage (they share the same paternal grandfather) and are asaba, they receive the bequest. Maternal uncles are of lower rank and receive nothing if paternal uncles exist.
This mirrors the inheritance priority: asaba precede dhawi al-arham.
5
Note the Cross-Madhhab Dispute
Recognize that Imam al-Shafi'i and others disagree: they hold that the bequest can be given to any relative, not necessarily the nearest. The Hanafi response relies on the Quranic indication and the practice of the Companions (e.g., Ibn Tawus).
The practical difference: if a person bequeaths to 'relatives' and has both close and distant kin, the Hanafi will give only to the closest, while the Shafi'i may distribute to all.

Source Text

كتاب الوصايا
رحم محرم منه ولا يدخل فيهم والوالدان والولد وتكون للاثنين فصاعدا [ ۱۳۱۸۰ (۴۳) و اذا اوصى بذلك وله عمان و خالان فالوصية لعميه عند ابي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى. آیت یہ ہے۔ کتب عليكم اذا حضر احدكم الموت ان ترك خيرا الوصية للوالدين والاقربين بالمعروف حقا على المتقين (الف) ( آیت ۱۸۰، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) دوسری آیت میں ہے۔ يسئلونك ماذا ينفقون قل ما انفقتم من خير فللوالدين والاقربين والیتمی (ب) ( آیت ۲۱۵ سورة البقرة (۲) ان دونوں آیتوں میں والدین کو خرچ کرنے کے لئے الگ ذکر کیا اور اقر بین کو الگ ذکر کیا جس سے معلوم ہوا کہ والدین اقر بین میں داخل نہیں ہیں۔
اور تیسری بات یہ کہی کہ اقارب جمع ہے اقرب کی اس لئے میراث کے قاعدے سے کم سے کم دو دو کے لئے وصیت ہوگی ایک کے لئے نہیں۔ قاعدہ تو یہی ہے کہ جمع کا صیغہ تین کے لئے آتا ہے لیکن میراث میں جمع کا صیغہ دو کے لئے آتا ہے۔ اور وصیت میراث کی بہن ہے۔ اس لئے کم از کم دو کو شامل ہوگی۔ اور جس طرح میراث میں اقرب کو دیا جاتا ہے وہ نہ ہو تب اس کے بعد والوں کو دیا جاتا ہے۔ اسی طرح وصیت میں اقرب کو دی جائے گی۔ وہ نہ ہوں تب اس کے بعد والوں کو دی جائے گی۔ عن ابن طاؤس عن ابيه قال كان لا يرى الوصية الا لذوى الارحام اهل الفقر، فان اوصى بها لغيرهم نزعت منهم فردت اليهم (ج) (مصنف ابن ابی شیبة ، ۶ امن قال برد علی ذی القرابة ، ج سادس ،ص ۲۱۵، نمبر ۷۴ ۳۰۷) اس اثر میں ہے کہ دور والوں کے لئے وصیت کی ہو تب بھی اس کو ساقط کر کے قریب والوں کو دی جائے گی۔ اسی طرح قریب کے ہوتے ہوئے دور والوں کو نہیں دی جائے گی ۔ اشارہ اس آیت میں بھی ہے۔ يسئلونك ماذا ينفقون
قل ما انفقتم من خير فللوالدين والاقربین والیتمی (آیت ۲۱۵ ، سورۃ البقرۃ ۲) اس آیت میں والاقربین اسم تفضیل کا صیغہ استعمال کیا ہے جس سے اشارہ ہوتا ہے کہ زیادہ قریب والوں کو پہلے وصیت کا مال دے۔
صاعد : اس کا لفظی ترجمہ ہے چھڑتے ہوئے، یہاں مراد ہے اس سے زیادہ ، یعنی دو یا اس سے زیادہ تین ، چار۔ [۱۳۱۸۰ (۴۳) اگر وصیت کی یہی اور اس کے لئے دو بچے اور دو ماموں ہیں تو وصیت اس کے دو چچاؤں کے لئے ہوگی امام ابو صیفہ کے
نزدیک۔
شر او پر قاعدہ گزرا کہ وصیت پہلے اقرب کو دی جائے گی وہ نہ ہو تب اس کے بعد والے کو دی جائے گی۔ اب کسی نے اقارب کے لئے وصیت کی اور اس کے لئے دو بچے ہیں اور دو ماموں ہیں تو وصیت چچاؤں کے لئے ہوگی ۔ اقرب کے قاعدے کے اعتبار سے چا اقرب ہیں اور عصبہ بھی ہیں۔ اور ماموں کا درجہ بعد کا ہے۔ اس لئے چچاؤں کو وصیت ملے گی (۲) حدیث میں اس کا اشارہ ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال قال رسول الله الله الله الحقوا الفرائض باهلها فما بقى فلا ولى رجل ذكر حاشیہ : (الف) تم میں سے کسی کو موت آئے تو تم پر فرض کیا گیا ہے کہ اگر مال چھوڑا ہو معروف کے ساتھ والدین اور رشتہ داروں کے لئے وصیت کرنی ہے۔ متقین پر یہ حق ہے (ب) آپ سے لوگ پوچھتے ہیں کہ کیا خرچ کریں؟ آپ کہہ دیجئے جو مال خرچ کرو وہ والدین، رشتہ دار اور قیموں کے لئے ہو (ج) حضرت طاؤس
وصیت مناسب نہیں سمجھتے ہیں مگر فقیر ذی رحم محرم کے لئے ۔ پس اگر اس کے علاوہ کے لئے وصیت کی تو اس سے نکال کر دی رحم محرم کی طرف واپس کر دی جائے۔
Book of Wills. (A relative who is) close relative (mahram) from him and they (parents and children) are not included, and it is for two or more. [13180(43)] And if he bequeaths that, and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him. This is the verse: 'Prescribed for you when death approaches any of you, if he leaves good, is the bequest to parents and near relatives in kindness – a duty upon the righteous.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:180). Another verse: 'They ask you what they should spend. Say, whatever you spend of good is for parents, relatives, and orphans.' (Surah Al-Baqarah 2:215). In these two verses, parents are mentioned separately, and relatives (aqrabin) are mentioned separately, indicating that parents are not included in relatives. And the third point said that 'aqarib' is plural of 'aqrab', therefore, according to the rule of inheritance, the bequest is for at least two, not for one. The rule is that the plural form is for three, but in inheritance the plural form is for two. And bequest is the sister of inheritance. Therefore, it will include at least two. And just as in inheritance it is given to the nearest, if there are none, then to the next, so in bequest it will be given to the nearest, if there are none, then to the next. From Ibn Tawus from his father that he did not consider bequest valid except for poor blood relatives; if he bequeaths to others, it is taken from them and given back to them (the relatives). (Mussanaf Ibn Abi Shayba, 6/...). This athar states that even if he bequeaths to distant ones, it is invalidated and given to the near ones. Similarly, when near ones exist, distant ones are not given. There is an indication in this verse also: 'They ask you what they should spend. Say, whatever you spend of good is for parents, relatives, and orphans.' In this verse, the word 'wal-aqrabin' is a superlative form, indicating that the nearer relatives should be given the bequest first. 'Sa'id': its literal translation is 'rising', here it means 'more than that', i.e., two or more, three, four. [13180(43)] If he bequeaths that, and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for his two paternal uncles according to Imam Abu Hanifa. The rule passed above is that bequest is given first to the nearest, if none then to the next. Now, if someone bequeaths to relatives and he has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, then the bequest is for the paternal uncles. According to the rule of nearness, paternal uncles are nearer, and they are also asaba (residuary heirs). And maternal uncles are of a lower rank. Therefore, the paternal uncles will get the bequest. (2) There is an indication in the hadith: from Ibn Abbas, the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) said: 'Give the shares to their owners, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative.' (Sahih Bukhari, Book of Inheritance). Footnotes: (a) 'When death approaches any of you, it is prescribed upon you that if he leaves wealth, to make a bequest to parents and relatives in kindness – a duty upon the righteous.' (b) 'They ask you what to spend. Say, whatever wealth you spend, it is for parents, relatives, and orphans.' (c) Hadrat Tawus did not consider bequest appropriate except for a poor mahram relative; if he bequeaths to other than that, it is taken from them and returned to the mahram relative.
Source pages p. 387

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof. It establishes the Hanafi position that when a person bequeaths to 'relatives' (aqarib), the bequest is given first to the closest relatives, then to the next closest, in order of inheritance priority. The author uses two Quranic verses (2:180 and 2:215) to show that parents are excluded from the category of 'aqarib' since they are mentioned separately. Then he argues that the plural 'aqarib' requires at least two recipients because in inheritance law, the plural form is interpreted for two (not three). The ruling is illustrated: if a man has two paternal uncles and two maternal uncles, the bequest goes to the paternal uncles because they are closer in lineage and are asaba (residuary heirs). The author cites an athar from Ibn Tawus supporting the principle that bequests to distant relatives are redirected to nearer relatives. The hadith from Ibn Abbas (صلى الله عليه وسلم) 'Give the shares to their owners, and whatever remains is for the nearest male relative' supports the concept of priority by closeness. Thus, Abu Hanifa's ruling is based on the principle of prioritizing the nearer relative in bequests, consistent with inheritance rules.

Key Terms
اقارب (aqarib): Plural of qarib, meaning relatives. In this context, it excludes parents and children, and the plural implies at least two recipients.
اقرب (aqrab): Superlative of qarib, meaning nearest. Used in this passage to prioritize the closest relative in receiving a bequest.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a person bequeaths to his relatives (aqarib) and he has both paternal uncles and maternal uncles, who receives the bequest?
A) The paternal uncles, because they are closer
B) The maternal uncles, because they are also relatives
C) It is divided equally among all
D) It goes to the poor among them

Key Takeaway
When a bequest is made to relatives (aqarib), the Hanafi school mandates giving it to the nearest relative in lineage, following inheritance priority, excluding parents and children.
