Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
6 min
One paternal uncle and two maternal uncles: half each
Ruling on distribution of bequest to relatives when one paternal and two maternal uncles exist.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the shares of a paternal uncle and maternal uncles in a bequest to relatives and apply the principle of closeness in distribution.

Core Idea
In bequests to relatives, the single nearest relative takes half; the next closest share the other half.

This lesson examines a specific ruling from the chapter on bequests (wasiyyah). When a testator leaves a bequest 'to my relatives' and only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles survive, the distribution is predetermined. Understanding this illustrates the principle of prioritizing closeness in bequest distribution, which differs from inheritance (faraid).

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
Determine the surviving relatives: one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles. Note that these are the only relatives entitled under the bequest.
The testator said 'to my relatives' which includes all blood relatives.
2
Apply the division rule
The paternal uncle, being the closest relative (nearest in kinship), receives half the bequest. The two maternal uncles, who are next in closeness, share the remaining half equally.
Closeness is determined by the degree of relation; paternal uncle is considered closer than maternal uncle in Hanafi fiqh.
3
Verify the reasoning
Why half and not equal division? The rule divides the bequest into two halves: one for the nearest relative (no matter how many in that category), and the other half for the next closest group. Here, the nearest group has one person, so he gets the entire first half. The next group has two, so they split the second half.
If there were multiple nearest relatives (e.g., two paternal uncles), they would share the first half.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۸۱ (۴۴) وان كان له عم وخالان فللعم النصف وللخالين النصف
[3181(44)] And if he has a (paternal) uncle and two maternal uncles, then the uncle gets half and the two maternal uncles get half.
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. It continues the previous discussion on bequest to relatives. If the testator has only one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, the bequest (which was for all relatives) is divided: the paternal uncle receives half, and the two maternal uncles share the other half. This is because the paternal uncle is closer (the nearest relative), so he gets the larger share? Actually, the ruling assigns half to the one uncle and half to the two maternal uncles. The reason is that the testator said 'to my relatives' (aqarib), which requires at least two recipients. The paternal uncle is one, so he fulfills one of the two shares. The remaining half goes to the next closest, who are the maternal uncles. Since they are two, they split that half. This follows the principle of prioritizing closeness in inheritance.

Key Terms
عم (amm): Paternal uncle (father's brother).
خال (khal): Maternal uncle (mother's brother).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In bequest to relatives, if there is one paternal uncle and two maternal uncles, what are their shares?
A) Paternal uncle gets 1/2, the two maternal uncles together get 1/2
B) Paternal uncle gets 1/3, maternal uncles get 2/3
C) All divide equally into thirds
D) Paternal uncle gets nothing because maternal uncles are more numerous

Key Takeaway
In bequests to relatives, the closest relative (e.g., paternal uncle) takes half, and the remaining half is shared by the next closest relatives (e.g., maternal uncles).

Wasiyyah — Bequest
beginner
6 min
Bequest of One-Third When Part of the Property Is Lost
Ruling on validity of bequest when property is partially lost

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a bequest of one-third of specific property is affected by partial loss of that property.

Core Idea
A bequest of a fraction of specific property applies to what remains after loss.

In the Hanafi school, when a testator bequeaths one-third of a specific asset (like dirhams or sheep) and two-thirds of that asset is lost, the bequest does not become void. Instead, the remaining one-third goes entirely to the legatee. This lesson clarifies the ruling and its rationale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is a bequest (wasiyyah) of a fraction (one-third) of specific property. Determine whether the bequest is valid after partial loss.
The ruling is that the bequest remains valid and the legatee takes the remaining property.
2
Understand the condition of the property
The property is specific (dirhams or sheep). Two-thirds are lost, leaving one-third. The bequest was of 'one-third' of that property.
The bequest is a fraction of the whole, not a fixed quantity.
3
Apply the principle of fraction bequests
In Hanafi fiqh, a bequest of a fraction (e.g., one-third) of an estate or specific property applies proportionally to what exists at the time of death.
Loss before death reduces the corpus, but the fraction remains attached to whatever remains.
4
Conclude the ruling
Therefore, the legatee is entitled to the entire remaining one-third (since it equals the bequeathed fraction of the original). The bequest is valid and executed.
This differs from a bequest of a specific item; if that item is lost, the bequest fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
[۳۱۸۳] (۴۶) و من اوطى لرجل بثلث دراهمه او بثلث غنمه فهلک ثلثا ذلك وبقى ثلثه وهو (الف) ( بخاری شریف، باب میراث ابن الابن اذالم یکن ابن بص ۹۹۷ نمبر ۶۷۳۵)
[3183](46) And whoever bequeaths to a man one-third of his dirhams or one-third of his sheep, then two-thirds of that is lost and one-third remains, and it (the remaining one-third) is (from the permissible third of the estate)?
Source pages p. 388

Commentary
This is a ruling statement. The passage deals with a specific scenario: a testator bequeaths one-third of his property (specifically dirhams or sheep) to someone. Later, two-thirds of that specific property is lost (destroyed). What remains is one-third of the original property. The ruling (based on the Urdu explanation) is that this remaining one-third goes entirely to the legatee, because the bequest was of one-third of the property, and the loss occurred before the testator's death? The text is somewhat fragmented, but the principle is that the bequest is of a fraction (one-third) of a specific asset; if the asset is partially lost, the bequest applies to what remains. The footnote references a hadith from Bukhari about inheritance, but it may be related to the general principle of shares.

Key Terms
ثلث (thuluth): One-third; the maximum portion that can be bequeathed to non-heirs in Islamic law.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to a bequest of one-third of a specific property if two-thirds of that property is lost?
A) The bequest is void because the property is lost
B) The legatee gets the entire remaining one-third as his share
C) The legatee gets only one-third of the remaining one-third
D) The bequest is recalculated based on the original estate

Key Takeaway
A bequest of a fraction of specific property remains valid even if part of that property is lost; the legatee receives that fraction of what remains.
